—?—
CHAPTER 1. INTRODUCTION
Welcome to the Undercity.
The Undercity is a sprawling metropolis built in the shadow of (and partially beneath) an interdimensional Tower. This city is sealed under a protective Dome and ringed by militarized walls, Riftwatch towers, and desperate faith. Monsters spill from dimensional tears called Rifts. Guilds compete for control. Gods bargain for attention. And adventurers are treated as both weapons and currency. 
This book is your complete campaign framework for running adventures in the Undercity. It blends urban intrigue, divine politics, Rift horror, and player-driven legacy-building in a way that’s meant to feel alive at the table.

 

—?—
WHAT THIS BOOK GIVES YOU
This sourcebook is structured so you can run the Undercity immediately, improvise quests on the fly, and escalate the stakes session by session. It gives you:
• Major Guilds
Five (sometimes six) power factions — Iron Fang Consortium, Argent Blades, Wardens of Ash, Serpent Choir, and Obsidian Lotus — each with perks, obligations, rivalries, quest hooks, and leaders who have opinions about your party. 
• The High Council
The political machine that governs the Undercity. Each of the Major guilds gets a seat. A neutral Arbiter — appointed ceremonially by the Tower Authority for a single term — presides and breaks ties. On paper, it’s order. In practice? It’s knives and prophecy. 
• Divine Struggle
The gods are not quiet background lore here — they are active stakeholders. They grant boons, meddle in mortal politics, and in some cases literally consume heroic essence to grow stronger. This includes the Culinary Council, a cabal of predatory deities who fatten heroes like cattle for harvest. 
• Quest Engines
Drop-in quest tables, Rift event generators, faction missions, timed crises, Council session drama, and escalating chaos you can trigger at any level. You can spin out patrol jobs, artifact recovery missions, political sabotage, or divine bargains in seconds. Quest Engines correspond to the tiered mission structure detailed in Chapter 5 (Quest Tables & Dynamic Events)
• Districts & Travel
Fully described districts like Markets Infinite, Sanctum Quarter, the Warrens, the Grand Forum, and the Outer Wall — all with NPCs, rumors, hazards, and encounter tables. Each district feels different, behaves differently during Rift surges, and gives you built-in story pressure. 
• Encounter & Creature Support
Street ambushes, Rift incursions, divine avatars, militant cultists, corrupted constructs, and Rift-twisted wildlife. Includes multi-phase boss structures, Rift corruption rules for PCs, and terrain effects like gravity inversion, planar bleed, and prophecy duels mid-combat. 
• NPC Compendium
A fast-reference section for guild leaders, Council personalities, cult Apostles, Tower Authority bureaucrats, and recurring faces in each district. Each profile includes approachability, voice, and how they try to use the party. 
• Glossary & Currencies
Campaign-specific systems (Kharma, Essence Coins, Legend Points, Divine Attention, Rank tiers, etc.) so players understand how fame, reputation, and god-interest actually work in play. 
 —?—
THE CORE THEMES OF THE UNDERCITY
This setting is built around four recurring themes. Lean into them hard:
Survival vs. Reputation
You don’t just live here. You are noticed.
Fame (Legend Points) and divine attention are tracked. Saving districts, thwarting cult rituals, or dominating in public combat raises your profile. That gets you paid. That also gets you hunted — by jealous rivals, corrupt guild captains, and hungry gods. 
Political Violence
The High Council is more dangerous than any dungeon. Every vote shapes trade, access to relics, patrol authority, Rift response strategy, and even who legally “owns” your kills. Guild missions often are political black ops. PCs can end up as fixers, saboteurs, kingmakers… or scapegoats. 
Divine Transactionalism
Worship isn’t free. The Serpent Choir will sell you survival in exchange for oaths you will regret. The Culinary Council will offer “immortality through glory,” which is code for “we’d like to eat you later.” The Culinary Council are predators in divine silk—some mortals claim their feasts are metaphor, but the gods know better.
Rift Ecology
Reality is fragile. Rifts rupture space in alleys, marketplaces, even the Council chamber. They spawn monsters, warp gravity, bleed timelines, or flood streets with ash rain. Entire neighborhoods can shift from “buy fruit and gossip” to “physics is screaming” in one round. 


—?—
PLAYER EXPECTATION PRIMER
Give this section directly to your players before Session 1.
• You Are Not Generic Adventurers
Adventurers are a recognized economic class here. You are graded, ranked, watched, taxed, tracked by guilds, and occasionally “managed” by divine agents. You are talent and product. 
• You Will Be Approached
Guild recruiters, Apostles, Council aides, cult fixers, Rift researchers — they will all offer you things. Protection. Access. Secrets. Weapons. Contracts. Miracles. They are never doing this for free. Most Apostle ‘offers’ come through front agents or rumors — few reveal their divine ties openly at low tiers.
• You Will Have to Choose
You can’t stay neutral forever. If you avoid picking a patron, someone will try to claim you anyway.
• Public Matters
Duels are watched. Rift clears are reported. Civilian saves are retold and embellished. Your party’s brand affects prices, access, and political leverage. This is tracked mechanically using Kharma, Legend Points, and Divine Attention. 
• Death Is Not the Worst Outcome
Being harvested by the Culinary Council is worse. Becoming the “property” of a god is worse. Becoming a living conduit for Rift energy is worse. Becoming the subject of Thesaurus’ final chapter might be better, but it will not be safe. 
—?—
RUNNING THE UNDERCITY (FOR DMs)
This setting is built to escalate.
At low levels, parties take local contracts: escort a Rift researcher, shut down a minor cult shrine in the Warrens, negotiate a safe trade lane through Markets Infinite, defend a small patrol post near the Outer Wall. 
By mid-tier play, the party is dealing with Council votes, prophecy theft, guild sabotage, assassination attempts during high-profile arena duels, and divine bargaining with consequences that last forever. They’ll be recognized in the street. People will take sides. Gods will take interest.
By high-tier play, entire districts can fall, merge with other planes, or become holy warzones. The party can decide:
Save the city.
Rule the city.
Sell the city.
Burn the city as an offering to something that shouldn’t exist.
 
—?—
CHAPTER 2. MAJOR GUILDS OF THE UNDERCITY

The Undercity runs on guild power. To live here without a banner is to be invisible; to carry one is to have purpose, protection, and enemies. Each guild commands a district, an economy, and a philosophy. They are the arteries of the city—and sometimes, its cancers.
Each entry below includes:
Theme & Alignment: Their creed and moral gravity.
Headquarters: Primary district of control.
Faction Perk (5e mechanics): Boon for members.
Leader NPC: Profile and approachability.
Adventure Hooks: Drop-in story seeds or side quests.
DM Note: Hidden agenda or divine tie-in.


 
—?—
THE IRON FANG CONSORTIUM
Theme: Mercenary-trader cartel; wealth built on monster parts, relics, and smuggling.
Alignment: Neutral Evil
Headquarters: Markets Infinite
Faction Perk: Advantage on checks to appraise or sell monster loot.
Leader NPC: Guildmaster Serrik Dhal — jovial yet ruthless, keeps a ledger for everything, even friendships.
Guild Culture
The Fang believes profit is proof of virtue. They sponsor Rift expeditions, buy trophies, and convert raw horror into merchandise. Their caravans move through unstable zones under banners of crimson fangs painted on steel.
Adventure Hooks
• A Rift-harvest convoy vanished in Neon Row—recover the cargo before Obsidian Lotus does.
• Fang smugglers found Riftstone richer than gold; the Council wants a tax, they want silence.
• Rival merchants claim Serrik Dhal is funding cult hunts only to corner relic sales.
DM Note
The Fang’s trade sometimes feeds Serpent Choir supply chains without realizing it; their ‘heroic remains’ often end up in Culinary Council alchemy labs.
—?—
THE ARGENT BLADES
Theme: Glory-driven adventurer guild; fame is currency, spectacle is survival.
Alignment: Chaotic Neutral
Headquarters: Guild Spires
Faction Perk: Once per long rest, gain +1 Inspiration beyond normal limits (max 2 at a time).
Leader NPC: Lady Cerys Valemont — charismatic duelist whose sword hums when crowds cheer.
Guild Culture
They believe the Tower’s trials should be celebrated, televised by magic, immortalized in song. Members wear polished silver armor and smile for the bards. Duels, tournaments, and Rift showcases feed the city’s hunger for heroes.
Adventure Hooks
• A Blades champion disappears before a grand duel—did the Wardens arrest him or did the Lotus buy him?
• A Rift beast crashes the arena mid-show; keeping the audience alive is half the challenge.
• Lady Cerys offers to sponsor the party—if they sign exclusive rights to their story.
DM Note
The Blades draw divine attention faster than any faction; their public heroics generate Legend Points that the Serpent Choir and Culinary Council harvest through contracts of fame. Every victory earns Legend Points—and Culinary Council notice. Their brightest members often “ascend” into myth… or the gods’ dinner plates.
—?—
THE WARDENS OF ASH
Theme: Militarized defenders of the city; discipline forged in Riftfire.
Alignment: Lawful Neutral
Headquarters: Outer Wall & Gates
Faction Perk: When standing adjacent to an ally wearing armor, gain +1 AC.
Leader NPC: Captain Havel Korin — gruff veteran who measures trust in scars.
Guild Culture
The Wardens see the Undercity as a fortress forever under siege. They maintain curfews, enforce law, and train civilians in evacuation drills. Their creed: “Hold the Line.”
Adventure Hooks
• A Rift breach at the Gate of Ash threatens containment; the Wardens call for reinforcements.
• A deserter flees into the Warrens with stolen Rifttech; capture before Lotus agents do.
• Rumors of corruption in Warden command—prove loyalty or expose treason.
DM Note
Many Wardens secretly worship Ashara, the war-god who fuels their discipline. During crises, her whispers echo in barracks halls. PCs aligned with peace gods will feel the tension immediately.
—?—
THE SERPENT CHOIR
Theme: Religious guild of divine contracts and forbidden blessings.
Alignment: Lawful Evil
Headquarters: Sanctum Quarter
Faction Perk: Advantage on Religion checks and divine negotiations.
Leader NPC: High Apostle Yzura — smooth, persuasive, her smile is scripture and threat both.
Guild Culture
The Choir preaches salvation through obedience. Their temples double as contract houses; every miracle comes with a clause. Members tithe Kharma, Essence Coins, or memories in exchange for divine favor. Publicly, they maintain order. Privately, they draft deals that can rewrite destinies.
Adventure Hooks
• A Choir broker vanishes with half a cathedral’s tithe—recover her before the faith fractures.
• Apostles offer to cleanse Rift corruption from a companion… at the cost of another’s memories.
• The Choir declares the PCs’ relic heretical and demands surrender; compliance might avert divine wrath.
DM Note
The Choir is the Culinary Council’s visible front. They enforce divine order as a form of husbandry—keeping the faithful fed, fat, and manageable.
—?—
THE OBSIDIAN LOTUS
Theme: Black-market syndicate controlling the Warrens; assassins, smugglers, information brokers.
Alignment: True Neutral
Headquarters: The Warrens
Faction Perk: Access to cursed artifacts and contraband (DMG magic items with drawbacks).
Leader NPC: The Widow — mask-veiled matriarch who speaks softly and never repeats herself.
Guild Culture
Where the Fang sells relics publicly, the Lotus deals in what should stay buried. They smuggle Rift residue, bottled souls, and god-tongue ink. Their couriers navigate collapsed tunnels the Wardens avoid. Many Lotus agents are former adventurers too stained to show their faces above ground.
Adventure Hooks
• A Lotus broker offers Rifttech armor in exchange for “a favor owed later.”
• Rumors speak of an auction for a living contract scroll—signed by a god.
• Someone poisons the district’s water supply; evidence points to a rival guild frame-job.
DM Note
The Lotus keeps balance in the underworld by controlling secrets. They worship Veha, the Silent Bloom—an exiled god who believes truth should die with its speaker. Her whispers can erase memories from an entire crowd. PCs may encounter her agents mid-cover-up.



—?—
THE GUILD OF ASHEN SCROLLS (optional Sixth Faction)
Theme: Scholars, archivists, and chroniclers sworn to Thesaurus, Keeper of the Endless Pages.
Alignment: Neutral Good (but fatalistic)
Headquarters: Grand Forum Library
Faction Perk: Once per session, the party may ask a lore question; the DM must answer honestly, though cryptically.
Leader NPC: Archivist Eir Velan — ex-Apostle turned historian, haunted by omniscient memories.
Guild Culture
They record every legend before it fades—and sometimes before it happens. To them, fate is a library constantly rearranging itself. Membership grants glimpses of possible endings, but each vision exacts a price: a page from one’s own story.
Adventure Hooks
• A prophecy in the Ashen Vaults mentions a player character by name. Can you burn the page before Thesaurus reads it?
• A stolen script from the Scrolls is being used as a divine exploit by the Culinary Council.
• The Archivist offers to trade the truth of a companion’s future for their voice.
DM Note
This faction ties to the meta-story of the campaign. Thesaurus himself tracks Legend Points earned by heroes and may rewrite history to achieve his “perfect ending.” Introduce their quests when the party starts to see themselves as mythic figures.
—?—
GUILD INTERACTIONS & POLITICS
All five (occasionally six) guilds hold seats on the High Council. Their alliances shift like Rift currents. Typical relations:
Guild	Ally	Rival	Secret Agenda
Iron Fang Consortium	Obsidian Lotus (trade routes)	Wardens of Ash	Monopolize relic market
Argent Blades	Serpent Choir (spectacle &faith)	Iron Fang	Create state-sanctioned heroes
Wardens of Ash	None (stoic neutral)	Lotus &Blades	Militarize Council authority
Serpent Choir	Argent Blades	Ashen Scrolls	Harvest Legend Points for Culinary Council
Obsidian Lotus	Iron Fang	Wardens	Control information flow and memory
Ashen Scrolls	None (outlier)	Serpent Choir	Preserve truth at all costs — even time itself
The High Council comprises five guild seats and one rotating Arbiter; when the Ashen Scrolls participate they do so as non-voting observers
—?—
CHAPTER 3. THE HIGH COUNCIL & POLITICS

Where gods play chess with mortals, the High Council pretends to keep score.
Every guild sends a delegate; together they dictate law, trade, and survival.
The Council is a monument to order balanced atop the abyss.
 
—?—
STRUCTURE OF THE HIGH COUNCIL
Seats: Six (five guilds + one rotating Arbiter); the Guild of Ashen Scrolls may attend as non-voting observers.
Headquarters: The Grand Forum, center of the Undercity
Meeting Schedule: Biweekly sessions, emergency convocations during Rift events
Voting Weight: One vote per guild; Arbiter breaks ties
The Arbiter
A neutral magistrate appointed ceremonially by the Tower Authority for a one-year term but sworn to impartial truth over law.
Their duty is to moderate, record, and prevent open warfare within the Forum.
Most Arbiters retire “quietly” after their tenure — or vanish into new names.
Current Arbiter: Magistrate Salien Vo
A former scribe of the Ashen Scrolls who now walks a moral tightrope.
Salien keeps records in three scripts: one for truth, one for law, one for survival.
—?—
COUNCIL DYNAMICS
Debate is theater.
Each session begins with incense and illusion wards — then devolves into shouting, divine omens, and the occasional thrown chair.
Iron Fang Consortium demands tax exemptions for relic trade.
Argent Blades push for more funding to turn heroism into state propaganda.
Wardens of Ash want martial law and stricter curfews.
Serpent Choir lobbies for faith-based jurisdiction in “spiritual crimes.”
Obsidian Lotus insists all memory-erasure contracts be legalized.
Ashen Scrolls (if present) petition for transparency, and are promptly ignored.
Every vote carries divine ripples. Such ripples raise or lower Divine Attention (see Chapter 4) as the gods react to political victories. When the Choir wins, the gods sing. When the Lotus wins, people forget.
DM Note: Treat Council sessions like combat encounters for dialogue. Track turns, alliances, and interruptions. Every PC intervention should shift one faction’s attitude.

 



—?—
POLITICAL DYNAMICS
Public Order vs. Divine Chaos
The Council’s goal is to appear in control of a city run by miracles and monsters.
Secretly, half its laws are rewritten nightly by divine influence or Lotus forgery, while FTA observers pretend oversight is maintained.
Political Tools (Mechanics):
Favors: PCs earn or spend favors as currency with delegates.
Council Tension (CT): Starts at 0; every scandal, Rift, or divine incident adds +1.
CT 5+: The Arbiter invokes emergency powers.
CT 8+: The Tower Authority intervenes directly (or through avatars).
Roleplaying Tip: Treat each Council member as both a bureaucrat and a priest; their morality bends to whichever side feeds their divine patrons.
—?—
THE ARBITER’S AUTHORITY
Arbiters can issue Forum Decrees, temporary laws that override guild control for 72 hours.
Abuse of this power draws divine scrutiny — or assassination attempts.
DM Hooks:
• A decree bans all Essence Coin trade for “investigation” — the Fang erupts.
• The Arbiter outlaws public worship, claiming divine interference threatens the Dome.
• PCs might be tasked to protect or replace the Arbiter mid-crisis.
—?—
THE TOWER AUTHORITY (FTA)
Type: External government body
Domain: Regulation of Tower access and Rift containment
Motto: “Order before Ascension.”
Though officially benevolent, the FTA acts more like a celestial audit firm than a protector.
They view adventurers as data points, faith as a resource, and death as a performance metric.
Key NPCs:
Director Myra Kess — smiling bureaucrat; wields paperwork like divine smite.
Inspector Hal Drayven — enforcer who considers mercy a breach of protocol.
Agent Liane Voss — secretly sponsored by Thesaurus to record the “final story.”
FTA Hooks:
• PCs are “invited” to submit Rift clear logs for inspection.
• An FTA envoy tries to arrest a god disguised as a Councilor.
• A bureaucratic error brands the party as unauthorized adventurers—making them outlaws overnight.
DM Note: The FTA can act as the campaign’s neutral villain: they believe good intentions justify control.
—?—
UNDERCITY POLITICS IN PLAY
You don’t have to run politics as long speeches. Think of it as stealth combat using words and reputation.
Skill Challenges & Social Combat Examples:
Scenario	Success Outcome	Failure Outcome
Argue for funding	PCs gain district access	Rival guild spreads slander
Expose divine interference	Council suspends Choir vote	Culinary Council marks PCs for consumption
Broker peace between guilds	Temporary truce	Assassination attempt mid-session
Deliver a prophetic text	Gain Legend Points	Rift opens in chamber mid-debate
—?—
THE SECRET COUNCIL (DM-ONLY)
Not every decision happens in daylight.
Beneath the Forum lies a circular chamber where divine echoes argue without mouths.
The true Council meets there: the gods behind each faction, negotiating fates.
DM Note: Each mortal seat mirrors a divine counterpart in the Secret Council; some gods hold multiple seats through different guilds.
PCs who uncover this secret will realize:
The High Council isn’t running the city. The city is running a simulation for the gods.
DM Hooks:
• Discover a Councilor’s body still speaking divine decrees post-mortem.
• Uncover minutes of the Secret Council written in prophecy ink.
• A Rift breach merges both Councils; mortals and gods must debate side by side—or die together.


—?—
Mechanics Note — Council Tension (CT), Kharma, and Legend Points interact directly with Divine Attention as detailed in the next chapter.

CHAPTER 4. DIVINE POWER & COSMIC STRUGGLE

In the Undercity, the divine are not distant—they’re competing for airtime. The gods walk through mortal politics like gamblers through a casino, staking faith and memory instead of coin. Their wars are subtle: fought through Apostles, contracts, miracles, and occasionally, dinner invitations.
—?—
THE DIVINE ORDER
The known pantheon consists of roughly thirty gods, though few have worshipers bold enough to name them aloud. Most fall under Three Pillars of Divinity:
Pillar	Domain	Example Gods	Role in the Undercity
The Pillar of Flesh	Life, Hunger, Transformation	The Culinary Council	Consume heroic essence to sustain existence
The Pillar of Mind	Knowledge, Fate, Memory	Thesaurus, Veha	Record, alter, or erase stories
The Pillar of Flame	Justice, War, Renewal	Ashara, Solmer	Fuel conflict to purge weakness
The gods within these pillars vie for mortal attention—the strongest form of divine sustenance since the Tower sealed heaven from the source.
DM Note: “Prayer economy” is a measurable force. Every notable act—combat victory, moral choice, or public miracle—feeds or starves a god. PCs who gain followers literally tilt the divine balance.
—?—
THE CULINARY COUNCIL
Continuity Note — The Culinary Council operate as the divine apex of consumption. Their mortal proxies include the Serpent Choir (public clergy) and Iron Fang Consortium (unknowing suppliers).
Motto: “To devour is divine.”
Domains: Hunger, Dominion, Preservation through Consumption
Nature: A cabal of deities that feed on mortal essence, primarily that of heroes.
The Culinary Council began as seven minor gods of harvest and feast. When the Rift tore open, they discovered that consuming souls infused with Legend Points amplified their divinity exponentially. Now they operate as predators in silk.
Council Goals:
Convert adventurers into “heroic stock.”
Dominate faith markets by rewarding spectacle.
Silence gods who oppose the practice.
Notable Members:
Gourmand Prime, the Bone King: Patron of feasts and famine; appears as a skeletal chef wreathed in divine smoke.
Mother Mire: Goddess of indulgence; whispers cravings that become addictions.
The Hollow Waiter: Serves divine banquets where guests realize too late they’re the entrée.
PC Interaction Hooks:
• PCs may earn invitations to divine banquets—quests in themselves.
• A godly “restaurant” in the Sanctum Quarter offers resurrection at the cost of a piece of the soul.
• A heroic deed may accidentally place a PC on the Council’s “menu.”
DM Note: When players gain too many Legend Points, introduce subtle omens—smells of spice during combat, phantom applause, or divine hunger pangs. These foreshadow attention from the Council. Their actions ripple through Council politics. When the Choir wins votes or the Fang profits, the Council’s Divine Attention rises one step.
—?—
THESAURUS, KEEPER OF THE ENDLESS PAGES
Domain: Knowledge, Fate, Story, Heroic Sagas
Alignment: Neutral Good (but deterministic)
Goal: To witness and record the ultimate heroic tale—even if it ends the world.
Thesaurus catalogues every legend ever lived. His realm is an infinite library where each book writes itself. Yet he is weary; he wishes for a story so perfect it can close the final volume.
Manifestation: Silver-robed scholar whose quill bleeds light. Sometimes speaks through dreams or written words that appear in midair.
Interaction Hooks:
• PCs find journals chronicling their future deeds.
• His Apostles request players to “improve” fate by repeating legendary patterns.
• He warns of the Culinary Council, but only in metaphor.His warnings often manifest through the Guild of Ashen Scrolls — the mortal archivists who echo his philosophy and serve as non-voting observers on the High Council.
Mechanics – Legend Points (LP):
LP track heroic impact.
Each 10 LP raises Divine Attention by +1 step.
At 5 steps, Thesaurus manifests guidance or prophecy.
At 7+, Culinary Council begins direct interference.
DM Note: Thesaurus is not an ally; he is an archivist. He may save the story, not the heroes.
—?—
THE REBELLION OF FLAME
God: Ashara, the Phoenix Marshal
Domain: War, Purity, Rebirth through Fire
Alignment: Lawful Neutral
Ashara opposes the Culinary Council not out of mercy but principle. She believes consumption corrupts the divine cycle. Her followers—the Wardens of Ash—wage literal and metaphysical wars to burn corruption away. The Wardens’ crusade often clashes with the Serpent Choir’s doctrine of divine consumption, framing Ashara’s faithful as the lawful opposition to the Culinary Council’s hunger.
PC Hooks:
• A Warden priest offers to “purify” a Rift-tainted PC with holy fire—lethal if resisted.
• Ashara demands a public trial by combat to cleanse a corrupt district.
• Her celestial emissary seeks mortal allies to raid the divine kitchens of the Council.
DM Note: Ashara’s blessings often manifest as destructive radiant flames—perfect for self-sacrifice arcs or catastrophic last stands.
—?—
VEHA, THE SILENT BLOOM
Domain: Secrets, Forgetting, Mercy in Oblivion
Alignment: True Neutral
Symbol: Black lotus petals swirling into mist.
Veha is the god of forgetting—patron of assassins, archivists, and anyone who believes ignorance is kindness. The Obsidian Lotus worship her as both muse and executioner. Veha’s neutrality reinforces the Lotus’ shift away from pure evil; their mercy lies in selective forgetting rather than malice.
Manifestation: Appears as shifting petals; her voice erases the memory of hearing it.
Hooks:
• PCs discover a ritual to erase an entire event from the city’s collective memory.
• Veha offers to remove a party member’s trauma—at the cost of erasing their relationships.
• A Lotus relic triggers temporary amnesia mid-mission.
DM Note: Veha’s interference allows time-bending or retroactive storytelling tools. Encourage creative “what if we forget this ever happened?” roleplay.



—?—
THE DIVINE ECONOMY
Every god competes for Kharma (faith energy). It can be traded, stolen, or gambled in divine markets.The following systems tie directly to Council mechanics. Kharma fuels miracles, Legend Points attract divine notice, and Divine Attention measures the gods’ response — all values that influence political and cosmic balance across the Undercity.
Currency	Description	Example Use
Kharma	Mortal faith crystallized through deeds	Buy miracles, fuel blessings
Essence Coins (EC)	Formed From Kharma for use in trade	Buy, sell, everyday items, pay tithe
Legend Points (LP)	Narrative significance	Attract divine notice, unlock story quests

		
Combine these currencies into dynamic tension. Too much Kharma draws divine eyes, too little and faith dies — erasing perks. When Divine Attention climbs, Council Tension (CT) rises as miracles bend law and order.
DM Note: Combine these currencies into dynamic tension. Too much Kharma makes gods notice. Too little, and faith dies—taking divine boons with it.
—?—
CHAPTER 5. QUEST TABLES & DYNAMIC EVENTS

The Undercity thrives on crisis. Quests directly affect Council Tension (CT) and Divine Attention (DA). Successes can stabilize the High Council; failures invite divine intervention or FTA oversight. Every day brings new contracts, divine interventions, or neighborhood implosions. This chapter provides tools for generating quests, events, and escalating consequences that make your campaign feel alive.










—?—
QUEST STRUCTURE OVERVIEW
Quests in the Undercity aren’t just errands—they’re investments. Each job affects guild standing, Divine Attention, and city stability. Each quest should specify which Guild or Divine Patron sponsors it. This maintains continuity with faction agendas in Chapter 2 and the divine rivalries of Chapter 4.
Use these tiers to balance risk and reward.
Tier	Typical Level	Scope	Example Objective	Kharma Reward	LP Gain
Local	1–2	Neighborhood	Escort, delivery, patrol	+10	+1
Standard	2–4	District	Guild dispute, Rift closure	+50	+2
Major	5–8	Multi-district	Political mission, divine interference	+100	+3
Epic	9+	Tower or divine realm	Council upheaval, godslaying	+500	+5
DM Note: Each completed quest should adjust at least two global metrics (Guild Favor, Divine Attention, Council Tension). Track them as parallel dials that slowly pressure the campaign world.
—?—
RANDOM QUEST TABLE (d10)
Roll or choose to fill your session in seconds.
d10	Hook	Tier	Complication
1	Escort a Rift researcher into unstable ruins	1	Rival guild interference
2	Track smugglers stealing Essence Coins	2	Discover they’re Choir operatives
3	Defend a public arena duel	2	Rift breach mid-fight
4	Investigate cult graffiti that predicts tomorrow’s deaths	2	It’s accurate—and self-referential
5	Deliver a divine message that erases itself when read	3	Target is already dead
6	Protect a bureaucrat revealing Council corruption	3	FTA agent replaces them mid-mission
7	Retrieve an artifact from the “silent” library	4	The library whispers your secrets
8	Escort a Choir relic through the Warrens	4	Relic absorbs emotions en route
9	Investigate Rift collapse near the Tower base	5	Collapse is artificial—FTA testing weaponry
10	Survive invitation to the Culinary Council’s Feast	6	PCs are the main course
—?—
DYNAMIC RIFT EVENTS (d10)
Rifts are semi-living tears in reality. Each one reshapes the environment and narrative tone. Roll for ambient madness:
d10	Event	Effect
1	Gravity folds inward	Movement halved; thrown items orbit midair
2	Air hums with reversed sound	Communication requires Insight saves
3	Time slows around monsters	Enemies act on initiative 10 every round
4	Blood crystallizes mid-spill	Slashing damage halves; piercing doubles
5	Echoes of future screams	PCs glimpse next turn’s damage rolls
6	Memories trade places	Swap mental stats between two PCs for 1d4 rounds
7	Divine glyphs rain from ceiling	Step on one—gain or lose random spell slot
8	Tower Authority drones arrive	Combat pauses for “inspection” (DC 20 Persuasion)
9	Rift turns transparent	Everyone sees themselves fighting in parallel
10	Rift manifests Culinary Council avatar	Reality check or immediate faith crisis
DM Note: Combine Rift events with guild missions for layered chaos—like an escort mission interrupted by a time inversion storm. When a dynamic event benefits or harms a guild, adjust Kharma and Legend Points for all affected PCs. Track any significant surge as +1 Divine Attention step, reflecting mythic escalation.

QUEST COMPLICATIONS (d6)
Rival guild already accepted the same contract.
Rift expands mid-mission; adds environmental hazard.
NPC client is an Apostle in disguise.
FTA classifies mission site as “restricted.”
A god rewrites quest parameters mid-run.
The job was staged to test the PCs’ loyalty.

LEGEND POINTS & QUEST CONSEQUENCES
?? Thesaurus’ Legend Meter (Quick Reference)

? Quick DM Usage Tips:
Track points per session; accumulate across arcs.
Use narrative events or major deeds to award points; small tasks may grant fractional points.
Check thresholds to trigger story escalations, subtle divine manipulations, or foreshadowing events.
Keep invisible to players — they should experience events organically.
You can annotate side notes per threshold: e.g., which NPCs or guild plots should become active.
 
?? Culinary Council Interaction Chart

? DM Tips:
Layer Threats Gradually: Begin with observation, then escalate through temptation, traps, and finally full-scale divine schemes.
Combine With Thesaurus’ Guidance: Council threats should often intersect with Thesaurus’ nudges, creating moral tension without breaking immersion.
Player Choice Matters: They can avoid, fight, or be manipulated into these situations. Consequences should ripple through guild politics, divine attention, and ongoing sagas.
Use Across Worlds & Guilds: The Council may employ agents or events from any world connected to the Tower, keeping the threat omnipresent.
??? Undercity Campaign Master Reference (DM Notes)

1?? Major Guilds
Additional Guilds for Integration:
Adventurers Guild: Quest hubs, Rift assignments
Arcanist Guild: Magical research, rare crafting
Thieves Guild: Underground info, smuggling, covert contracts

2?? Console / Arbiter Overview
Seats: Each major guild, Thesaurus, and select divine proxies hold seats.
Motivations:
Guilds: Power, wealth, fame, survival
Thesaurus: Guides heroes for legendary story potential
Culinary Council: Harvest heroic deeds for divine energy
Gods: Raise heroes to increase personal power, vying for influence after top Christian pantheon head disappearance

3?? Thesaurus, Keeper of the Endless Pages
Domain: Knowledge, Fate, Stories, Heroic Sagas
Alignment: Neutral Good (opposes Culinary Council)
Secret Goal: Be ended in the greatest heroic story ever told
Library Layout:
General Section: Public, common/uncommon books
Special Section: Invitation-only, ongoing sagas, divine-level events
Abilities / Mechanics:
Grants divine knowledge, hints, prophecy fragments
Warns of Culinary Council or divine interference
Can subtly alter library reality
Tracks heroes and divine attention points
Player Interaction Hooks:
Invitations to special section
Story guidance & epic quest hints
Safe haven, neutral ground
Moral dilemmas & heroic preservation
Long-term plot threads (e.g., missing pantheon head)

4?? Legend Meter (Tracking PCs’ Contribution to Thesaurus’ Saga)
Legend Points Awarded for:
Rift clears, heroic deeds, moral sacrifices, guild & divine interactions

5?? Legend Event Tracker

6?? Culinary Council Interaction

? DM Usage Notes
Keep Legend Points invisible to players; treat as narrative fuel.
Combine guild, divine, and Culinary Council events to escalate tension naturally.
Thesaurus subtly nudges story arcs while opposing Culinary Council practices.
Player agency matters: Choices influence guild politics, divine attention, and the legendary outcome.
Use LP thresholds to trigger events, rivalries, and moral dilemmas organically.
?? Undercity Random Quest Table (1–10)

? DM Tips
Scale Rewards: Use Kharma and Essence Coins according to risk and LP tier.
Add Complications: Even low-level missions can have unexpected twists — rival guilds, minor divine interventions, or hidden Culinary Council observation.
Randomize on the Fly: Roll d10 to generate spontaneous missions during downtime or story progression.
Mix Lore Hooks: Each quest can include undercity landmarks, ongoing sagas in Thesaurus’ library, or hints of higher-tier plots (Culinary Council / divine manipulations).

 
?? Undercity Quest Hooks Sheet

Tier 1 – Local Trouble (Roll 1)
A tavern brawl escalates; the PCs are blamed for stolen goods.
A guild courier disappears with minor loot; someone wants it recovered quietly.
Neighborhood kids are lured into a minor Rift; prevent injuries and damage.
Petty thieves are disrupting small market stalls; guild wants them caught discreetly.

Tier 2 – Patrol Duty (Roll 2)
Strange monster sightings near a residential district; investigate before panic spreads.
A small Rift emits unusual magical readings; report findings before it grows.
Missing livestock or magical beasts; clues point toward rift-adjacent tunnels.
Patrol team encounters suspicious guild members acting outside orders.

Tier 3 – Escort (Roll 3)
Protect a scholar carrying forbidden magical research to the Arcanist Guild.
Escort a merchant with rare artifacts through dangerous streets.
Transport a minor divine relic under threat from a local cult faction.
Guard a festival caravan while preventing theft by rival guild spies.

Tier 4 – Investigation (Roll 4)
Track the source of sabotage in the Iron Fang trade route.
Investigate rumors of cursed books circulating from Thesaurus’ library.
Follow a trail of clues linking petty thefts to an unknown undercity faction.
Discover who is secretly recruiting young adventurers for the Culinary Council.

Tier 5 – Rift Clearance (Roll 5)
A mid-sized Rift is growing; failure could flood a district with monsters.
Monsters emerge with new abilities, hinting at a larger threat.
Guild competition pushes PCs to close Rift first to claim bounty.
The Rift emits strange magical readings; closing it could reveal hidden treasures.

Tier 6 – Dungeon Delve (Roll 6)
Abandoned lower floor revealed beneath Undercity streets; monsters now occupy it.
Recover a missing Arcanist Guild artifact rumored to be in a sealed vault.
Rescue a group of adventurers trapped in a collapsed tunnel near a Rift.
Investigate an illicit Obsidian Lotus smuggling hub hidden in an old ruin.

Tier 7 – Inter-Guild Conflict (Roll 7)
Rival guild attempts to sabotage Argent Blades’ arena events; PCs intervene.
Smuggling dispute between Obsidian Lotus and Iron Fang spills into public streets.
Wardens of Ash suspect the Serpent Choir of unlawful rites; PCs mediate or spy.
Thieves Guild blackmails a minor guild leader; PCs decide who to support.

Tier 8 – High-Stakes Contract (Roll 8)
Recover a powerful relic from a Rift-infested zone before another guild.
Assassinate or sabotage a rival guild operative without leaving trace.
Retrieve a divine artifact for the Serpent Choir under strict time pressure.
Thesaurus requests PCs to secure story-critical NPCs or events.

Tier 9 – Rift Catastrophe (Roll 9)
Large Rift erupts, threatening multiple districts; civilians trapped.
Emerging monsters possess intelligence; require tactical planning to seal Rift.
Rival guild exploits chaos; PCs must manage both combat and politics.
Culinary Council observes heroic deeds; success may place PCs on harvesting list.

Tier 10 – Floor-Level Invasion (Roll 10)
Massive monster swarm breaches multiple floors; entire Undercity section in danger.
High-tier divine agents interfere, either helping or complicating matters.
Legendary guild operatives challenge PCs for control of the battlefield.
Thesaurus subtly directs PCs to save pivotal heroes, influencing saga outcome.

? DM Tips:
Hooks are flexible; combine them with Legend Points escalation and guild involvement.
Even low-tier missions can have ripple effects that raise LP unexpectedly.
Use Culinary Council or Thesaurus nudges to create moral tension or plot twists.
 
?? Dynamic Rift Events – Undercity
1?? Rift Anatomy
Size / Tier: Minor ? Medium ? Large ? Floor-Level Invasion.
Spawn Window: 3 days before spillover into districts.
Creature Type: Determined by Rift origin; normal weapons ineffective.
Magic Requirement: Only magical/system-created weapons can harm creatures.
Environmental Effect: Rifts distort terrain, lighting, gravity, or ambient magic.

2?? Event Triggers
Roll a d10 or select based on LP / Quest Tier:

3?? Dynamic Event Mechanics
Scale: Adjust CR or number of monsters based on LP or party level.
Time Pressure: Rifts naturally escalate every X turns; PCs must act quickly.
Loot / EC / Kharma: Reward for closing Rift includes randomized EC, Kharma, and chance for rare magical crafting materials.
Complications: Combine multiple event triggers for higher-tier Rifts (e.g., 6 + 3 = Hostages + Mutation).

4?? Quick Rift Event Table (d20 for granularity)

5?? DM Tips
Combine Quick Rift Events + Random Quest Table for instant mission generation.
Use LP as scaling factor: higher LP ? more complex / dangerous events.
Track Culinary Council / Divine Observation: each heroic action near a Rift can increase attention.
Make environmental hazards interactive: PCs can manipulate floors, walls, or magical devices to affect outcomes.
Encourage creative solutions: magic-only combat, environmental tricks, teamwork.
 Example Rifts. 
Scenario 1: The Shopfront Rift
Tier: 1–2 | Quest Type: Rift Clearance / Local Trouble
Setup:
A minor Rift opens in a busy street-level marketplace of the Undercity. Strange, weak creatures begin spilling out. Local merchants panic, and one Arcanist Guild shop is at risk of total destruction.
Objectives:
Seal the Rift before it grows.
Protect civilians and the merchant’s shop.
Optional: recover magical residue for the Arcanist Guild.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
d6 minor monsters emerge (e.g., small slimes, imps, or shadow critters).
Rift causes random sparks that occasionally stun or damage nearby PCs (Dex save DC 12).
Rival Thieves Guild shows up to steal loot while chaos erupts.
Rewards:
5–10 Kharma.
10–15 EC.
Minor magical trinket from Arcanist Guild shop.

Scenario 2: Sewer Skirmish
Tier: 2 | Quest Type: Patrol / Investigation
Setup:
A small Rift has appeared in the old sewage tunnels under the Warrens. Monsters are starting to infect the tunnel ecosystem. The Wardens of Ash request PCs to investigate.
Objectives:
Navigate tunnels safely and locate Rift source.
Eliminate minor monster threats (giant rats infused with Rift energy, small oozes).
Map tunnel hazards for future Warden patrols.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Environmental hazard: collapsing ceiling, slick floors (Dex save DC 11 to avoid falling prone).
Rift leaks minor magic pulses; low-level spells sometimes misfire (Magic Surge).
Obsidian Lotus gang scouts appear, curious about Rift loot.
Rewards:
7–12 Kharma.
15–20 EC.
Recognition by Wardens; possible minor favor for later high-stakes quests.

Scenario 3: Library Disturbance
Tier: 1–2 | Quest Type: Investigation / Escort
Setup:
A Rift has appeared in the general access section of Thesaurus’ library. Low-level magical anomalies are causing books to animate and attack visitors.
Objectives:
Escort librarians and scholars to safety.
Close Rift and calm animated books.
Optional: recover rare story scrolls for Thesaurus.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Animated books (AC 12, HP 8 each, low-damage melee attacks).
Rift emits strange temporal pulses; characters may act twice or miss a turn randomly (Temporal Glitch).
Culinary Council observer discreetly watches heroic actions.
Rewards:
5–10 Kharma.
10–15 EC.
Special “Story Insight” bonus: PCs can gain temporary Inspiration or advantage on lore checks next session.
Scenario 1: Abandoned Workshop (Level 1)
Floor: 2nd sublevel beneath Undercity
Quest Type: Exploration / Investigation
Setup:
The PCs are asked by the Arcanist Guild to investigate an abandoned workshop that has been mysteriously sealed for decades. Rumors say a Rift briefly appeared here, leaving behind unstable magical residues.
Objectives:
Explore the workshop safely.
Identify lingering magical anomalies.
Recover usable magical components for Arcanist Guild.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Minor animated constructs (AC 13, HP 10) patrol the floor.
Magic pulses randomly trigger minor traps or alarms.
Floor tiles are unstable; small Dex checks (DC 12) to avoid falls.
Rewards:
5–8 Kharma.
10 EC.
Low-tier magical crafting material (e.g., component for a +1 wand or enchanted coin).

Scenario 2: Flooded Passage (Level 2)
Floor: 3rd sublevel — partially submerged tunnels
Quest Type: Rift Clearance / Environmental Hazard
Setup:
A small Rift has opened in a flooded floor beneath the Undercity. The Wardens of Ash request a clearance team. The water makes movement difficult and creates hazards.
Objectives:
Seal the Rift.
Rescue trapped NPC workers or minor adventurers.
Avoid environmental hazards like strong currents or sudden collapses.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Water-borne Rift creatures (CR 1/2–1) attack on sight.
Flooding can trap PCs; Strength or Athletics checks (DC 12–13) required to avoid being swept away.
Rival guild scavengers may attempt to claim loot mid-mission.
Rewards:
8–12 Kharma.
15 EC.
Minor magical trinket or consumable (healing potion or elemental vial).

Scenario 3: Library Spiral (Level 3)
Floor: 5th sublevel — Thesaurus’ restricted floors (low-tier access)
Quest Type: Escort / Exploration / Light Combat
Setup:
Thesaurus sends the PCs to retrieve a series of story scrolls from the restricted spiral floors. The area is protected by animated storybooks, minor constructs, and environmental traps to prevent casual access.
Objectives:
Navigate maze-like floor safely.
Avoid or defeat low-level guardians.
Recover designated scrolls and return to the general library.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Animated books (AC 12, HP 12, low-damage attacks) roam hallways.
Floors shift periodically due to Rift instability (Dex check DC 13 to avoid falling or being separated).
Minor Temporal Glitches may cause PCs to repeat or skip a turn.
Rewards:
10–15 Kharma.
20 EC.
“Story Insight”: temporary advantage on Investigation, Arcana, or History checks for next session.
Optional minor boons from Thesaurus (e.g., hint about ongoing saga or safe shortcut).
Tower Floor Ascention: 
Scenario 1: The Mirror Plains (Level 1)
Floor: 1st above Undercity — warped reflection of Undercity streets
Quest Type: Exploration / Investigation
Setup:
The PCs are transported to a mirrored version of the Undercity. Everything is subtly off: reflections move independently, street vendors sell impossible items, and monsters appear as warped reflections of real citizens.
Objectives:
Investigate anomalies in this mirrored world.
Rescue captured NPCs trapped in reflection prisons.
Close a minor Rift connecting the Mirror Plains to the Undercity.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Reflected monsters mimic PCs’ abilities (low-level clones, AC 12–13, HP 8–10).
Environmental hazards: streets twist and rotate, forcing DC 12 Acrobatics/Perception checks.
Rival adventurers (or minor god agents) are hunting the Rift.
Rewards:
5–8 Kharma.
10–15 EC.
Minor magical trinket that reacts to reflections.

Scenario 2: The Past Rewritten (Level 2)
Floor: 2nd above Undercity — fragment of a historical world
Quest Type: Exploration / Story Alteration
Setup:
The floor recreates a past event from one of the Tower’s attached worlds: a siege or festival gone wrong. The PCs discover a “down-on-his-luck” hero trapped by the timeline who failed to make the right choices. They can intervene and alter history, saving him from death or disgrace.
Objectives:
Prevent the Rift from fully rewriting the past.
Rescue or guide the trapped hero to success.
Collect magical story fragments for Thesaurus.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Rift anomalies: minor monsters from “future” timelines attack (AC 12, HP 10–12).
Puzzle: manipulate events to ensure history stabilizes while allowing the hero’s survival.
Environmental hazards: collapsing buildings, magical feedback from Rift energy (Dex/Arcana DC 12–13).
Consequences / Continuity:
The rescued hero survives and appears in the next floor to aid PCs in the Tower Defense scenario.
Player choices here influence narrative: hero may inspire NPC defenders or provide tactical insight.
Rewards:
8–12 Kharma.
15–20 EC.
Temporal Insight: advantage on Investigation, Arcana, or History checks next session.

Scenario 3: Tower Defense – The Shattered Gate (Level 3)
Floor: 3rd above Undercity — fortress floor
Quest Type: Tower Defense / Combat / Guild Coordination
Setup:
A large Rift erupts, threatening the defensive gates of the Tower’s upper floors. PCs must organize defenses, coordinate with low-level Warden squads, and fight monsters until reinforcements arrive. The hero saved on the previous floor joins the defense, providing buffs, extra attacks, or tactical advice.
Objectives:
Hold key choke points against waves of Rift creatures.
Direct NPC defenders and set up barricades or magical wards.
Close Rift at the gate before it collapses.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Rift waves spawn every 3 rounds (CR 1–2 creatures).
Environmental hazards: partial floor collapse, magical surges (Dex/Strength checks DC 12).
Rival guild spies may try to sabotage defenses.
Rewards:
12–18 Kharma.
20–25 EC.
Minor magical items (enhanced shield, +1 weapon, consumables).
Guild reputation boost; opens access to higher-tier missions.
Player choices in the Past Rewritten floor can influence hero’s performance and NPC morale.

? DM Tips for Linked Floors:
Track player decisions in the past floor: who they save, which events they change.
Allow NPC hero to scale slightly with player level for the Tower Defense.
Introduce dynamic Rift events mid-defense for added tension.
Highlight story consequences: saving someone may change guild interactions or divine observation.

Tower Floor 4: The Hall of Fools – Comedic / Tragic Court
Floor Theme
The floor simulates a living court, combining absurd politics, heroic satire, and tragicomic nobles.
Court is run by various minor gods or archetypal “nobles” who observe PC choices for divine Kharma.
Most problems are social puzzles, diplomacy, or chaos avoidance, not combat.
Trigger combat if PCs insult the Baron, ignore court etiquette, or meddle too heavily in divine theater.

Random Roles & Equipment

Roles Assignment
Randomly roll or assign via table: 1–6 above.
Equipment comes with minor magical or narrative effects, often useful for solving court problems or RP challenges.
Roles don’t carry over from Floor 3, emphasizing the absurdity of the court.

Scenario Mechanics
Social Challenges: etiquette checks, persuasion contests, rumor management, bribery, and divine favor rolls.
Kharma Gain / Loss: heavily influenced by clever or funny roleplaying.
Combat Trigger (Baron):
If PCs insult the Baron, sabotage divine rituals, or provoke nobles: trigger Baron-level fight (CR 4–5, single powerful enemy).
Combat is rare, meant as punitive / climactic event.

Baron NPC (Optional Boss)
Baron Aristrok: pedantic, narcissistic minor god in noble guise
Stat Block: Mage (MM p.347) with buffs for courtly “envy / prestige”
Special Abilities:
Scornful Command: force one PC to waste turn bowing or apologizing
Wealth Drain: temporarily removes Kharma from careless PCs
Comedic Potential: exaggerated gestures, slipping on rugs, angry poetry recitations

DM Tips
Encourage comedic mishaps, absurd political negotiations, and tragic RP elements.
Let equipment have narrative effects, e.g., joke wand causes NPCs to burst into laughter, feather quill accidentally sets papers on fire.
Make combat the least desirable outcome; reward clever social maneuvering.
Minor Kharma bonuses for clever resolutions, improvisation, or amusing failures.
Court Hooks for Social / Diplomatic Challenges
1. The Missing Crown
Hook: The Baron’s ceremonial crown has gone missing right before a divine inspection.
Objective: Investigate, interrogate nobles or servants, and recover it without embarrassing the Baron.
Chaos Potential: Accusing the wrong NPC triggers scandal; combat if Baron deems you “criminals.”

2. Poisoned Dessert
Hook: A tray of magically infused pastries meant for a minor god causes unpredictable effects.
Objective: Identify the culprit or neutralize effects before the god consumes it.
Chaos Potential: PCs fail checks ? minor god temporarily enraged, NPCs start panicking.

3. Rumor Mill
Hook: False rumors are spreading in the court, threatening to topple a minister’s standing.
Objective: Use persuasion, deception, or social insight to reveal the truth or redirect blame.
Chaos Potential: Mishandling rumors may spark duels or baronial wrath.

4. Duel of Etiquette
Hook: Two nobles challenge each other over a slight insult; Baron demands a “trial by manners.”
Objective: Advise, mediate, or participate to prevent catastrophic embarrassment.
Chaos Potential: Misstep ? a slapstick duel escalates into full combat; PCs may gain or lose Kharma.

5. Misfiled Decrees
Hook: Ancient scrolls with contradictory laws accidentally sent to the wrong offices.
Objective: Find and correct misfiled decrees without offending the gods.
Chaos Potential: PCs accidentally enforce the wrong law ? court riot or magical anomaly.

6. Divine Complaints
Hook: Minor gods complain to the court about heroes’ behavior in lower floors.
Objective: Smooth over grievances with diplomacy or creative offerings (e.g., humorous apology, symbolic gift).
Chaos Potential: Failure ? god sends a small Rift, or Baron summons magical enforcers.

7. Errant Bard
Hook: A bard performs a satirical song mocking the Baron and court traditions.
Objective: Calm tensions, redirect performance, or secretly enhance it to please the Baron.
Chaos Potential: PCs intervene poorly ? bard insults Baron, triggering combat or public disgrace.

8. Magical Malfunction
Hook: Enchanted décor (floating candles, self-replenishing wine) malfunctions mid-ceremony.
Objective: Fix it using clever items, spells, or improvisation without causing panic.
Chaos Potential: Failing a check may cause small explosions, injured NPCs, or Baron outrage.

9. Guest of Honor
Hook: A visiting hero or minor god refuses to sit according to protocol.
Objective: Mediate seating, flattery, or negotiation to avoid insulting anyone.
Chaos Potential: Mismanagement ? duel, magical attack, or NPC mutiny.

10. Secret Alliance
Hook: Two court factions are plotting behind the Baron’s back.
Objective: Discover their plan, negotiate, or manipulate for maximum Kharma / minimal damage.
Chaos Potential: Mistakenly supporting a faction ? Baron declares betrayal; PCs must improvise escape or appeasement.

?? DM Tips:
Each hook can be resolved through clever roleplay, skill checks (Persuasion, Insight, Deception, Performance), or minor magical use.
Roll for chaos escalation if PCs fail key checks.
Small Kharma rewards for subtle, creative, or funny solutions—punitive consequences for blunders.
Further City Information 
 
?? Markets Infinite – Key Locations
Districts & Streets:
Neon Row – Bright holograms, alien tech shops, and cyberpunk-style gadget stalls. Locals claim the lights themselves sometimes “hint” at hidden sales or secret vendors.
Cobbleway Market – Medieval-style streets with blacksmiths, forges, and enchanted weapon shops. Street performers demonstrate minor magical feats for coins.
Floating Bazaar – Airships and levitating platforms host interdimensional merchants selling rare ingredients and exotic pets.
The Crimson Alley – Hidden among Neon Row; black market with rift-forged weapons, illegal artifacts, and cursed scrolls. Guards are rumor-sensitive—if you hear about it, you already shouldn’t be there.
Taste of Worlds – Multicultural food court. You can sample alien delicacies alongside traditional Earth meals; some vendors claim to cook with “essence from Rifts” for enhanced effects.
Major Stores & Stalls:
Veyra’s Vault – System-made weapons & armor. Prices skyrocket for SS-Rank adventurers. Rumor: Some weapons “choose” their wielders.
Elune’s Apothecary – Potions, cures, magical supplements, and rare rift reagents. Occasionally blessed by gods.
Kalyx Tech & Trinkets – Alien cybernetics, AI familiars, dimensional gadgets. Neon-blue signage flickers in unknown scripts.
The Wishing Stall – A tent where merchants sell “prayers” as scrolls or charms. Some are genuine blessings; others are cursed trinkets.
Patchwork Oddities – Artifacts salvaged from failed rifts, often dangerous but high-risk/high-reward.
Rumors to Seed Players:
A portal to a hidden floor opens randomly somewhere in the Floating Bazaar—but only at midnight under the artificial moon.
Crimson Alley has a dealer who “trades sins for power” – you leave stronger but with a secret debt to a god.
Some shops are sentient; if you speak to the wrong object, it whispers secrets or vanishes with your money.

?? Sanctum Quarter – Key Locations
Temple Streets & Shrines:
Pantheon Walk – A grand avenue lined with small shrines and statues to gods of all known worlds, from Ra to Quetzalcoatl.
Hall of Echoes – A central cathedral for the Tower’s “official” pantheon; every prayer echoes as if answered, though the echo may lie.
Divine Garden – A magically sustained garden surrounding the Hall of Echoes; priests say it changes layout according to divine moods.
Shrine of the Silver Light – Athena’s temple; strategic blessings, riddles, and occasional visions.
Chapel of the Iron Eye – Odin’s military-focused temple; ritual sparring with magical guidance.
Hermes’ Crossing – Trade-focused shrine; adventurers leave offerings for travel, safe passage, and information.
The Emerged Shrine – A mysterious temple devoted to newly arrived gods from other dimensions. Some adventurers disappear after visiting.
Notable NPCs & Leaders:
High Priestess Lytha (Athena) – Known for wisdom and tactical guidance. Rumor: she solves disputes through elaborate puzzles.
Warden Thorgar (Odin) – Oversees training rituals. Often recruits Rated adventurers for godly missions.
Messenger Kiva (Hermes) – Scout and info broker; rumors say she knows “who will rise and who will fall” before the System declares it.
Seer Morven (The Emerged) – Unpredictable; sometimes grants visions, sometimes curses. Reputation for testing adventurers in morally ambiguous ways.
Rumors to Seed Players:
A god sometimes visits the Sanctum incognito to observe mortals; being noticed can be both a blessing and a curse.
There is a hidden chamber where wishes can be granted—but for SS-Rank adventurers only, and the price is unknown.
Some shrines are “anchors” for Rifts; if desecrated or tampered with, the Rifts in the city behave unpredictably.
?? Grand Forum – Key Locations
Mini-Map of Locations:
Central Plaza – Statues of legendary adventurers; messages from the gods appear in the sky at sunrise.
Tower Authority Hall – Magister Liora coordinates contracts here; doors are open but the guards never leave your side.
The Black Ledger Hall – Secretive; rumored to track the sins of SS-Rank adventurers.
Adventurer’s Inn – Safe haven for Rated newcomers; gossip flows like ale.
Rift Bulletin Board – A magical board updating all active and expiring Rifts.
Aric’s Observation Tower – SS-Rank Aric Veyne occasionally appears here to watch new adventurers.
Kessan & Mira’s Info Shack – Twins trade rumors for small tasks or favors.
Starlight Stage – Occasionally hosts divine performances; rumors say gods appear disguised in the audience.
Guild Permit Office – Where new guilds submit petitions; bribes rumored to speed approval.
Fountain of Echoes – Toss a coin, hear whispers of upcoming Rifts—or someone’s secret.
Rumors:
Some say the Fountain of Echoes can show you a vision of your death in the Tower.
Contracts occasionally vanish as if the System itself is intervening.
SS-Rank adventurers may secretly manipulate who gets assignments.

?? Guild Spires – Key Locations
Mini-Map of Guilds:
Silver Spire HQ – Aric Veyne’s guild; tactical planning rooms, training dummies enchanted for Rifts.
Ashen Vanguard Keep – Korran’s guild; battlefield arena on top floor for live training.
Emerald Veil Shadow Tower – Hidden from casual view; stealth trials and black ops missions.
Crimson Wing Guildhall – Mercenary hub, known for morally gray contracts.
Iron Ring Citadel – Crafting guild; specializes in rift-resistant weapons and armor.
Guild Tavern Cluster – Social hub for negotiations and rivalries.
Hall of Records – Lists all guild achievements; sometimes manipulated.
Towerbound Academy – Training center for novice Rated adventurers; some floors shift magically.
The Pact Chamber – Secret meeting place where guild alliances are formed or broken.
Arena of Ascendance – Guild duels are held here; winners may gain godly favor.
Rumors:
Some guilds receive contracts directly from gods, bending the System’s rules.
Guilds sometimes sabotage rivals using cursed items or “accidentally” unleashed Rifts.
A secret “floor map” supposedly exists that details every Tower layer; its existence is hotly debated.

??? The Warrens – Key Locations
Mini-Map of Locations:
Scrapworks District – Mara the Scrapper’s territory; salvaging rift tech is a competitive sport.
Brother Thane’s Cult House – Recruitment, strange rituals, rumored divine visions.
Patchwork Saints Hideout – Failed adventurers try to maintain order through force.
The Collapsed Plaza – Streets that disappeared overnight; rumored treasure beneath.
Warren Bazaar – Black market and barter hub for essentials and rare items.
The Night Pits – Fighting pits for survival, entertainment, and divine favor.
The Forgotten Docks – Used for smuggling and secret departures into the Tower.
Echo Alley – Sounds carry oddly; some say it’s haunted by rift spirits.
Marauder’s Crossing – Dangerous shortcut between districts; patrols advised.
Shantytown Heights – Perched slums where rumors say SS-Rank deserters hide.
Rumors:
Entire districts vanish overnight, sometimes with people trapped inside.
Children are rumored to be taken for training by unseen divine hands.
Some hidden caches of SS-Rank gear are said to exist, but none have returned alive.

??? Outer Wall & Gates – Key Locations
Mini-Map of Locations:
Gate of Dawn – Main entrance to Floor 1; guarded heavily by Tower Authority.
Rift Watchtower – Keeps watch on incoming or escaping Rifts.
Captain Verren’s Command Post – Oversees expeditions into the Tower.
Sera’s Scout Outpost – Observation and reconnaissance hub; scouts monitor divine activity.
Barracks of the Rated – Training and lodging for adventurers before expeditions.
Supply Depots – Magical and mundane provisions for teams; heavily rationed.
Gate Plaza – Gathering spot for adventurers awaiting contracts.
Trial Grounds – Practice area for those new to Rifts.
Observation Deck – Offers a view of Floor 1; rumors say you can glimpse higher floors under certain conditions.
Outer Wall Lookout – Monitors the Undercity and surrounding lands for incursion.
Rumors:
Some gates refuse entry to even SS-Rank adventurers if gods are displeased.
Certain gates are alive, whispering secrets or warnings to those nearby.
Expedition teams sometimes return changed, claiming they crossed “forbidden floors” unseen by others.

?? EC Price Guide for Hireables

Optional Price Modifiers
Long-term Hire (7+ days): 10% discount per week
Guild Reputation / Famous Adventurers: +20–50 EC/day for high Rank or fame
Specialized Skills Premiums:
Trap disarming, stealth infiltration, divine rituals, crafting, or diplomacy: +10–30 EC/day
Dual-role adventurers (e.g., Fighter/Mage, Cleric/Rogue): +15–40 EC/day

Approachability Notes
Level 1: High approachability; eager to please, follow orders
Level 2: Moderate; more discerning, expect fair treatment
Level 3+: Low to moderate; confident, may refuse low-paying or unsafe missions

? Outside the Dome
Faction: US Federal “Tower Authority” (FTA)
Type: Bureaucratic Oversight / Paramilitary
HQ: “The Tower” – a heavily fortified, nondescript office complex rumored to intersect a minor rift node.
Operating Philosophy: Paperwork first, action last. Officially tasked with rift monitoring, containment, and “national security compliance,” but in practice, most operations exist to justify budgets and maintain internal hierarchies.

Hierarchy / Major Players
Director Claiborne “Clipboard” Hargrove
Role: FTA Director
Personality: Obsessively detail-oriented, loves memos and flowcharts, terrified of personal liability.
Special Notes: Rarely seen in the field; personally approves every field action. Known to veto effective strategies if forms are incomplete.
Deputy Director Margot “Stamp” Li
Role: Second-in-command, enforcement coordinator
Personality: Efficient but passive-aggressive; wields the rubber stamp like a weapon.
Notes: Operates clandestinely outside the Tower to ensure local authorities submit compliance reports on rift phenomena.
Field Operations Officer “Red Tape” Ramirez
Role: Lead field agent
Personality: Loves procedure over problem-solving. A misstep in the rulebook causes panic.
Notes: Often sends PCs on wild goose chases to complete forms before allowing combat or rift investigation.
Analyst Team Lead Dr. Sophie Kwan
Role: Rift data analyst / arcane bureaucrat
Personality: Brilliant with data, but her reports are indecipherable and rarely actionable.
Notes: Frequently leaks “preliminary rift findings” to outside private groups for personal amusement.

Operations Outside the Tower
Unofficial Field Offices: The FTA maintains covert field offices in major cities, often disguised as mundane federal agencies (e.g., “Department of Infrastructure Compliance”).
Shadow Monitoring Teams: Deploy agents to track rift anomalies under the guise of mundane activities (census, infrastructure inspections, “safety audits”).
Black-File Projects: Certain agents secretly operate outside official Tower orders to secure artifacts or experiment with rift tech, often to pad reports or curry favor.
Bureaucratic Interference: Their presence often slows down other factions, sometimes unintentionally creating rift chaos they are supposed to prevent.

Faction Notes / Flavor
Strengths: Unlimited paperwork, government resources, influence over law enforcement, legal immunity within the Tower’s bureaucratic network.
Weaknesses: Ineffective in actual combat, slow decision-making, and prone to internal sabotage due to factional infighting.
Public Perception: A mix of fear, frustration, and mockery; the FTA is seen as an impenetrable institution that accomplishes little.
Interaction Hooks for PCs:
PC missions delayed or rerouted due to mandatory compliance forms.
Secret FTA agents recruiting “contractors” to handle dangerous rift work outside official channels.
Rumors of internal corruption and rogue experimentation within shadow teams.

2. Terrain / Environmental Notes

3. Random Event Table

4. Scaling Notes (Level 4–6)
Creature Upgrades
Add +1 to attack rolls and +5–10 HP per level bracket.
Increase elemental or rift damage by 1d4.
Combine minor rift creatures into small packs or swarms for added challenge.
Environmental Scaling
Rift cracks widen: Dexterity save DC 13–15, damage 1d6–1d8.
Unstable terrain can collapse partially, creating zones that cost extra movement or deal 1d4 damage.
FTA Scaling
Higher-level field agents gain minor rift tech (stun grenades, energy pistols).
Rogue FTA operatives may have experimental rift devices (ranged AoE, temporary buffs, or status effects).
Event Scaling
Rift surges deal 1d6–1d10 damage and have larger area radius.
Bureaucratic delays may impose additional rounds of skill checks or temporary debuffs.
?? The Apostles – Cultists of Gods & Constellations
Overview:
The Apostles are powerful, devoted agents of gods, demi-gods, or cosmic entities. They seek to influence events inside and outside the Tower, sway adventurers, manipulate guilds, and even control Rift incursions. Some are political and persuasive, others are fanatical combatants.
Traits of Apostles:
Alignment: Varies; some fanatically good or lawful, some chaotic or sinister.
Approachability: Often intimidating but can offer blessings or powerful boons.
Motivation: Advance the goals of their patron god, sway mortals, secure artifacts, or protect sacred sites.
Operating Zones:
Inside the Tower: Temples, Sanctum Quarter, Guild Spires, or hidden chambers.
Outside / Undercity: Street preaching, secret cults, controlling illegal trade, spying on adventurers.
Common Behaviors:
Offer blessings or magical aid for tribute or service.
Recruit adventurers to perform dangerous “holy missions” or clear Rifts in the god’s name.
Manipulate politics, guilds, or city districts to align with divine agendas.
Sometimes oppose one another; conflicting Apostles can cause open skirmishes.

? Example Apostles (Level 1–3)
Acolyte of the Dawn (Level 1)
Race: Human
Class: Cleric (Light Domain)
Alignment: Lawful Good
AC: 12 | HP: 18 (4d8)
Speed: 30 ft.
Attacks:
Mace: +3 to hit, 1d6+1 bludgeoning
Sacred Flame: DC 12 Dex save, 1d8 radiant
Abilities:
Healing Word (1/day)
Guiding Light: Can give +1 bonus to one attack or skill check per round
Appearance: Robes of gold and white, halo-like circlet, radiant eyes
Sayings: “The light guides all who walk the righteous path.”
Motivation: Recruit adventurers to spread the god’s influence, protect sacred shrines
Approachability: Moderate; friendly if respect is shown, otherwise strict

Constellation Seer (Level 2)
Race: Elf
Class: Divination Wizard
Alignment: Neutral Good
AC: 13 | HP: 27 (5d8+5)
Speed: 30 ft.
Attacks:
Staff Strike: +4 to hit, 1d6+2 bludgeoning
Magic Missile: 3 darts, 1d4+1 each
Abilities:
Augury (1/day): Divination to predict outcomes
Constellation Sight: Advantage on Perception or Arcana in outdoor/sky locations
Appearance: Star-patterned robes, glowing sigils on skin
Sayings: “The stars do not lie, but men often misread them.”
Motivation: Identify rising threats and guide events to favor their celestial patron
Approachability: Moderate; cryptic and aloof

Fanatical Apostle (Level 3)
Race: Tiefling
Class: Warlock (Celestial Patron)
Alignment: Chaotic Neutral
AC: 15 | HP: 40 (6d8+12)
Speed: 30 ft.
Attacks:
Eldritch Blast: +5 to hit, 2d10 force
Flaming Smite (Recharge 5–6): 2d8 radiant on hit
Abilities:
Channel Divinity (1/day): Can inspire allies with radiant energy
Dark Oath: Can curse a target (disadvantage on next attack roll)
Appearance: Horns wrapped in silver thread, radiant sigil tattoos, glowing eyes
Sayings: “By my god’s will, I will shape the world… whether you consent or not.”
Motivation: Expand god’s influence via fear, combat, or prophecy
Approachability: Low; intimidating, often demands obedience

??? Typical Apostles’ Tools & Gear
Holy/Arcane Focus: Wands, staves, divine symbols
Minor Magical Items: Potions, scrolls, ritual kits
Blessings: Temporary buffs or resistance granted to allies (1–2 rounds)
Secret Tokens: Mark of their god, can identify fellow Apostles

? Notes for GMs:
Apostles can serve as quest givers, allies, rivals, or city-level manipulators.
A group of mixed-level Apostles can orchestrate complex plots in the Undercity.
Interactions can involve combat, diplomacy, bribery, or divine trial challenges.
Each successful mission earns Legend Points (LP). Use LP to measure how loudly the world notices your party.
At 10 LP: Commoners recognize the PCs.
At 20 LP: Guilds start offering sponsorships.
At 30 LP: Thesaurus begins recording their story directly.
At 40 LP+: The Culinary Council schedules a “banquet.”
DM Tip: Have bards and posters exaggerate PC actions. Fame spreads like Rift infection.
