DISTRICT EVENT TABLE (d8)
Use when PCs spend downtime in a specific area.
d8	District	Event
1	Markets Infinite	Essence Coin inflation sparks riots
2	Sanctum Quarter	Choir miracle backfires—statues bleed
3	Grand Forum	Council speech interrupted by Rift anomaly
4	Guild Spires	Rival Blades duel spills into public plaza
5	Warrens	Lotus enforcers purge informants
6	Outer Wall	Rift incursions breach defenses
7	Understreets	Sewer system mutates; tunnels shift overnight
8	Dome Edge	FTA drones report cracks in a containment barrier
DM Note: Treat these as narrative weather—recurring background conditions that remind the players the city is alive.








CHAPTER 6. LOCATIONS & DISTRICTS

The Undercity is alive—breathing through markets, shrines, alleys, and pipes. Each district pulses with unique culture, dangers, and opportunities. What happens in one block can ripple across the entire Dome within a day.
—?—
OVERVIEW
District	Theme	Guild Influence	Danger Level	Typical Encounters
Markets Infinite	Trade, Relics, Corruption	Iron Fang Consortium	Moderate	Smugglers, relic spirits
Sanctum Quarter	Faith, Politics, Divine Intrigue	Serpent Choir	High	Apostles, zealots
Grand Forum	Governance, Information	Ashen Scrolls, Council	Variable	Bureaucrats, spies
Guild Spires	Heroics, Competition	Argent Blades	Moderate	Duelists, recruiters
The Warrens	Crime, Survival	Obsidian Lotus	High	Assassins, mutants
Outer Wall &Gates	Defense, Discipline	Wardens of Ash	Severe	Soldiers, Rift creatures

—?—
MARKETS INFINITE
Theme: Endless bazaar of relics, monster parts, and miracles-for-sale.
Guild: Iron Fang Consortium
Atmosphere: Neon rune signs, hagglers shouting over Rift alarms, relic inspectors in gilded masks.
Landmarks:
The Bloodscale Exchange: Central auction house for monster materials.
Fanghall: Serrik Dhal’s fortified counting house and office.
The Molten Street: Vendors selling illegally active Rift residue tainted items (requires Arcana save to approach).
Encounters:
Relic appraisal gone wrong—artifact awakens.
Smuggler duel over forged relic permits.
Rift crack opens beneath an auction stage mid-sale.
Rumors:
“They say the Consortium’s profits are blessed by the Culinary Council.”
“Buy the wrong charm, and it’s you that’s bound.”
DM Note: The marketplace is a perfect hub for introducing new PCs, equipment upgrades, or moral gray zones.
—?—
SANCTUM QUARTER
Theme: Faith made flesh; temples rise like cathedrals stitched from light.
Guild: Serpent Choir
Atmosphere: Constant hymns, incense clouds, contract-priests debating loopholes.
Landmarks:
The Basilica of Binding: Central hub for divine contract signing.
Shrine of Endless Taste: Culinary Council front disguised as soup kitchen.
Mirrormouth Plaza: Square of statues that whisper divine messages.
Encounters:
Miracle duel—two clerics invoke rival gods to heal a dying noble.
Apostles demand inspection of holy relics, suspecting heresy.
Rift bloom erupts inside a confession chamber.
Rumors:
“The Choir keeps records of every prayer ever spoken.”
“You can buy forgiveness here—just not cheaply.”
DM Note: The Quarter runs on spiritual capitalism. Treat faith as contract law; morality is enforceable only if notarized.
—?—
GRAND FORUM
Theme: Bureaucratic theater; the city’s laws are written, rewritten, and debated in public spectacle.
Guilds: High Council, Ashen Scrolls, Tower Authority offices.
Atmosphere: Gold-marbled halls filled with echoing arguments and drifting Riftlight through stained-glass ceilings.
Landmarks:
Council Hall of Six: The heart of Undercity politics.
Vault of Decrees: Magical archive that updates laws in real time.
Tower Authority Annex: Government building doubling as containment facility.
Encounters:
Bureaucrat duel—arguments resolved through spell duels of semantics.
Rift anomaly during Council vote.
PCs must retrieve a misplaced prophecy document before it “self-destructs.”
Rumors:
“The Arbiter’s desk bleeds ink if lies are spoken nearby.”
“There’s a second Council chamber below, where gods sit in judgment.”
DM Note: The Forum is your political dungeon. Every hallway is a trap of etiquette; every sentence can kill a career.
—?—
GUILD SPIRES
Theme: Heroism as spectacle; adventurers as celebrities.
Guild: Argent Blades
Atmosphere: Marble arenas, neon banners, and magical projectors broadcasting duels.
Landmarks:
The Silver Colosseum: Arena for sanctioned guild battles and Rift showcases.
Hall of Deeds: A massive ledger that automatically records verified heroics.
Hero’s Rest Tavern: Gathering spot for braggarts and recruiters.
Encounters:
A rival party challenges PCs to a public duel for sponsorship rights.
Rift opens mid-performance—real blood spills for audience applause.
PCs must protect or sabotage a champion’s rise.
Rumors:
“Every cheer feeds a god.”
“Some Blades fake their deaths to sell their stories twice.”
DM Note: Use the Spires for lighthearted chaos or emotional crescendos. The crowd is always watching—and judging.
—?—
THE WARRENS
Theme: Survival, secrecy, and sin.
Guild: Obsidian Lotus
Atmosphere: Claustrophobic tunnels lit by fungus and stolen light-crystals.
Landmarks:
Lotus Den: Underground bazaar for contraband and information.
Whisper Wells: Communal shrines that “drink” secrets whispered into them.
Memory Market: Place where people sell fragments of their past.
Encounters:
Ambush by amnesiac thieves who forgot why they attacked.
Rift mutation causing the tunnels to rearrange themselves.
PCs hired to silence a memory dealer who knows too much.
Rumors:
“If you can’t remember last night, check the Market—you might’ve sold it.”
“The Widow sees through every shadow.”
DM Note: The Warrens are ideal for noir-style plots and espionage adventures. Morality down here costs extra.





—?—
OUTER WALL & GATES
Theme: Militarized bastion protecting the city from outside Rift zones.
Guild: Wardens of Ash
Atmosphere: Smoky forges, disciplined soldiers, blaring alarms, endless drills.
Landmarks:
The Ash Gate: Main defense against Rift incursions.
Warden Bastion: Command post of Captain Havel Korin.
The Burnfields: Area beyond the Wall where reality still burns.
Encounters:
Rift breach overwhelms patrol squads—PCs reinforce defenses.
Wardens court-martial one of their own for heresy.
FTA envoy arrives demanding control a portion of the Wall.
Rumors:
“Wardens train with real demons—because they’re cheaper than recruits.”
“Ashara herself walked these walls once.”
DM Note: Treat this district as the campaign’s pulse during wartime arcs. When the Wall trembles, the city panics.
—?—
CHAPTER 7. ENCOUNTERS & CREATURES
The Undercity is a living dungeon. Its streets spawn predators, divine echoes, and experimental horrors built from bad decisions. Encounters here are not random—they’re the ecosystem’s immune response to heroism.
—?—
USING ENCOUNTERS IN THE UNDERCITY
Treat every encounter as a conversation between factions, gods, and the city itself. Even the smallest fight can shift guild politics or divine balance.
Encounter Categories:
Urban Hazards: Street-level conflicts, riots, or relic accidents.
Rift Events: Monsters or distortions leaking through tears in reality.
Divine Manifestations: Gods testing mortals or “collecting” fame.
FTA Interventions: Bureaucratic enforcers showing up mid-chaos.

—?—
?? Dynamic Rift Events – Undercity
1?? Rift Anatomy
Size / Tier: Minor ? Medium ? Large ? Floor-Level Invasion.
Spawn Window: 3 days before spillover into districts.
Creature Type: Determined by Rift origin; normal weapons ineffective.
Magic Requirement: Only magical/system-created weapons can harm creatures.
Environmental Effect: Rifts distort terrain, lighting, gravity, or ambient magic.

2?? Event Triggers
Roll a d10 or select based on LP / Quest Tier:

3?? Dynamic Event Mechanics
Scale: Adjust CR or number of monsters based on LP or party level.
Time Pressure: Rifts naturally escalate every X turns; PCs must act quickly.
Loot / EC / Kharma: Reward for closing Rift includes randomized EC, Kharma, and chance for rare magical crafting materials.
Complications: Combine multiple event triggers for higher-tier Rifts (e.g., 6 + 3 = Hostages + Mutation).

4?? Quick Rift Event Table (d20 for granularity)

5?? DM Tips
Combine Quick Rift Events + Random Quest Table for instant mission generation.
Use LP as scaling factor: higher LP ? more complex / dangerous events.
Track Culinary Council / Divine Observation: each heroic action near a Rift can increase attention.
Make environmental hazards interactive: PCs can manipulate floors, walls, or magical devices to affect outcomes.
Encourage creative solutions: magic-only combat, environmental tricks, teamwork.
 Example Rifts. 
Scenario 1: The Shopfront Rift
Tier: 1–2 | Quest Type: Rift Clearance / Local Trouble
Setup:
A minor Rift opens in a busy street-level marketplace of the Undercity. Strange, weak creatures begin spilling out. Local merchants panic, and one Arcanist Guild shop is at risk of total destruction.
Objectives:
Seal the Rift before it grows.
Protect civilians and the merchant’s shop.
Optional: recover magical residue for the Arcanist Guild.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
d6 minor monsters emerge (e.g., small slimes, imps, or shadow critters).
Rift causes random sparks that occasionally stun or damage nearby PCs (Dex save DC 12).
Rival Thieves Guild shows up to steal loot while chaos erupts.
Rewards:
5–10 Kharma.
10–15 EC.
Minor magical trinket from Arcanist Guild shop.

Scenario 2: Sewer Skirmish
Tier: 2 | Quest Type: Patrol / Investigation
Setup:
A small Rift has appeared in the old sewage tunnels under the Warrens. Monsters are starting to infect the tunnel ecosystem. The Wardens of Ash request PCs to investigate.
Objectives:
Navigate tunnels safely and locate Rift source.
Eliminate minor monster threats (giant rats infused with Rift energy, small oozes).
Map tunnel hazards for future Warden patrols.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Environmental hazard: collapsing ceiling, slick floors (Dex save DC 11 to avoid falling prone).
Rift leaks minor magic pulses; low-level spells sometimes misfire (Magic Surge).
Obsidian Lotus gang scouts appear, curious about Rift loot.
Rewards:
7–12 Kharma.
15–20 EC.
Recognition by Wardens; possible minor favor for later high-stakes quests.

Scenario 3: Library Disturbance
Tier: 1–2 | Quest Type: Investigation / Escort
Setup:
A Rift has appeared in the general access section of Thesaurus’ library. Low-level magical anomalies are causing books to animate and attack visitors.
Objectives:
Escort librarians and scholars to safety.
Close Rift and calm animated books.
Optional: recover rare story scrolls for Thesaurus.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Animated books (AC 12, HP 8 each, low-damage melee attacks).
Rift emits strange temporal pulses; characters may act twice or miss a turn randomly (Temporal Glitch).
Culinary Council observer discreetly watches heroic actions.
Rewards:
5–10 Kharma.
10–15 EC.
Special “Story Insight” bonus: PCs can gain temporary Inspiration or advantage on lore checks next session.
Scenario 1: Abandoned Workshop (Level 1)
Floor: 2nd sublevel beneath Undercity
Quest Type: Exploration / Investigation
Setup:
The PCs are asked by the Arcanist Guild to investigate an abandoned workshop that has been mysteriously sealed for decades. Rumors say a Rift briefly appeared here, leaving behind unstable magical residues.
Objectives:
Explore the workshop safely.
Identify lingering magical anomalies.
Recover usable magical components for Arcanist Guild.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Minor animated constructs (AC 13, HP 10) patrol the floor.
Magic pulses randomly trigger minor traps or alarms.
Floor tiles are unstable; small Dex checks (DC 12) to avoid falls.
Rewards:
5–8 Kharma.
10 EC.
Low-tier magical crafting material (e.g., component for a +1 wand or enchanted coin).

Scenario 2: Flooded Passage (Level 2)
Floor: 3rd sublevel — partially submerged tunnels
Quest Type: Rift Clearance / Environmental Hazard
Setup:
A small Rift has opened in a flooded floor beneath the Undercity. The Wardens of Ash request a clearance team. The water makes movement difficult and creates hazards.
Objectives:
Seal the Rift.
Rescue trapped NPC workers or minor adventurers.
Avoid environmental hazards like strong currents or sudden collapses.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Water-borne Rift creatures (CR 1/2–1) attack on sight.
Flooding can trap PCs; Strength or Athletics checks (DC 12–13) required to avoid being swept away.
Rival guild scavengers may attempt to claim loot mid-mission.
Rewards:
8–12 Kharma.
15 EC.
Minor magical trinket or consumable (healing potion or elemental vial).

Scenario 3: Library Spiral (Level 3)
Floor: 5th sublevel — Thesaurus’ restricted floors (low-tier access)
Quest Type: Escort / Exploration / Light Combat
Setup:
Thesaurus sends the PCs to retrieve a series of story scrolls from the restricted spiral floors. The area is protected by animated storybooks, minor constructs, and environmental traps to prevent casual access.
Objectives:
Navigate maze-like floor safely.
Avoid or defeat low-level guardians.
Recover designated scrolls and return to the general library.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Animated books (AC 12, HP 12, low-damage attacks) roam hallways.
Floors shift periodically due to Rift instability (Dex check DC 13 to avoid falling or being separated).
Minor Temporal Glitches may cause PCs to repeat or skip a turn.
Rewards:
10–15 Kharma.
20 EC.
“Story Insight”: temporary advantage on Investigation, Arcana, or History checks for next session.
Optional minor boons from Thesaurus (e.g., hint about ongoing saga or safe shortcut).
Tower Floor Ascention: 
Scenario 1: The Mirror Plains (Level 1)
Floor: 1st above Undercity — warped reflection of Undercity streets
Quest Type: Exploration / Investigation
Setup:
The PCs are transported to a mirrored version of the Undercity. Everything is subtly off: reflections move independently, street vendors sell impossible items, and monsters appear as warped reflections of real citizens.
Objectives:
Investigate anomalies in this mirrored world.
Rescue captured NPCs trapped in reflection prisons.
Close a minor Rift connecting the Mirror Plains to the Undercity.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Reflected monsters mimic PCs’ abilities (low-level clones, AC 12–13, HP 8–10).
Environmental hazards: streets twist and rotate, forcing DC 12 Acrobatics/Perception checks.
Rival adventurers (or minor god agents) are hunting the Rift.
Rewards:
5–8 Kharma.
10–15 EC.
Minor magical trinket that reacts to reflections.

Scenario 2: The Past Rewritten (Level 2)
Floor: 2nd above Undercity — fragment of a historical world
Quest Type: Exploration / Story Alteration
Setup:
The floor recreates a past event from one of the Tower’s attached worlds: a siege or festival gone wrong. The PCs discover a “down-on-his-luck” hero trapped by the timeline who failed to make the right choices. They can intervene and alter history, saving him from death or disgrace.
Objectives:
Prevent the Rift from fully rewriting the past.
Rescue or guide the trapped hero to success.
Collect magical story fragments for Thesaurus.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Rift anomalies: minor monsters from “future” timelines attack (AC 12, HP 10–12).
Puzzle: manipulate events to ensure history stabilizes while allowing the hero’s survival.
Environmental hazards: collapsing buildings, magical feedback from Rift energy (Dex/Arcana DC 12–13).
Consequences / Continuity:
The rescued hero survives and appears in the next floor to aid PCs in the Tower Defense scenario.
Player choices here influence narrative: hero may inspire NPC defenders or provide tactical insight.
Rewards:
8–12 Kharma.
15–20 EC.
Temporal Insight: advantage on Investigation, Arcana, or History checks next session.

Scenario 3: Tower Defense – The Shattered Gate (Level 3)
Floor: 3rd above Undercity — fortress floor
Quest Type: Tower Defense / Combat / Guild Coordination
Setup:
A large Rift erupts, threatening the defensive gates of the Tower’s upper floors. PCs must organize defenses, coordinate with low-level Warden squads, and fight monsters until reinforcements arrive. The hero saved on the previous floor joins the defense, providing buffs, extra attacks, or tactical advice.
Objectives:
Hold key choke points against waves of Rift creatures.
Direct NPC defenders and set up barricades or magical wards.
Close Rift at the gate before it collapses.
Complications / Dynamic Events:
Rift waves spawn every 3 rounds (CR 1–2 creatures).
Environmental hazards: partial floor collapse, magical surges (Dex/Strength checks DC 12).
Rival guild spies may try to sabotage defenses.
Rewards:
12–18 Kharma.
20–25 EC.
Minor magical items (enhanced shield, +1 weapon, consumables).
Guild reputation boost; opens access to higher-tier missions.
Player choices in the Past Rewritten floor can influence hero’s performance and NPC morale.

? DM Tips for Linked Floors:
Track player decisions in the past floor: who they save, which events they change.
Allow NPC hero to scale slightly with player level for the Tower Defense.
Introduce dynamic Rift events mid-defense for added tension.
Highlight story consequences: saving someone may change guild interactions or divine observation.
Scenario 1: Mirror Plains (Level 1)
NPCs
Mira Veyra – Trapped Mirror Vendor
Role: Civilians needing rescue
Stat Block: Commoner (MM p.345)
Hooks: Will reward PCs with minor reflective trinkets; knows secret mirror shortcuts.
Reflected Minor God Agent
Role: Rival adventurer-like agent from minor deity
Stat Block: Scout (MM p.349)
Hooks: Observes PCs; may interfere or challenge based on Divine favor.
Creatures / Monsters
Mirror Imps
AC: 12 | HP: 8 | Attack: 1d4 piercing (claws)
Traits: Mimic PC abilities at random (choose 1 spell or attack per round)
Dynamic Event: Occasionally swap places with PCs’ reflections (Dex save DC 12 to avoid confusion).
Mirror Slime
AC: 11 | HP: 10 | Attack: 1d6 acid
Traits: Splits on death into two 1 HP slimes
Environmental Interaction: Can slide across reflective surfaces for advantage.

Tower Floor 4: The Hall of Fools – Comedic / Tragic Court
Floor Theme
The floor simulates a living court, combining absurd politics, heroic satire, and tragicomic nobles.
Court is run by various minor gods or archetypal “nobles” who observe PC choices for divine Kharma.
Most problems are social puzzles, diplomacy, or chaos avoidance, not combat.
Trigger combat if PCs insult the Baron, ignore court etiquette, or meddle too heavily in divine theater.

Random Roles & Equipment

Roles Assignment
Randomly roll or assign via table: 1–6 above.
Equipment comes with minor magical or narrative effects, often useful for solving court problems or RP challenges.
Roles don’t carry over from Floor 3, emphasizing the absurdity of the court.

Scenario Mechanics
Social Challenges: etiquette checks, persuasion contests, rumor management, bribery, and divine favor rolls.
Kharma Gain / Loss: heavily influenced by clever or funny roleplaying.
Combat Trigger (Baron):
If PCs insult the Baron, sabotage divine rituals, or provoke nobles: trigger Baron-level fight (CR 4–5, single powerful enemy).
Combat is rare, meant as punitive / climactic event.

Baron NPC (Optional Boss)
Baron Aristrok: pedantic, narcissistic minor god in noble guise
Stat Block: Mage (MM p.347) with buffs for courtly “envy / prestige”
Special Abilities:
Scornful Command: force one PC to waste turn bowing or apologizing
Wealth Drain: temporarily removes Kharma from careless PCs
Comedic Potential: exaggerated gestures, slipping on rugs, angry poetry recitations

DM Tips
Encourage comedic mishaps, absurd political negotiations, and tragic RP elements.
Let equipment have narrative effects, e.g., joke wand causes NPCs to burst into laughter, feather quill accidentally sets papers on fire.
Make combat the least desirable outcome; reward clever social maneuvering.
Minor Kharma bonuses for clever resolutions, improvisation, or amusing failures.
Court Hooks for Social / Diplomatic Challenges
1. The Missing Crown
Hook: The Baron’s ceremonial crown has gone missing right before a divine inspection.
Objective: Investigate, interrogate nobles or servants, and recover it without embarrassing the Baron.
Chaos Potential: Accusing the wrong NPC triggers scandal; combat if Baron deems you “criminals.”

2. Poisoned Dessert
Hook: A tray of magically infused pastries meant for a minor god causes unpredictable effects.
Objective: Identify the culprit or neutralize effects before the god consumes it.
Chaos Potential: PCs fail checks ? minor god temporarily enraged, NPCs start panicking.

3. Rumor Mill
Hook: False rumors are spreading in the court, threatening to topple a minister’s standing.
Objective: Use persuasion, deception, or social insight to reveal the truth or redirect blame.
Chaos Potential: Mishandling rumors may spark duels or baronial wrath.

4. Duel of Etiquette
Hook: Two nobles challenge each other over a slight insult; Baron demands a “trial by manners.”
Objective: Advise, mediate, or participate to prevent catastrophic embarrassment.
Chaos Potential: Misstep ? a slapstick duel escalates into full combat; PCs may gain or lose Kharma.

5. Misfiled Decrees
Hook: Ancient scrolls with contradictory laws accidentally sent to the wrong offices.
Objective: Find and correct misfiled decrees without offending the gods.
Chaos Potential: PCs accidentally enforce the wrong law ? court riot or magical anomaly.

6. Divine Complaints
Hook: Minor gods complain to the court about heroes’ behavior in lower floors.
Objective: Smooth over grievances with diplomacy or creative offerings (e.g., humorous apology, symbolic gift).
Chaos Potential: Failure ? god sends a small Rift, or Baron summons magical enforcers.

7. Errant Bard
Hook: A bard performs a satirical song mocking the Baron and court traditions.
Objective: Calm tensions, redirect performance, or secretly enhance it to please the Baron.
Chaos Potential: PCs intervene poorly ? bard insults Baron, triggering combat or public disgrace.

8. Magical Malfunction
Hook: Enchanted décor (floating candles, self-replenishing wine) malfunctions mid-ceremony.
Objective: Fix it using clever items, spells, or improvisation without causing panic.
Chaos Potential: Failing a check may cause small explosions, injured NPCs, or Baron outrage.

9. Guest of Honor
Hook: A visiting hero or minor god refuses to sit according to protocol.
Objective: Mediate seating, flattery, or negotiation to avoid insulting anyone.
Chaos Potential: Mismanagement ? duel, magical attack, or NPC mutiny.

10. Secret Alliance
Hook: Two court factions are plotting behind the Baron’s back.
Objective: Discover their plan, negotiate, or manipulate for maximum Kharma / minimal damage.
Chaos Potential: Mistakenly supporting a faction ? Baron declares betrayal; PCs must improvise escape or appeasement.

?? DM Tips:
Each hook can be resolved through clever roleplay, skill checks (Persuasion, Insight, Deception, Performance), or minor magical use.
Roll for chaos escalation if PCs fail key checks.
Small Kharma rewards for subtle, creative, or funny solutions—punitive consequences for blunders.
Further City Information 
 
?? Markets Infinite – Key Locations
Districts & Streets:
Neon Row – Bright holograms, alien tech shops, and cyberpunk-style gadget stalls. Locals claim the lights themselves sometimes “hint” at hidden sales or secret vendors.
Cobbleway Market – Medieval-style streets with blacksmiths, forges, and enchanted weapon shops. Street performers demonstrate minor magical feats for coins.
Floating Bazaar – Airships and levitating platforms host interdimensional merchants selling rare ingredients and exotic pets.
The Crimson Alley – Hidden among Neon Row; black market with rift-forged weapons, illegal artifacts, and cursed scrolls. Guards are rumor-sensitive—if you hear about it, you already shouldn’t be there.
Taste of Worlds – Multicultural food court. You can sample alien delicacies alongside traditional Earth meals; some vendors claim to cook with “essence from Rifts” for enhanced effects.
Major Stores & Stalls:
Veyra’s Vault – System-made weapons & armor. Prices skyrocket for SS-Rank adventurers. Rumor: Some weapons “choose” their wielders.
Elune’s Apothecary – Potions, cures, magical supplements, and rare rift reagents. Occasionally blessed by gods.
Kalyx Tech & Trinkets – Alien cybernetics, AI familiars, dimensional gadgets. Neon-blue signage flickers in unknown scripts.
The Wishing Stall – A tent where merchants sell “prayers” as scrolls or charms. Some are genuine blessings; others are cursed trinkets.
Patchwork Oddities – Artifacts salvaged from failed rifts, often dangerous but high-risk/high-reward.
Rumors to Seed Players:
A portal to a hidden floor opens randomly somewhere in the Floating Bazaar—but only at midnight under the artificial moon.
Crimson Alley has a dealer who “trades sins for power” – you leave stronger but with a secret debt to a god.
Some shops are sentient; if you speak to the wrong object, it whispers secrets or vanishes with your money.

?? Sanctum Quarter – Key Locations
Temple Streets & Shrines:
Pantheon Walk – A grand avenue lined with small shrines and statues to gods of all known worlds, from Ra to Quetzalcoatl.
Hall of Echoes – A central cathedral for the Tower’s “official” pantheon; every prayer echoes as if answered, though the echo may lie.
Divine Garden – A magically sustained garden surrounding the Hall of Echoes; priests say it changes layout according to divine moods.
Shrine of the Silver Light – Athena’s temple; strategic blessings, riddles, and occasional visions.
Chapel of the Iron Eye – Odin’s military-focused temple; ritual sparring with magical guidance.
Hermes’ Crossing – Trade-focused shrine; adventurers leave offerings for travel, safe passage, and information.
The Emerged Shrine – A mysterious temple devoted to newly arrived gods from other dimensions. Some adventurers disappear after visiting.
Notable NPCs & Leaders:
High Priestess Lytha (Athena) – Known for wisdom and tactical guidance. Rumor: she solves disputes through elaborate puzzles.
Warden Thorgar (Odin) – Oversees training rituals. Often recruits Rated adventurers for godly missions.
Messenger Kiva (Hermes) – Scout and info broker; rumors say she knows “who will rise and who will fall” before the System declares it.
Seer Morven (The Emerged) – Unpredictable; sometimes grants visions, sometimes curses. Reputation for testing adventurers in morally ambiguous ways.
Rumors to Seed Players:
A god sometimes visits the Sanctum incognito to observe mortals; being noticed can be both a blessing and a curse.
There is a hidden chamber where wishes can be granted—but for SS-Rank adventurers only, and the price is unknown.
Some shrines are “anchors” for Rifts; if desecrated or tampered with, the Rifts in the city behave unpredictably.
?? Grand Forum – Key Locations
Mini-Map of Locations:
Central Plaza – Statues of legendary adventurers; messages from the gods appear in the sky at sunrise.
Tower Authority Hall – Magister Liora coordinates contracts here; doors are open but the guards never leave your side.
The Black Ledger Hall – Secretive; rumored to track the sins of SS-Rank adventurers.
Adventurer’s Inn – Safe haven for Rated newcomers; gossip flows like ale.
Rift Bulletin Board – A magical board updating all active and expiring Rifts.
Aric’s Observation Tower – SS-Rank Aric Veyne occasionally appears here to watch new adventurers.
Kessan & Mira’s Info Shack – Twins trade rumors for small tasks or favors.
Starlight Stage – Occasionally hosts divine performances; rumors say gods appear disguised in the audience.
Guild Permit Office – Where new guilds submit petitions; bribes rumored to speed approval.
Fountain of Echoes – Toss a coin, hear whispers of upcoming Rifts—or someone’s secret.
Rumors:
Some say the Fountain of Echoes can show you a vision of your death in the Tower.
Contracts occasionally vanish as if the System itself is intervening.
SS-Rank adventurers may secretly manipulate who gets assignments.

?? Guild Spires – Key Locations
Mini-Map of Guilds:
Silver Spire HQ – Aric Veyne’s guild; tactical planning rooms, training dummies enchanted for Rifts.
Ashen Vanguard Keep – Korran’s guild; battlefield arena on top floor for live training.
Emerald Veil Shadow Tower – Hidden from casual view; stealth trials and black ops missions.
Crimson Wing Guildhall – Mercenary hub, known for morally gray contracts.
Iron Ring Citadel – Crafting guild; specializes in rift-resistant weapons and armor.
Guild Tavern Cluster – Social hub for negotiations and rivalries.
Hall of Records – Lists all guild achievements; sometimes manipulated.
Towerbound Academy – Training center for novice Rated adventurers; some floors shift magically.
The Pact Chamber – Secret meeting place where guild alliances are formed or broken.
Arena of Ascendance – Guild duels are held here; winners may gain godly favor.
Rumors:
Some guilds receive contracts directly from gods, bending the System’s rules.
Guilds sometimes sabotage rivals using cursed items or “accidentally” unleashed Rifts.
A secret “floor map” supposedly exists that details every Tower layer; its existence is hotly debated.

??? The Warrens – Key Locations
Mini-Map of Locations:
Scrapworks District – Mara the Scrapper’s territory; salvaging rift tech is a competitive sport.
Brother Thane’s Cult House – Recruitment, strange rituals, rumored divine visions.
Patchwork Saints Hideout – Failed adventurers try to maintain order through force.
The Collapsed Plaza – Streets that disappeared overnight; rumored treasure beneath.
Warren Bazaar – Black market and barter hub for essentials and rare items.
The Night Pits – Fighting pits for survival, entertainment, and divine favor.
The Forgotten Docks – Used for smuggling and secret departures into the Tower.
Echo Alley – Sounds carry oddly; some say it’s haunted by rift spirits.
Marauder’s Crossing – Dangerous shortcut between districts; patrols advised.
Shantytown Heights – Perched slums where rumors say SS-Rank deserters hide.
Rumors:
Entire districts vanish overnight, sometimes with people trapped inside.
Children are rumored to be taken for training by unseen divine hands.
Some hidden caches of SS-Rank gear are said to exist, but none have returned alive.

??? Outer Wall & Gates – Key Locations
Mini-Map of Locations:
Gate of Dawn – Main entrance to Floor 1; guarded heavily by Tower Authority.
Rift Watchtower – Keeps watch on incoming or escaping Rifts.
Captain Verren’s Command Post – Oversees expeditions into the Tower.
Sera’s Scout Outpost – Observation and reconnaissance hub; scouts monitor divine activity.
Barracks of the Rated – Training and lodging for adventurers before expeditions.
Supply Depots – Magical and mundane provisions for teams; heavily rationed.
Gate Plaza – Gathering spot for adventurers awaiting contracts.
Trial Grounds – Practice area for those new to Rifts.
Observation Deck – Offers a view of Floor 1; rumors say you can glimpse higher floors under certain conditions.
Outer Wall Lookout – Monitors the Undercity and surrounding lands for incursion.
Rumors:
Some gates refuse entry to even SS-Rank adventurers if gods are displeased.
Certain gates are alive, whispering secrets or warnings to those nearby.
Expedition teams sometimes return changed, claiming they crossed “forbidden floors” unseen by others.
?? Grand Forum NPCs

Personality & Motivation: Calculating strategist; devoted to protecting humanity and training strong adventurers.
Sayings: “Every move echoes… make yours count.” / “The Tower tests us; we do not test the Tower.”

?? EC Price Guide for Hireables

Optional Price Modifiers
Long-term Hire (7+ days): 10% discount per week
Guild Reputation / Famous Adventurers: +20–50 EC/day for high Rank or fame
Specialized Skills Premiums:
Trap disarming, stealth infiltration, divine rituals, crafting, or diplomacy: +10–30 EC/day
Dual-role adventurers (e.g., Fighter/Mage, Cleric/Rogue): +15–40 EC/day

Approachability Notes
Level 1: High approachability; eager to please, follow orders
Level 2: Moderate; more discerning, expect fair treatment
Level 3+: Low to moderate; confident, may refuse low-paying or unsafe missions

? Outside the Dome
Faction: US Federal “Tower Authority” (FTA)
Type: Bureaucratic Oversight / Paramilitary
HQ: “The Tower” – a heavily fortified, nondescript office complex rumored to intersect a minor rift node.
Operating Philosophy: Paperwork first, action last. Officially tasked with rift monitoring, containment, and “national security compliance,” but in practice, most operations exist to justify budgets and maintain internal hierarchies.

Hierarchy / Major Players
Director Claiborne “Clipboard” Hargrove
Role: FTA Director
Personality: Obsessively detail-oriented, loves memos and flowcharts, terrified of personal liability.
Special Notes: Rarely seen in the field; personally approves every field action. Known to veto effective strategies if forms are incomplete.
Deputy Director Margot “Stamp” Li
Role: Second-in-command, enforcement coordinator
Personality: Efficient but passive-aggressive; wields the rubber stamp like a weapon.
Notes: Operates clandestinely outside the Tower to ensure local authorities submit compliance reports on rift phenomena.
Field Operations Officer “Red Tape” Ramirez
Role: Lead field agent
Personality: Loves procedure over problem-solving. A misstep in the rulebook causes panic.
Notes: Often sends PCs on wild goose chases to complete forms before allowing combat or rift investigation.
Analyst Team Lead Dr. Sophie Kwan
Role: Rift data analyst / arcane bureaucrat
Personality: Brilliant with data, but her reports are indecipherable and rarely actionable.
Notes: Frequently leaks “preliminary rift findings” to outside private groups for personal amusement.

Operations Outside the Tower
Unofficial Field Offices: The FTA maintains covert field offices in major cities, often disguised as mundane federal agencies (e.g., “Department of Infrastructure Compliance”).
Shadow Monitoring Teams: Deploy agents to track rift anomalies under the guise of mundane activities (census, infrastructure inspections, “safety audits”).
Black-File Projects: Certain agents secretly operate outside official Tower orders to secure artifacts or experiment with rift tech, often to pad reports or curry favor.
Bureaucratic Interference: Their presence often slows down other factions, sometimes unintentionally creating rift chaos they are supposed to prevent.

Faction Notes / Flavor
Strengths: Unlimited paperwork, government resources, influence over law enforcement, legal immunity within the Tower’s bureaucratic network.
Weaknesses: Ineffective in actual combat, slow decision-making, and prone to internal sabotage due to factional infighting.
Public Perception: A mix of fear, frustration, and mockery; the FTA is seen as an impenetrable institution that accomplishes little.
Interaction Hooks for PCs:
PC missions delayed or rerouted due to mandatory compliance forms.
Secret FTA agents recruiting “contractors” to handle dangerous rift work outside official channels.
Rumors of internal corruption and rogue experimentation within shadow teams.

1. Loot / Rewards

2. Terrain / Environmental Notes

3. Random Event Table

4. Scaling Notes (Level 4–6)
Creature Upgrades
Add +1 to attack rolls and +5–10 HP per level bracket.
Increase elemental or rift damage by 1d4.
Combine minor rift creatures into small packs or swarms for added challenge.
Environmental Scaling
Rift cracks widen: Dexterity save DC 13–15, damage 1d6–1d8.
Unstable terrain can collapse partially, creating zones that cost extra movement or deal 1d4 damage.
FTA Scaling
Higher-level field agents gain minor rift tech (stun grenades, energy pistols).
Rogue FTA operatives may have experimental rift devices (ranged AoE, temporary buffs, or status effects).
Event Scaling
Rift surges deal 1d6–1d10 damage and have larger area radius.
Bureaucratic delays may impose additional rounds of skill checks or temporary debuffs.
?? The Apostles – Cultists of Gods & Constellations
Overview:
The Apostles are powerful, devoted agents of gods, demi-gods, or cosmic entities. They seek to influence events inside and outside the Tower, sway adventurers, manipulate guilds, and even control Rift incursions. Some are political and persuasive, others are fanatical combatants.
Traits of Apostles:
Alignment: Varies; some fanatically good or lawful, some chaotic or sinister.
Approachability: Often intimidating but can offer blessings or powerful boons.
Motivation: Advance the goals of their patron god, sway mortals, secure artifacts, or protect sacred sites.
Operating Zones:
Inside the Tower: Temples, Sanctum Quarter, Guild Spires, or hidden chambers.
Outside / Undercity: Street preaching, secret cults, controlling illegal trade, spying on adventurers.
Common Behaviors:
Offer blessings or magical aid for tribute or service.
Recruit adventurers to perform dangerous “holy missions” or clear Rifts in the god’s name.
Manipulate politics, guilds, or city districts to align with divine agendas.
Sometimes oppose one another; conflicting Apostles can cause open skirmishes.

? Example Apostles (Level 1–3)
Acolyte of the Dawn (Level 1)
Race: Human
Class: Cleric (Light Domain)
Alignment: Lawful Good
AC: 12 | HP: 18 (4d8)
Speed: 30 ft.

Healing Word (1/day)
Guiding Light: Can give +1 bonus to one attack or skill check per round
Appearance: Robes of gold and white, halo-like circlet, radiant eyes
Sayings: “The light guides all who walk the righteous path.”
Motivation: Recruit adventurers to spread the god’s influence, protect sacred shrines
Approachability: Moderate; friendly if respect is shown, otherwise strict

Dark Oath: Can curse a target (disadvantage on next attack roll)
Appearance: Horns wrapped in silver thread, radiant sigil tattoos, glowing eyes
Sayings: “By my god’s will, I will shape the world… whether you consent or not.”
Motivation: Expand god’s influence via fear, combat, or prophecy
Approachability: Low; intimidating, often demands obedience

??? Typical Apostles’ Tools & Gear
Holy/Arcane Focus: Wands, staves, divine symbols
Minor Magical Items: Potions, scrolls, ritual kits
Blessings: Temporary buffs or resistance granted to allies (1–2 rounds)
Secret Tokens: Mark of their god, can identify fellow Apostles

? Notes for GMs:
Apostles can serve as quest givers, allies, rivals, or city-level manipulators.
A group of mixed-level Apostles can orchestrate complex plots in the Undercity.
Interactions can involve combat, diplomacy, bribery, or divine trial challenges.
RANDOM ENCOUNTER TABLE (d20)
Roll for tension, not for time. The Undercity doesn’t sleep.
d20	Encounter	Notes
1	Lost courier delivers sealed divine writ addressed to PCs	Document writes itself as they read
2	Fang traders arguing over cursed relic	Relic animates mid-debate
3	Choir procession transforms into zealot mob	Draws divine attention if disrupted
4	Warden patrol interrogates adventurers mid-quest	Can escalate to lawful combat
5	Argent Blade duel spills into public square	Winner gains +1 Kharma, loser loses sponsor
6	Rift crack births floating eye swarms	Track sound; vulnerable to light
7	FTA drones demand Rift license verification	Bureaucratic hazard; not optional
8	Rift residue mutates nearby flora	Area becomes difficult terrain
9	Choir miracle goes wrong—instant divine storm	Save vs. radiant surge
10	Smuggler deal in Warrens interrupted by Rift echo	Both sides blame PCs
11	Rift creature mimics beloved NPC	Insight DC 15 to notice wrongness
12	Shadow of a god passes overhead	Random magic surges for 1 hour
13	Council riot over relic taxation	PCs can influence or exploit chaos
14	Rift opens beneath Adventurers’ Guild bar	Drink special: “Reality on the Rocks”
15	The Widow’s assassin delivers message via dagger	You bleed the words
16	Rift hound stalking prey across rooftops	Follows until noticed
17	Rift stabilizer malfunction causes time rewind	PCs repeat last turn, memories intact
18	Rift-born bureaucrat appears demanding “paperwork of existence”	Will vanish if document signed correctly
19	Rift collapses into pocket of the Tower itself	New mini-dungeon forms
20	Divine inspection—Thesaurus’ page turns itself	PCs see their own deaths written
DM Note: Reuse this table but change flavor by district. In the Warrens, drones rust. In the Forum, divine storms get televised.

CREATURE TYPES
All creatures in the Undercity share one of three origins:
Type	Description	Examples
Riftborn	Physical manifestations of broken laws of reality	Time Leeches, Gravity Wasps, Echo Hounds
Divine Constructs	Created by gods to enforce faith	Choir Sentinels, Ledger Seraphs
Corrupted Mortals	People reshaped by faith, greed, or exposure	Rift Junkies, Apostles, Fallen Wardens

ENVIRONMENTAL HAZARDS
Rifts twist not just space, but bureaucracy, memory, and logic. Use 1 hazard per session to keep players uneasy.
Hazard	Effect
Rift Pulse	Randomly swaps two PCs’ initiative counts each round.
Faith Storm	Divine lightning targets anyone who lies.
Paperwork Overflow	FTA forms materialize mid-combat; must be signed to end spell effects.
Echo Corridor	Spells cast here repeat 1 round later on random targets.
Glass Rain	Minor slashing damage every turn until shelter found.
DM Note: These hazards can act as encounters by themselves—no monsters required.

DM Note: Perfect mid-tier adventure for scholar or bard characters; each destroyed sentence spawns a prophecy fragment for later.


In the Undercity, faith is weaponized. Every god needs hands, and those hands need plausible deniability. Apostles and cults act as divine enforcers, fixers, and living loopholes.
—?—
WHAT IS AN APOSTLE?
An Apostle is a mortal given direct authority by a god, typically under a binding contract. They manifest divine power but suffer constant degradation—either physical, mental, or moral. Apostles are the gods’ answer to bureaucracy: fast, messy, effective.
Traits of Apostles:
Bear a visible Divine Mark tied to their patron’s symbol or domain.
Can channel limited divine power without formal worship rites.
Often compelled to act in specific moral or narrative patterns.
Rarely live long.
DM Note: Treat Apostles like temporary bosses or tragic rivals. Many were heroes once, twisted by divine bargains.
—?—
COMMON CULTS OF THE UNDERCITY
Cult	Patron	Domain	Goal	Typical Behavior
The Gilded Tongue	The Culinary Council	Hunger, Excess	Spread divine feasts and harvest souls	Lavish parties with hidden altars
The Blooming Silence	Veha	Forgetting, Mercy	Erase painful memories, even entire events	Perform “mercy rituals” for trauma
Ashen Choir	Ashara	Purity through Fire	Burn corruption (and sometimes people)	Street-level zealots
Archivists of the End Page	Thesaurus	Knowledge, Fate	Record every tragedy as sacred text	Collect prophecies, forbid revision
The Coinless Faith	Unknown (possibly dead god)	Poverty, Desperation	Free the city from divine economy	Theft, chaos, sabotage of temples

—?—
SAMPLE APOSTLES
Apostle of Hunger – “The Feastbound” (CR 4)
Medium humanoid (any), chaotic evil
AC 15?HP 70?Speed 30 ft
STR 16?DEX 12?CON 16?WIS 10?CHA 14
Multiattack: 2 claw attacks +5 (1d8+3 slashing).
Divine Ability: Devour Essence — when Feastbound reduces a creature to 0 HP, regains 10 HP and emits aura of hunger (Wis save DC 13 or disadvantage on next attack).
Flavor: Always smiling, always chewing.
Apostle of Flame – “Ash-Touched Crusader” (CR 5)
AC 17?HP 88?Resistances: Fire, radiant
Ability: Purging Blaze — 15 ft cone, Dex save DC 14 (3d8 fire). Removes poison, disease, and subtle heresies.
Tactics: Target “sinners” first, often mistaken in identification.
Apostle of Memory – “The Whisper Archivist” (CR 3)
AC 12?HP 52?Attack: Psychic quill (1d8 psychic + memory theft)
Ability: Erase Recall — once per day, remove one memory (CHA save DC 15).
Motivation: Preserve the story of Thesaurus without spoilers.

—?—
CULT OPERATIONS IN THE CITY
Cults serve as both antagonists and quest engines.
Operating Styles:
Hidden Worship: masked as civic clubs or charities.
Faith-as-Product: selling miracles through guild fronts.
Rift Conversion: creating divine “test zones” by spawning Rifts intentionally.
Proxy Wars: cults fund adventurers to fight rival faiths.
Event Hooks:
A cult’s “purity feast” coincides with the Council’s peace festival.
Apostles demand citywide fasting—while Culinary Council feasts above.
The Coinless Faith hacks donation wards, stealing divine energy.
DM Note: Rotate cults as villains the way weather rotates storms—predictable yet inescapable.
—?—
FAITH CORRUPTION SYSTEM
Use this system to track divine influence on PCs.
Corruption Level	Effect	Example
1	Minor whispers	Random intrusive divine thoughts
2	Physical mark	Eyes glow, divine sigils appear
3	Compulsion	Forced to act according to faith’s principle
4	Possession risk	God manifests partially through PC
5	Ascension or consumption	PC becomes Apostle or divine meal
Reducing Corruption:
Cleansing at neutral shrines (costly)
Performing faith-neutral acts (charity, anonymity)
Divine intervention from a rival god (never free)
—?—
MAJOR CULT EVENT: “THE FEAST OF NAMES”
Every few years, the Culinary Council holds a divine gala where mortals unknowingly attend their own eulogies.
Structure:
Invitations sent to rising heroes.
Banquet with surreal foods—each dish contains a memory.
Mid-meal, the guests realize the feast is them.
Outcomes:
PCs can disrupt it, earning wrath of the Council.
Accepting the feast grants divine power at terrible cost.
Surviving as “unconsumed” makes PCs living myths.
DM Note: Perfect late-game divine horror event.


The Undercity is full of people who matter, even when they pretend not to. Every district, every guild, every Rift has someone pulling strings—or cutting them.
Use this compendium as both a quick-reference index and a story seed generator. Each entry lists faction, demeanor, voice, motive, and how they might connect to your players’ fate.
—?—
MAJOR GUILD LEADERS
Serrik Dhal
Guildmaster of the Iron Fang Consortium
Voice: Confident merchant baritone, too friendly to trust.
Personality: Greedy, pragmatic, oddly paternal to successful adventurers.
Motive: Profit and control of relic trade; wants to monopolize Essence Coin circulation.
Secret: Supplies bodies to the Culinary Council through “accidental” shipments.
Hook: May sponsor the party if they recover valuable Rift salvage.
Lady Cerys Valemont
Commander of the Argent Blades
Voice: Charismatic, slightly theatrical; loves public speeches.
Personality: Courageous but vain; obsessed with legacy.
Motive: Seeks to immortalize herself as the “face” of divine heroism.
Secret: Privately terrified of obscurity; struck a secret deal with Thesaurus to remember her name forever.
Hook: Offers sponsorship in exchange for dramatic heroics.
Captain Havel Korin
Warden of Ash
Voice: Gravel and iron.
Personality: Dutiful, inflexible, yet quietly compassionate toward civilians.
Motive: Maintain order and discipline; purge Rift corruption.
Secret: Suffers recurring dreams of Ashara’s rebellion—may be fragment of her soul.
Hook: Assigns PCs defense missions; could request aid against internal mutiny.
High Apostle Yzura
Head of the Serpent Choir
Voice: Smooth, melodic; never raises volume yet commands silence.
Personality: Controlled, patient, manipulative.
Motive: Extend divine contracts to every mortal; believes true freedom is dangerous.
Secret: Keeps a mirror that records every broken oath; sells memories to Veha.
Hook: May offer divine sponsorship… or attempt to claim PCs’ souls by “clerical error.”
The Widow
Matriarch of the Obsidian Lotus
Voice: Calm and intimate; whispers directly into the ear.
Personality: Patient, fatalistic, and fond of irony.
Motive: Preserve balance by controlling information leaks.
Secret: Knows the true nature of the Secret Council.
Hook: Provides PCs with illegal truths—at a price payable in secrets.
Archivist Eir Velan
Leader of the Guild of Ashen Scrolls
Voice: Scholarly, halting, constantly distracted by unseen words.
Personality: Kind but existentially tired.
Motive: Record all possible endings before the final collapse.
Secret: Already met the PCs in multiple timelines.
Hook: Requests protection of lost tomes, or help transcribing prophecies that change as they’re written.
—?—

Magistrate Salien Vo
Current Arbiter of the High Council
Voice: Precise, clipped, deliberately neutral.
Personality: Honest to a fault, verging on naďve.
Motive: Maintain peace between guilds; keep the Tower Authority from taking direct control.
Secret: Writes secret decrees in invisible ink that only appear during Rifts.
Hook: Could recruit the party as “independent observers” for Council sessions.
Director Myra Kess
Tower Authority Overseer
Voice: Sweet but commanding; weaponized politeness.
Personality: Bureaucratically devout; believes form completion is divine ritual.
Motive: Bring the city under full Tower regulation.
Secret: Partly artificial—half mindware powered by archived god-thought.
Hook: “Invites” PCs for debriefing after any major Rift event.
Agent Liane Voss
FTA Field Investigator
Voice: Curious, conversational; notes everything in a floating tome.
Personality: Observant, witty, deeply empathetic.
Motive: Uncover the truth about divine interference.
Secret: Actually an apostle of Thesaurus; records data as scripture.
Hook: Can act as ally, rival, or uneasy companion—depending on how public the PCs become.

Hook: May pose as talent scout for the Argent Blades.

Motive: Record PC deeds; prevent paradox.
Hook: Appears whenever players rewrite destiny; offers commentary.

The Undercity operates on its own vocabulary — a fusion of divine science, political slang, and cultural shorthand. Use this glossary as both in-game reference and worldbuilding texture.
—?—
SYSTEM & WORLD TERMS
Adventurer:
A legally recognized operative registered under one or more guild banners. Functionally mercenaries, symbolically city saviors, bureaucratically “freelance civic contractors.”
Arbiter:
Rotating judge-mediator of the High Council. Acts as both moderator and scapegoat for policy failures.
Ash Gate:
Primary defensive checkpoint at the city’s outer boundary. Named for the volcanic ash used in early Rift sealing.
Council Tension (CT):
A hidden metric measuring political instability. Rising CT triggers divine scrutiny or state overreach.
Dome:
Massive magical containment structure sealing the Undercity. Filters Riftlight, holds breathable air, and broadcasts divine frequencies.
Essence Coin (EC):
Condensed fragment of monster or divine essence, used as universal currency. Physically minted by the Iron Fang Consortium, metaphysically taxed by the gods.
FTA (The Tower Authority):
The Foundation for Tower Administration—bureaucratic overseer of Rift activity. Claims neutrality, but functions as both regulator and prophet.
Guild Favor:
A relational measure of trust, influence, and debt between PCs and specific guilds. Can be spent like political currency.
High Council:
Six-seat governing body balancing guild interests under divine threat. Known for corruption, theatrics, and “emergency” decrees.
Kharma:
Moral currency of the Undercity; accumulates through deeds, reputation, or divine attention. Used by gods as both energy and entertainment.
Legend Points (LP):
Narrative significance score reflecting how memorable PCs are. Determines fame, divine interference, and story resonance.
Rift:
Tear in local reality caused by the Tower’s pulse. Connects to random timelines, planes, or divine kitchens. Rifts feed monsters and the gods alike.
Rift Event:
Any spontaneous distortion or incursion; scales from mild anomaly to city-wide catastrophe.
Riftlight:
The spectral radiation emitted by open Rifts. Beautiful, dangerous, mildly addictive.
Secret Council:
Mythical divine version of the High Council, composed of the gods behind each guild. May debate mortal fates beneath the city’s surface.
Thesaurus:
Divine Keeper of the Endless Pages. Records every story, edits none, awaits “the perfect ending.”
Tower:
A multidimensional construct piercing the Dome, rumored to connect mortal and divine planes. Houses the raid floors and resets periodically.
Tower Raid (or Floor Raid):
Organized expedition into Tower floors—each one an autonomous realm or moral trial. Failure reshapes the Tower’s architecture.
Tower Pulse:
Regular burst of energy syncing all Rifts across the city. Treated like a natural disaster combined with divine festival.
Undercity:
The urban sprawl surrounding the Tower’s base. Half metropolis, half containment zone.
Wardens of Ash:
Militarized guild maintaining the Dome’s defenses. Followers of Ashara, goddess of purifying fire.

—?—
MECHANICAL METRICS SUMMARY
Metric	Description	Game Function
Kharma	Measures moral weight of actions	Affects divine favor and cult responses
Legend Points (LP)	Tracks fame and story significance	Increases Divine Attention and unlocks story events
Divine Attention	Gauge of how much the gods notice you	Too high = interference; too low = forgotten
Council Tension (CT)	Measures political instability	At CT 8+, Council or gods intervene directly
Guild Favor	Represents alliances and debts	Spent for aid, favors, or political leverage
Rift Stability	Tracks how damaged reality is in a region	Impacts encounter frequency and severity

—?—
SLANG & IN-UNIVERSE PHRASES
“To Get Gilded”:
To sell one’s story to the Culinary Council for fame before death.
“Paper Burn”:
FTA jargon for bureaucratic erasure—removing an incident from official records.
“Riftborn”:
Someone or something born inside a Rift; unstable, sometimes prophetic.
“Towerborne”:
Adventurer who’s ascended a Tower floor and returned alive. Usually missing something intangible.
“Coinblind”:
Addicted to Essence Coin trading or divine gambling.
“Ash-Baptized”:
Term for those who survived Warden initiation rituals.
“Bloomed”:
Forgetting something intentionally under Veha’s blessing.
“Fanged Contract”:
Trade deal or faith bargain that bites back later.
“To Be Written”:
Thesaurus’ euphemism for impending death—meaning “your chapter is almost done.”
—?—
DIVINE CURRENCIES COMPARISON
Currency	Mortal Control	Divine Demand	Volatility
Kharma	Medium	High	Stable
Essence Coin	High	Medium	Market-driven
Legend Points	Low	Very High	Narrative
Faith Energy	Variable	Absolute	Unstable
DM Note: Treat these like competing economies. Excess in one always depletes another.
—?—
CONCEPTUAL MAP – “THE THREE LAYERS OF REALITY”
The Dome (Mortal Plane): Tangible world of markets, politics, and daily life.
The Tower (Liminal Plane): Challenge layer blending physical and metaphysical laws.
The Divine Shelf: Plane of gods, myth, and consumption. Connected through faith, fame, and food.

—?—
DM Summary:
If you can describe it, it exists.
If you can measure it, it changes.
If you can name it, a god is already listening.
—?—

TOWER FLOOR 1: THE MIRRORED WORLD (Level 1)
Theme: Reflection • Duality • Self-Confrontation
Genre: Psychological Fantasy / Light Horror
Tone: Uncanny and introspective — like waking in a dream that knows your secrets.

Overview
The first floor manifests as a fractured reflection of the PCs’ home world — distorted through endless glass. Every building, face, and sound seems familiar but reversed. Rain falls upward. Voices echo backwards. When the party looks into any mirror, their reflections move a half-second too slow.
This world is dying not from invasion, but from confusion: its people no longer know which version of themselves is real.

Environment
Layout: A city built entirely of mirrored surfaces. Streets shimmer with inverted skies. Each PC’s reflection sometimes acts independently, watching them with slight disapproval.
Light: Perpetual twilight. No sun, only ambient glow from mirrored clouds.
Ambient Sound: Echoes of laughter that loop mid-note; every footstep has two shadows.
Smell: Metallic tang, like ozone after a storm.
The “true” exit to Floor 2 lies behind a sealed Cathedral of Reflection, which only opens when each PC resolves a personal fragment reflected in-world — an act of self-recognition, confession, or rejection.

Key NPCs
Mira Veyra – Trapped Mirror Vendor
Reflects Chicago 2024 and the anime convention held there every summer.
Stat Block: Commoner (MM p.345)
Appearance: Young woman in cracked mirror armor, vending fragments of glass showing other realities.
Personality: Nervous but curious. Can sense which world the PCs came from by their reflections.
Hooks:
Will trade safe passage for “true reflections” (the PCs must show vulnerability).
Rewards success with Reflective Trinkets granting +1 to saving throws vs. illusion for 24 hours.
Knows secret “mirror slides” — portals between locations if one speaks their own name backwards.
Secret: Mira is not the original — she is a reflection who forgot that she was created.

Reflected Minor God Agent
Acts like a rival adventurer serving a lesser deity.
Stat Block: Scout (MM p.349)
Motivation: To test mortals for the divine entertainment of the Mirror Court.
Behavior: Non-hostile unless provoked; mimics one PC’s fighting style precisely.
Hook:
Observes and occasionally helps the party in exchange for seeing their “other sides.”
If befriended, hints that the Tower was once built to repair gods, not just worlds.
If defeated, drops a Mirror Shard Sigil — usable once to cast Mirror Image.

Creatures
Mirror Imps
AC: 12?HP: 8?Attack: 1d4 piercing (claws)
Trait: Mimic Action — each round, copy the last attack or spell made by any PC (DC 12 save to resist confusion).
Behavior: Giggle constantly, mockingly repeat PCs’ words backward.
Mirror Slime
AC: 11?HP: 10?Attack: 1d6 acid
Trait: Reflection Split — on death, splits into two 1 HP fragments that each mirror a PC’s expression.
Movement: Slides effortlessly across reflective surfaces.
Tactic: Swarm in hallways, forcing PCs to fight in tight mirrored corridors.

Dynamic Events
Reflection Swap:
When a PC stares too long into their reflection, they must roll a Dex save (DC 12). On failure, their reflection swaps places with them for 1d4 rounds — the duplicate acts with “inverse morality,” subtly sabotaging the team.
The Mirror Storm:
Periodically, shards rain from the sky; any who take cover behind reflections find themselves sheltering under scenes from other worlds. Shards can be collected — 3 create a Reflective Gate allowing teleport within line of sight.
Mira’s Revelation:
At the midpoint, Mira Veyra realizes she’s not real and shatters — revealing a stairway of light leading deeper. PCs can attempt to restore her (Arcana/Insight DC 13) or let her vanish, influencing Floor 5’s future visions.

Environmental Hazards
Fractured Pathways: DC 11 Dex save or fall into a shallow reflection pit (mirror-water surface that pulls downward).
Echo Loops: Rooms repeat endlessly unless a PC speaks something true aloud (Wis save DC 12 to resist psychic disorientation).
Inverted Physics: Jumping feels reversed; fall damage reduced but prone risk doubled.

Player Role Integration
Role	Advantage	Contribution
Champion / Soldier	Rally allies trapped in reflection loops	Draws enemy reflections’ aggro
Scout / Ranger	Navigate distorted streets	Sees movement 1 second ahead
Sage / Scholar	Identifies reality threads	Analyzes divine resonance of mirrors
Healer / Cleric	Restores identity through prayer	Dispels reflection possession
Artificer / Tinker	Creates anchor wards	Stabilizes broken mirror bridges

Optional Feat Reward: “Mirrorheart”
Granted for completing this floor without killing any reflections.
You cannot be surprised by mirror or illusion-based effects.
Once per long rest, you may copy one ability check or saving throw made by another creature you can see (using their roll result).

Resolution
When the party accepts their mirrored selves — through combat, confession, or forgiveness — the Cathedral of Reflection opens, shattering into ascending light. The floor stabilizes briefly, and the city’s people regain individuality.
As the PCs ascend the staircase of glass, the reflections below wave — not in farewell, but in gratitude.

DM Notes
Encourage introspective RP; this floor tests identity, not power.
Perfect intro to the Tower’s meta-theme: “Every failure is a mirror of your world.”
Mira’s survival or destruction should ripple into Floors 2, 5, and 10 as thematic echoes.






TOWER FLOOR 2: PAST REWRITTEN (Level 2)
Theme: History • Regret • Course Correction
Genre: Temporal Tragedy / Heroic Reconstruction
Tone: Somber, cinematic, and looping — a morality puzzle in motion.

Overview
The second floor manifests as a war-torn city moments before its fall. The air hums with déjŕ vu; every face the heroes see insists they’ve already met before.
History is repeating endlessly — each cycle slightly different — and the world itself begs for someone to make the right choice this time.
The party must uncover what went wrong, fix the decisions that doomed this world, and stabilize the timeline before paradox consumes it.

Environment
Setting: Crumbling city center under an amber sky, frozen between bombardment and silence.
Temporal Distortions: Echoes of events loop around the party — a child runs past again and again, never reaching safety.
Time Echo Zones: Areas replaying specific tragedies. Interaction can change the loop temporarily.
Time Mechanics:
Each major decision the players make causes the Timeline Stability Counter to shift:
Stability +1: Correcting or preventing harm.
Stability -1: Interfering selfishly or killing an echo.
At Stability +3, the city solidifies, opening the way to Floor 3.
At Stability -3, time collapses, forcing combat against the paradox itself.

Primary NPCs
Cedric Thane – “Down-on-his-luck Hero”
Stat Block: Veteran (MM p.350)
Gear: Standard longsword, small shield.
Personality: Hesitant, self-doubting; has failed this loop hundreds of times.
Hook: Regains confidence if saved or inspired by PCs.
Development: If restored, joins as NPC ally in Floor 3’s Tower Defense.
Quote: “You don’t understand — we already lost. I just haven’t stopped moving yet.”

Historical NPCs / Minor Heroes
Stat Block: Commoner (MM p.345)
Role: Background actors caught in repeating tragedies (collapsed bridge, burning tower, barricade scene).
Hook: PCs can intervene to stabilize each micro-event, earning +1 Stability.

Creatures & Hazards
Temporal Shadow (CR 1)
AC: 12?HP: 12?Attack: 1d6 psychic.
Traits:
Echo Return: Reappears 1d4 rounds after “death” unless its past self is altered.
Temporal Distortion: On hit, target loses next reaction.
Behavior: Whisper PCs’ choices before they make them.
Past Rift Spawn (CR 1)
AC: 13?HP: 14?Attack: 1d8 slashing or radiant.
Trait: Historic Imprint — reflects conditions of the battle it “remembers.”
If slain where civilians died, it explodes in radiant backlash (2d6, DC 13 Dex).
Environmental Hazards:
Collapsing ruins, unstable timelines, localized déjŕ vu storms (Wis save DC 12 or lose a round repeating a past action).

Key Scenes
The Broken Bridge
A group of refugees runs endlessly across a collapsing bridge. PCs must stabilize supports (Engineer) or shield civilians (Champion/Medic).
Success = +1 Stability.
Failure = permanent time fracture zone (doubles movement cost).
The False Flag
A memory echo of Cedric executing a “traitor.” If PCs investigate, they realize it was misinformation.
Expose truth = +1 Stability.
Ignore = time distortion grows stronger.
The Hour of Flame
The city’s tower burns while citizens pray for salvation. PCs can channel divine energy to “rewrite” the outcome (Arcana or Religion DC 13).
Critical success: Flame turns blue, revealing the path forward.

Player Roles
Role	Rank	Special Power	Description / Mechanics	Notes
Champion / Soldier	Major	Rallying Strike	Once/short rest: attack + grant +1 to ally’s attack/AC for 1 round	Leads temporal defense squads
Scout / Ranger	Lieutenant	Eyes of the Past	Advantage on Perception, Stealth, or Investigation (1/short rest)	Locates stability points
Sage / Scholar	Scholar	Temporal Insight	+2 on Arcana, History, or Investigation once per scenario	Reads echo patterns
Healer / Cleric	Medic	Moment of Grace	Heal 1d8+mod or remove minor status (1/short rest)	Restores echo NPCs
Artificer / Tinker	Engineer	Quick Contraption	Craft barricade or device in 1 round	Crucial for bridge / tower repairs

Optional Feat Reward: “Echoborne”
Prerequisite: Completion of Past Rewritten
You perceive 1 second into the future.
Once per long rest, you may reroll an initiative check or force one enemy to reroll theirs.

Resolution
When Timeline Stability reaches +3, the city freezes, then inhales.
The sun reappears for the first time in ages.
Cedric kneels, sword blazing:
“You’ve changed something. I can feel it. Maybe… we can hold the gate this time.”
He hands the PCs the Warden’s Seal, a relic key to Floor 3.

If Stability reaches -3:
The city folds into itself. Time implodes, forming the Paradox Titan — a monstrous amalgamation of overlapping timelines. Destroying it clears the floor, but Cedric vanishes permanently.

DM Notes:
This floor rewards moral and logical problem-solving over combat.
Encourage players to narrate “how” they fix moments, not just roll for it.
Time echoes can reveal details about PCs’ pasts — especially unresolved failures.
Cedric’s survival dramatically alters dialogue and bonuses on Floor 3.


The heroes awaken at the war council table of The Warden Command, where soldiers chant prayers and hammer metal sigils into armor. Above, a massive rift pulses in the sky — the Shattered Gate — the hole that once doomed this world.
This floor tests leadership, tactical awareness, and endurance. The heroes are not merely adventurers; they are commanders defending the last light of civilization.

Environment
Setting: Fortress-city “Bastion Vale,” perched along a collapsing cliffside.
Mood: Claustrophobic grandeur — like Helm’s Deep by way of divine apocalypse.
Lighting: Blood-orange twilight as Riftlight burns through clouds.
Soundscape: War drums echo across the valley; shouts, horns, and dying prayers fill the air.
Three defensive layers define the battlefield:
Outer Ramparts – lightly fortified; the first to fall.
Inner Courtyard – command post and supply routes.
Sanctum of the Gate – ancient crystal focus sealing the Rift.
The PCs must allocate time and NPCs to strengthen these areas before the siege begins.

Key NPCs
Cedric Thane – Redeemed Hero
Stat Block: Veteran (MM p.350)
Gear: Longsword +1, Shield of Faith
Special Action: Inspire Defenders — 1/round, grants +2 AC or attack to 1 NPC squad for 1 turn.
Hook: If saved in Floor 2, becomes the morale anchor of the defense.
Death Flag: If morale drops below 0, Cedric dies rallying the final stand, inspiring +2 attack rolls for all allies until wave end.

Captain Havel Korin – Warden Commander
Stat Block: Knight (MM p.347)
Gear: Bulwark of Ash — Tower Shield that projects 10-ft-radius Sanctuary once per day.
Personality: Stoic strategist; believes in duty over survival.
Hook: Entrusts PCs with tactical command — “You decide who lives where we cannot.”

NPC Warden Squads
Stat Block: Guard (MM p.347)
Role: Modular defensive units under PC command.
Command Options (choose each round):
Hold Position: +2 AC for 1 turn.
Volley Fire: 1d6 ranged attack per squad.
Reinforce: Move to assist adjacent zone.
Each choice influences the Siege Morale Meter (SMM):
+1 for clever tactics, reinforcement, or saving civilians.
-1 for abandoned positions or heavy losses.
If SMM drops to -3, the Gate begins collapsing; if +3, reinforcements arrive from other floors.

Creatures & Siege Waves
Wave 1 – Rift Horde
4–6 minor Rift Creatures (CR ˝)
AC: 12?HP: 10?Attack: 1d6 slashing.
Tactics: Climb walls, overwhelm in numbers.
Wave 2 – Rift Elites
2–3 Elite Rift Fiends (CR 1–2).
AC: 14?HP: 18?Attack: 1d8+1 magical.
Trait: Summon Spawn (1d4 Riftlings each round).
Wave 3 – The Gatebreaker (Boss)
Huge Aberration, CR 5
AC: 16?HP: 85?Multiattack: Slam (2× 2d10+3).
Trait: Reality Distortion Aura (30 ft) — ranged attacks have disadvantage.
Death Burst: Tears in space release psychic shockwave (4d6 psychic, DC 14 Wis save for half).

Environmental Hazards
Collapsing Ramparts: Dex save DC 12 or take 2d6 bludgeoning.
Magical Surge Zones: Arcana DC 12 or suffer spell misfire (random effect).
Rift Light Exposure: Con save DC 10 each round beyond turn 10; 3 fails = temporary exhaustion.

Player Role Progression
Role	Rank	Special Power	Description / Mechanics	Notes
Champion ? General	Commanding Presence	Once/round, grant +1 AC/+1 attack to adjacent defenders	Inspires allies	
Scout ? Captain	Rapid Flank	Ignore difficult terrain; make ranged attack same turn	Key for counterattacks	
Sage ? Arcane Advisor	Ward of Stability	Create 10-ft zone reducing Rift damage by 1d6 (1/encounter)	Defensive utility	
Healer ? Field Medic	Circle of Protection	AoE heal 1d8+mod + remove one effect (1/encounter)	Keeps squads fighting	
Artificer ? Chief Engineer	Fortification Expert	Reinforce barricades: +2 AC or +2 saves for allies behind cover	Resource control	

Optional Feat Reward: “Warden of the Gate”
You can bolster morale through sheer presence.
When an ally within 30 ft drops to 0 HP, they may immediately make a DC 10 Con save to stay at 1 HP instead.
You can use this ability twice per long rest.

Resolution
If the PCs’ Siege Morale Meter ? 0 when the Gatebreaker dies:
The Gate seals with holy light; Rift energy collapses harmlessly.
Surviving NPCs salute the PCs as heroes.
Cedric stands beside Havel Korin, exhausted but alive:
“For once… we held the line.”
If the SMM < 0:
The Gate implodes, consuming half the fortress.
PCs survive, but the city is gone — replaced by a flickering memory that will haunt them on later floors.
The next floor (The Hall of Fools) begins in the aftermath of divine mourning.

DM Notes
Encourage leadership and delegation; each PC’s choices shape outcomes beyond combat.
Let players assign NPCs or use role abilities as “commands.”
If Cedric survives both Floors 2 and 3, he becomes a semi-immortal “echo hero” — returning in Floor 10 as the embodiment of second chances.

TOWER FLOOR 4: THE HALL OF FOOLS – The Comedic / Tragic Court (Level 4)
Theme: Vanity • Judgment • Divine Absurdity
Genre: Social Farce / Political Theater / Divine Satire
Tone: Whimsical yet dangerous — a mask of comedy stretched over divine cruelty.

Overview
The fourth floor is a divine stage play gone wrong — a living satire of nobility, theater, and faith.
Here, minor gods and archetypal nobles perform endless court sessions where nothing is resolved, and everyone applauds failure as genius.
The heroes arrive uninvited during the Eternal Banquet of Reflection, where mortals are cast as caricatures of themselves for the gods’ amusement. The challenge is not to fight, but to survive the performance — and perhaps rewrite the script.

Environment
Setting: A grand mirrored ballroom that reforms itself every hour.
Atmosphere: Perfumed laughter, chandeliers of frozen time, walls lined with portraits that whisper commentary.
Lighting: Gold-and-lavender, warm but unsettling — the light itself watches.
Sound: Harpsichord and divine laughter.
Hazard: Reality reshapes to maintain the play; if a PC “breaks character,” the floor punishes them.

Structure of Play (DM Framework)
Act I – Entrance of the Fools:
PCs are instantly dressed in gaudy costumes matching their perceived “roles.”
They must participate in polite small talk with divine nobles to avoid suspicion.
Act II – The Misunderstanding:
A scandal breaks out — a missing crown, a poisoned dessert, or an insulted noble (roll 1d6 or choose).
The PCs must use skill checks and creativity to diffuse or redirect chaos.
Act III – The Trial of Wit:
A series of social contests or riddles decide “justice.”
Each round escalates divine attention until the Baron himself appears.
Act IV – The Baron’s Wrath:
If players mishandle etiquette or offend divinity, combat begins — a stylized duel of pride and irony.

Major NPCs
Baron Aristrok, Lord of Etiquette
Stat Block: Mage (MM p.347) with Charisma 18, Intelligence 20.
Appearance: Overdressed, powdered minor god with glowing monocle and an ever-hovering fan.
Abilities:
Scornful Command (Recharge 5–6) — Forces one PC to waste their next turn bowing or apologizing (Wis save DC 15).
Wealth Drain — Temporarily removes 1d4 Kharma from careless PCs.
Mocking Verse — When struck, recites poetry that inflicts psychic damage (1d8).
Goal: Maintain perfect absurdity; punishes anyone who acts earnestly.
Secret: He was once mortal — a playwright executed for heresy. His divine punishment was immortality in satire.

The Minister of Ceremonies
Stat Block: Noble (MM p.348)
Ability: Grand Gesture — Once per encounter, grants +2 to Persuasion or Intimidation checks.
Hook: Might help PCs if they flatter him with new “dramatic material.”
Court Jester “Bells”
Stat Block: Bandit Captain (MM p.344), but deals nonlethal “slapstick” damage.
Personality: Chaotic neutral, hyperaware he’s in a play.
Quote: “The joke is always funny until the laughter stops echoing.”
Hook: Offers secret help — if PCs promise to “make the next act worth watching.”

Court Roles (Random or Assigned)
Role	Outfit / Visual	Equipment	Special Power	Use Case
Court Jester	Multicolored tunic, bells	Joke wand (1d4, minor smoke)	Prankster’s Timing — once per encounter, force NPC failure	Comic relief or chaos manipulation
Herald / Announcer	Tabard, feathered hat	Speaking trumpet	Echo of Fame — repeat NPC’s statement to sway crowd (+2 Insight)	Speech control, rumor management
Chamber Scholar	Long robes, spectacles	Ledger &ink	Bureaucratic Overload — delay any decree for 1 round	Puzzle &paperwork control
Royal Guard	Ornate armor, overlong pike	Small shield	Rigid Posture — advantage on Perception checks	Protects others, physical interjections
Minister of Ceremonies	Flowing coat, quill	Scrolls of divine law	Grand Gesture — impress/intimidate nobles (+2 Kharma)	Negotiation &performance
Chef / Culinary Hero	Apron, flamboyant hat	Magical ladle (1d4 fire)	Dish of Destiny — prepare miracle meal, unpredictable	Ritual chaos &divine favor gambit
Each role grants temporary narrative abilities — magical or social — but vanishes upon leaving the floor.

Court Scenarios (Choose or Randomize)
The Missing Crown – PCs must find the Baron’s lost crown before divine inspection.
Success: Gain +1 Kharma, earn Baron’s applause.
Failure: Duel of etiquette triggers.
Poisoned Dessert – Magical pastries cause gods to hallucinate or rage.
Success: Reveal culprit (Insight DC 13) or purify desserts (Religion DC 14).
Failure: 1d4 gods begin reciting accusations; social combat ensues.
Rumor Mill – False gossip destabilizes the court.
Success: Redirect rumors (Deception DC 13) to rival noble.
Failure: PCs become new scandal focus.
Duel of Etiquette – Combat-as-conversation.
Uses Charisma checks as “attacks.”
First to lose 3 “reputation points” is humiliated or magically silenced.

Environmental Hazards
Laughing Portraits: Psychic backlash if players refuse to laugh (Wis save DC 13).
Mimicry Wine: Drinking too much forces PCs to imitate others involuntarily.
Temporal Curtains: Passing through the wrong curtain resets an NPC’s memory of the scene.

Player Roles & Feat Integration
Role	Function
Champion / Soldier	Protects allies during etiquette duels; can “tank” social backlash.
Scout / Ranger	Detects shifting alliances; reads body language for insight.
Sage / Scholar	Decodes divine double-speak; prevents logical paradoxes.
Healer / Cleric	Restores composure; can remove embarrassment or confusion.
Artificer / Tinker	Manipulates props, creates diversions, rigs comedic disasters.

Optional Feat Reward: “Stageborne”
Prerequisite: Completion of The Hall of Fools without starting combat.
You gain advantage on all Deception and Performance checks when under observation.
Once per long rest, you may deliver a one-liner or speech that counts as the Calm Emotions spell.

Resolution
If the PCs play along while subtly subverting the court, they earn the Baron’s twisted admiration.
He bows — once, mockingly — and the court freezes into a living mural.
A portal of rippling velvet opens where the throne once stood.
As they pass through, the Baron’s voice follows:
“Well performed, my players. Do tell me how the next tragedy ends.”
If the PCs defy the script or fight, they must duel Baron Aristrok directly.
Upon victory, the stage collapses, revealing the golden staircase to the Fifth Floor beneath the shattered ballroom.

DM Notes
Encourage humor and creativity.
Reward clever dialogue and narrative wit over dice rolls.
The Hall of Fools serves as a palette cleanser after the previous war floor — a test of social agility rather than strength.
Surviving it without violence establishes the PCs’ first true divine reputation within the Tower.

TOWER FLOOR 5 – THE ORACLE’S GRAVE (Level 5)
Theme: Prophecy • Fate Fatigue • Cyclical Doom
Genre: Mystical Horror / Narrative Puzzle
Tone: Haunting and philosophical — where foresight becomes a curse.

Overview
A desert world made of glass and bones where the sun never moves.
Each grain of sand remembers a possible future.
The Oracles here sealed themselves in crystal tombs, driven mad by knowing every tomorrow that could be.
The heroes must decide: destroy prophecy, preserve it, or become part of it.

Environment
Terrain: Desert plain of mirrored dunes; crystalline mausoleums half-buried in the sand.
Light: Perpetual amber dusk; shadows crawl the wrong direction.
Sound: Constant whispering—sometimes echoing the PCs’ voices before they speak.
Hazards: After-images of the party walk parallel paths; touching one inflicts psychic shock.
Unique Mechanic – Foresight Fatigue
Each character begins with 1 Foresight Token.
Spend a token ? gain advantage on any roll that represents prediction, analysis, or defense.
Each token spent adds 1 Fatigue point.
At 3 Fatigue points, the character takes 1d4 psychic damage at the start of each turn until they take a Short Rest.
A PC can clear 1 Fatigue by willingly accepting blindness for 1 minute (no save).

NPCs
Eila the Last Seer
Medium Humanoid (any race), Neutral Good
AC 13, HP 40, Speed 30 ft
STR 8, DEX 10, CON 12, INT 16, WIS 18, CHA 14
Saves: WIS +6, INT +5?Skills: Insight +6, Arcana +5, Persuasion +4
Abilities:
Prophecy Loop. Eila always acts as if under foresight (advantage on initiative, attacks against her have disadvantage).
Foretell Doom (1/round). Force a creature within 60 ft to reroll a successful saving throw.
Goal: Beg for the Mirror of Tomorrows to be destroyed so she can finally rest.
Secret: Eila’s body is a reflection; her real form is one of the mummified seers entombed below.

The Keeper of the First Prediction (CR 5 Boss)
Huge Aberration, Lawful Neutral
AC 15, HP 95?Speed 40 ft
Multiattack. Two Hands of Certainty (+6 to hit, reach 10 ft, 2d10+3 force).
Words of Inevitability (Recharge 5–6). Each creature of its choice within 30 ft makes a DC 14 Wis save or loses its next action.
Lair Action (Init 20). The Keeper acts twice this round by skipping ahead in time.
Weakness. If no creature takes any action on a round, the Keeper loses initiative and has disadvantage for 1d4 turns.

Encounters and Events
The Desert of Futures – PCs see footprints ahead of themselves; every choice they make rewrites them.
The Mirror of Tomorrows – Shows older versions of each PC; destroying it frees Eila, preserving it grants prophetic insight but adds Fatigue.
The Keeper’s Lament – Final trial where doing nothing is sometimes the only winning move.

Environmental Hazards
Glass Storms: 2d6 slashing, Dex save DC 13 half, fail = blinded 1d4 rounds.
Echo Tombs: Disturbing one creates 1–2 Echo Wraiths (use Specter stats).
Sands of Prediction: Footprints form sentences of future failure; reading them inflicts 1d6 psychic damage (Wis save DC 12).
