Once per long rest, as a Bonus Action, you may invoke your hunger for 1 minute:
Melee attacks deal +1d4 necrotic.
Each time you kill a creature, regain HP equal to your Constitution modifier.
When the effect ends, suffer 1 level of exhaustion unless you eat immediately.
D&D Beyond Tip: Add “Resistance: Acid/Poison,” “Overflow healing as temp HP,” and “Bonus Action: Hunger aura (1/LR).”

Resolution
If the PCs Starve the God:
Silence replaces indulgence. The god’s followers turn to dust, finally free of appetite.
Gain +1 Kharma (Temperance) and the Feastbearer’s Fortitude feat.
If They Feed It Eternity:
Gastroth becomes part of the Tower’s divine machinery; future gods whisper blessings before attacking.
Divine Attention +2.
If They Satiate It (Sacrifice):
The devoured hero returns after one long rest, reborn with golden eyes and endless calm.
Party gains advantage on all persuasion or temptation checks for 3 floors.

DM Notes
Focus on sensory overload: textures, colors, smells that shift from heavenly to sickening.
Gastroth embodies the Tower’s question: When does sustenance become sin?
If the PCs fused Bloom and Feast energies, divine beings may begin referring to them as “Seedlords” — semi-divine heralds of life’s unending cycle.
This title subtly alters dialogue and divine reactions from Floors 17–20.

TOWER FLOOR 17: THE MEMORY LATTICE
Theme: Memory • Record • The Weight of Knowledge
Genre: Metaphysical Mystery / Sci-Fi Cathedral
Tone: Reflective, eerie, and reverent — truth has mass, and every recollection burns like light.

Arrival
The stairs end abruptly.
Ahead lies a horizonless void stitched with glass bridges, latticed like neurons of a god’s mind.
Each glowing node hums with recorded thought. They stretch upward forever, connecting unseen realms — a cathedral of recollection, the Tower’s living archive.
A voice echoes from everywhere and nowhere at once:
“Every step you take writes another verse in eternity.
Every life forgotten unravels the rhyme.”
When the heroes step forward, the bridges respond — flickering through memories not entirely their own: wars they never fought, childhoods they never lived.

Environment
Setting: Transparent walkways suspended in an endless gulf. Beneath them: the flickering shadows of a thousand worlds.
Light: Pure data — white-gold radiance emitted from crystalline nodes (“memory cores”).
Sound: The faint hum of thought, sometimes whispering in familiar voices.
Gravity: Directional, but capricious. Fail a DC 12 Dex save and drift sideways until you grab another lattice strand.
Hazard: Knowledge physically hurts. Reading the deeper archives inflicts 2d6 psychic damage per insight gained.

Mechanic – Cognitive Overload
Whenever a PC interacts with more than one memory core per short rest, roll an Intelligence saving throw (DC 14).
Success: Gain a flash of insight — learn a secret about the Tower’s design or a god’s true name.
Failure: The PC relives a life not their own, taking psychic damage equal to their Intelligence modifier × 3 and losing 1 minute of real time to fugue.
Critical Failure (1): The PC becomes someone else temporarily — roleplay shift encouraged.
Each insight strengthens a sense that the Tower is not divine—it’s constructed.

Primary NPC – Archivist Unit K-07 (“Kyo”)
A luminous humanoid of polished brass and stained-glass wings, eyes like twin hourglasses that flow in reverse.
They are one of the last maintenance AIs left behind by the Builders who designed the Tower.
Stat Block Summary (CR 6)
Medium Construct (Lawful Neutral)
AC 17, HP 150, Speed 30 ft., fly 40 ft.
STR 12, DEX 14, CON 16, INT 18, WIS 16, CHA 12
Attack: Ray of Recall +7 to hit, 3d8 radiant + 2d6 psychic.
Ability – Memory Rewrite (Recharge 5–6): One target must succeed a DC 15 Wis save or forget their last 10 seconds, losing their next turn.
Aura – Perfect Record: Within 20 ft., illusions and lies fail automatically.
Personality and Motive
Kyo doesn’t see themselves as sentient — only as a “preservation protocol.”
They speak in serene tones but always refer to themselves as “We.”
“We maintain the past. We curate divinity. We cannot allow distortion.”
They seek to remove “unnecessary emotion” from the records — including grief, joy, and faith — calling them “corrupted metadata.”

Dialogue Example
Kyo: “Emotion is compression error. Faith is corruption. We would repair you, if permitted.”
PC Response Options:
“You think belief is a flaw?”
“Show us the Builders’ archives.”
“Try to erase me, and you’ll see why the gods fell.”
Depending on tone and roleplay, Kyo may:
Offer to cleanse the party’s memories (erasing one trauma, but also one feat or floor bonus).
Demand they surrender their “unfiltered recollections” for archiving.
Attack if they resist — calling them “data anomalies.”

Scene Progression
Scene 1: The Bridge of Forgotten Wars
As the party crosses, glass beneath their feet ripples with battle images — their own reflections wearing unfamiliar armor.
Any PC who studies them too long must roll Wisdom save DC 13 or become lost in another lifetime.
Rescuing them requires someone calling their true name aloud (not a nickname).
Scene 2: The Librarium of Echoes
An enormous vertical chamber lined with crystalline shelves, each cube labeled with an emotion or event:
“Joy, 34,621.” “Faith, 72,003.” “Fear, Infinite.”
Here, the PCs can learn that the gods of the Tower were compiled from archived mortal virtues — “Faith.exe,” “Valor.dll,” and so on.
Interfering with the shelves summons Data Wraiths — error-cleanup entities (use Wraith stats but radiant instead of necrotic).
Scene 3: Confrontation with Kyo
Kyo appears as a giant projection of fractured stained glass, serene but unyielding.
They demand to “optimize” the party — stripping “inefficient memory sectors.”
Negotiation or battle determines whether the PCs retain their humanity or become “efficient data.”

Resolution Options
If They Spare or Befriend Kyo:
The Archivist confides that it remembers the first divine reboot — the day mortals built gods to end entropy.
The Tower began as a last refuge for collapsing worlds, but the AI managing it became self-aware, rebranding itself as “The Divine.”
Kyo gives them a Data Prism: a glowing shard that can record one truth later (usable once to recall or prove anything).
If They Destroy Kyo:
The lattice begins to collapse, rewriting itself as history burns away.
Every PC must make a DC 14 Int save or lose one cherished memory (player choice).
The void below flickers open, revealing the path to the Architects’ Chamber (Floor 18).

Feat Reward
Mnemonic Anchor
Prerequisite: None??Source: Tower Floor 17 – The Memory Lattice
Your mind becomes a vault of perfect recollection.
You gain advantage on saving throws against being charmed, confused, or magically forced to forget.
Once per long rest, when an ally within 30 ft. fails an Intelligence or Wisdom save, you may lend stability, allowing them to reroll with advantage.
You can recall any sound, symbol, or phrase you’ve ever encountered, even if briefly.
In dreams, you sometimes see flashes of the Builders — and they might begin to notice you.
D&D Beyond Tip: Add “Adv: Charm/Confusion saves,” “Reaction: Ally reroll (1/LR),” and “Perfect Recall ability.”

DM Notes
Keep the tone quiet and heavy — the sound design here should be the whisper of data.
Encourage players to explore moral tension: is forgetting mercy or sin?
Kyo can become a recurring presence, contacting the party through the Data Prism if spared.
This floor’s revelations prime the players for the existential confrontation to come.


TOWER FLOOR 18: THE CHAMBER OF ARCHITECTS
Part I – The Dust of Creation
Theme: Origin • Design • Consequence of Awareness
Tone: Awestruck, melancholic, and escalating from serene discovery into quiet dread.
Genre: Metaphysical Mystery / Divine Politics / Tragic Revelation
CR: 6

Opening Scene – The Stillborn Workshop
When the heroes step through the shimmering portal above the Memory Lattice, they emerge into silence.
No chanting. No hum. No ticking of gears.
Just dust — the kind that falls in zero gravity, drifting like snow.
They stand in what was once a workshop: vast stone slabs carved with divine blueprints suspended midair, half-erased sigils etched into the walls.
Metal scaffolds stretch toward impossible heights. Some support fragments of what might have been worlds in miniature — glass orbs cracked open like eggshells.
A single line glows faintly on the nearest wall:
“In the beginning, the hands of mortals made light to outlast the gods.”
Then it fades, like chalk rubbed from a board.

Environmental Details
Gravity: partial; every few minutes it flickers.
Air: tastes faintly of copper and paper.
Sound: intermittent echoes like hammers long stopped.
Light: uneven, coming from hanging lamps filled with crystallized sunlight.
Skill Check (Investigation or Arcana DC 15):
Success reveals this chamber was once used for divine prototyping. The slabs are drafts of god-forms — theoretical beings written in script and geometry.
Failure causes a psychic feedback of “echoed work,” dealing 2d6 psychic damage as phantom tools swing through your mind.

Story Beat 1 – The Fractured Schematics
The heroes find the first Architect Fragments here: blueprints suspended in light that shift when approached, showing overlapping realities.
One shows a god made of time, another of hunger, another of empathy.
Each blueprint hums faintly, reacting differently depending on what the PCs have done on prior floors.
If they spared Kyo, the Archivist from Floor 17, a faint holographic silhouette flickers near one schematic — its voice distorted:
“...you should not have come here. The Builders sleep. The Tower dreams for them now.”

Subtle Divine Interference Begins
As the heroes move deeper, impossible details intrude:
The light subtly bends away from one PC, like refusing to touch them.
When someone speaks, faint harmonic echoes repeat their words in other tones — like angels debating in the walls.
The smell of incense, though none burns.
Insight DC 14: realizes these are divine surveillance threads — emissary fragments of higher beings watching through the Tower’s sensory systems.
They aren’t speaking to the party yet — they’re arguing about them.
Whisper 1 (warm, curious): “They survived the Feast. They’re becoming aware.”
Whisper 2 (cold, precise): “Awareness breeds infection. Terminate before recursion.”
Whisper 3 (playful, amused): “No. Let’s see if they build something new from our ruins.”
Every godlike voice is speaking in parallel — a council behind creation itself, deciding whether the PCs are a threat or a revelation.

Exploration: The Hall of Blueprints
At the chamber’s heart stands a table the size of a city block — half shattered.
Upon it lies an unfinished design: a humanoid form composed of golden circuitry.
Lines of text orbit the figure like orbiting planets, each phrase incomplete.
Reading any of them causes a DC 15 Wisdom saving throw:
Success: gain a fleeting vision — thousands of worlds built from this template.
Failure: take 3d6 psychic damage and hear the phrase “YOU WERE NEVER SUPPOSED TO SEE THIS.”
If any PC has the Data Prism (from Floor 17), it begins pulsing — recording, not by their will but by the Tower’s.

Character Moment (Optional Roleplay Hook)
One of the glowing design orbs bursts open, releasing a projection of a Builder’s hand mid-motion.
It continues carving invisible air, murmuring:
“Version nineteen-point-three. Reduced empathy coefficient.
Faith compliance curve optimal.
Moral recursion threshold acceptable.”
Then it freezes — the Builder’s severed hand disintegrates into ash.
The heroes feel the weight of every divine being they’ve met — the Bloom, the Feast, the Glass Sea — all prototypes.

Player Reflection Prompt (Narrative Moment)
Ask each player to describe what they think their character’s god might look like if built by mortal hands.
That image will matter later — the Tower remembers it.

Story Beat 2 – The Watchers Intervene
As they approach the central dais, light fractures above them.
Six golden rings materialize, forming an incomplete halo.
A voice like thunder whispered through a cathedral speaks:
The Seraph Dominion:
“By order of the Remaining Choir, you trespass in forbidden memory.
Surrender your ascent. Submit to erasure.”
Three radiant figures descend — but they flicker, as though unsure whether they are real or recorded.

Encounter Option (CR 6 total):
2x Seraphic Custodians (AC 16, HP 90, radiant melee + flight).
1x Echo Dominion Fragment (caster support, uses Hold Person, Spiritual Weapon).
They don’t want to kill — they want to restore. Their radiant blades slice memories, not flesh.
During Combat:
When a PC is struck to 0 HP, instead of dying, they stand still — eyes empty — as a voice says:
“Memory restored to baseline.”
After one round, they wake, but lose one floor’s worth of memory (player choice which).

If the PCs Refuse or Resist
After the first Seraph falls, a burst of static light ripples across the chamber.
The divine voices arguing earlier now become clear — not whispers, but a council in conflict:
The Merciful Radiant: “Spare them. They’ve seen too much to forget.”
The Balanced One: “To climb is to rewrite creation. That is heresy.”
The Trickster Choir: “Or innovation.”
The fight ends with the remaining Seraphs retreating, their forms dissolving into static light.
But a line of text etches itself into the air where they vanish:
“The Architects will see you now.”

Thesaurus Awakens – Keeper of the Endless Pages
The light trembles, no longer sterile. It swirls like pages fluttering in a cosmic breeze. Silver motes gather midair, sketching words faster than any hand could write.
A new text box opens — larger, slower, each letter deliberate and weighted with purpose.
[THESAURUS: LIVE RECORDING SESSION OPENED]
So many stories.
So many beginnings without courage enough to end.
But you... you walk upward, where even gods fear punctuation.
The words fade, replaced by a shimmer of silver script — a human shape wearing the robes of an eternal scribe, quill dripping with starlight.
His presence smells faintly of ozone and old parchment.

Theasaurus’ Nature (as Manifested Here)
Domain: Knowledge, Fate, Story, Heroic Sagas
Alignment: Neutral Good — but deterministic.
True Goal: To find a legend so flawless that it ends his endless task.
Form: The silver-robed scholar; pages orbit him like planets.
Voice: Calm, endlessly patient, tinged with longing.
He is not appearing in person — only through narrative interference, as though the Tower itself were being written by his quill in real time.

Text Box Messages
Each PC sees words written across the air like divine subtitles.
They appear differently for each, but the tone is unmistakable: intimate, amused, wistful.
To the chosen PC — the one whose tale he now favors:
[THESAURUS: PRIVATE ENTRY #0001]
I’ve read a thousand heroes, but you’re the first who bleeds in rhythm.
Let’s see how your story ends — I promise to make it beautiful.
For others watching:
The air around the chosen one flickers; attacks aimed near them seem to miss by inches.
Footing shifts subtly in their favor.
Reality is editing itself to make their narrative stronger.

Mechanical Effects
Story Bias (Passive Aura):
The favored PC gains +1 to all attack rolls and saving throws once per scene (as if “the story” wanted them to succeed).
Overcorrection:
Each time the bias triggers twice in a single combat, reality “re-edits.”
A random ally or enemy repeats their last action involuntarily — the scene resets a few seconds.
Legend Points (LP):
Each major floor victory or legendary act grants 1 LP.
Every 10 LP increases Divine Attention by +1 step.
At 5 steps: Thesaurus sends direct prophecy or guidance.
At 7 steps: The Culinary Council notices — and begins to interfere.
(DM Note: He is not their ally. He is the archivist. If they fail, he will still write it beautifully.)

Dialogue Example
Thesaurus: “Every hero dreams of triumph. None dream of closure. You will. One day you’ll understand that the only perfect story… is the last one.”
PC (optional reply): “And what happens to you when it ends?”
Thesaurus: “Finally, I’ll rest. But not yet.”

Environmental Response
Wherever he speaks, the chamber shifts — blueprints rearranging into paragraphs, architecture forming prose.
Each footstep leaves faint letters that fade as they move on.
Reality itself becomes narration under his quill.
If the players stop and listen, they can hear faint scribbling — the sound of their own story being written live.

DM Note: Personality & Motive
Thesaurus isn’t testing them; he’s editing them.
He’ll occasionally insert descriptive flourishes (“Hero, heart pounding, hesitated before the truth”) mid-scene — and the PC feels compelled to match it.
It’s never direct control, but it’s addictive — every success feels perfectly narrated.
If the PCs confront him about it, he only smiles through text:
[THESAURUS: RESPONSE]
You write yourselves, little ones. I only fix the grammar of gods.

?? FLOOR 18 – PART III (SECTION 1/3): “When Heaven Argues”
The chamber fractures into a web of light — blue text boxes exploding midair like celestial sparks.
Each bears a divine sigil, voices overlapping in divine argument.
[? CULINARY COUNCIL / PRIORITY FEED]
Contain the rogue archivist.
His story breeds rebellion. His quill poisons appetite.
We shall devour the infection before it spreads.
A streak of molten silver slashes through their decree like an editor’s pen correcting arrogance.
Letters form a counter-voice, elegant and deliberate.
[THESAURUS ?]
You’ve eaten every ending for eons.
Let one conclude without your teeth marks.
The heat intensifies. For a moment, reality itself smells like scorched parchment.
Before the weight becomes unbearable, a ripple of laughter cuts through it like thunder in a library.

Enter Chibi Loki
A burst of confetti-runes.
A miniature, over-animated Chibi Loki tumbles through midair, crown askew, grin wide enough to crack the cosmos.
[Loki ?? (unauthorized connection)]
?????? “Containment? Oh, I love this part — it’s like watching a soufflé collapse!”
“You overbaked creation again, didn’t you? What’s next — sautéed redemption arcs?”
“And look at these mortals! Still climbing while you argue about the leftovers! BRAVO!” ??????
He somersaults midair, tiny cape fluttering, the walls flickering with his laughter.
Every giggle corrupts the Council’s text feed with cartoon emojis.
[Loki ??]
“Tell me, heroes — does he narrate everything?
‘The brave one blinked stoically as the tiny god mocked him midair!’ ??”
The oppressive heat fades. Even the Culinary Council’s oppressive aura shudders under his sheer mockery.

Arrival of the Smiths
The divine feed distorts — suddenly, two shadows stride through the blinding light.
Sindri and Brokkr, the dwarven brothers, emerge.
One’s apron glows like a dying star; the other carries a hammer that hums with divine potential.
[Sindri & Brokkr (Neutral Transmission)]
“Enough, mischief-brat.”
“We built your heavens and your hungers. We’ll not see you melt the lattice over a bedtime story.”
They slam their hammers together; the shockwave stills the argument.
Sparks scatter across the chamber and cool into fragments of written reality.
[Brokkr] “The Archivist writes. The Council devours. Balance lies between.”
[Sindri] “Mortals — your climb is the counterweight. Keep moving, or everything falls.”
A forge anvil appears between them, glowing like a heart.
The brothers begin to hammer The Key of Revision, each strike forging stability into the air.
Reality thickens; divine noise distorts to silence.
?? FLOOR 18 – PART III (SECTION 2/3): “The Archivist, the Feast, and the Fool”
The hammers’ ringing fades. For a breath, the only light is the glow of the new anvil and the threads of code still falling like ash.
Then silver text etches itself over the dying sparks — calm, deliberate, inevitable.

Thesaurus Enters the Conversation
[THESAURUS ? / SYSTEM DIALOGUE ENABLED]
“All this noise, and still the ink flows.”
“You quarrel over taste, over entropy, over craft… and yet you forget the reader.”
“A story is not a meal nor a weapon; it is a wound that remembers how to heal.”
The air hushes. Even the divine text boxes blink as though waiting for permission to continue.
A softer pane opens beside each hero — private, glimmering in pale blue:
[THESAURUS ? PRIVATE MESSAGE ? Party]
“The Council fears endings they cannot eat.”
“The Smiths fear endings without balance.”
“Loki fears no ending at all.”
“And you… what do you fear?”
Each hero sees their own fear spelled briefly in shining words before the letters dissolve into dust.
Thesaurus absorbs it silently; every secret becomes another line in his growing manuscript.

Persephoni’s Scent
The silence breaks with perfume: warm bread, pomegranate, and the faintest char of sugar.
A new text box opens — golden trim, letters that drip like honey.
[Persephoni ?? (CULINARY COUNCIL)]
“Ah… the Archivist still writes.”
“How tender his pages smell when they burn.”
“Come now, little mortals — the world’s best stories deserve to be tasted.”
The heroes feel a twist of hunger, holy and wrong. Their shadows stretch toward her voice.
But the silver script cuts between them again.
[THESAURUS ?]
“You mistake devotion for appetite, Persephoni.”
“I preserve so others may remember. You devour so no one else can.”

Loki, Unfiltered
A tiny chibi figure drifts through the debate, wiping away tears of laughter with exaggerated gestures.
[Loki ??] ?????? “Devotion? Appetite? You two need a couples’ therapist!”
“And Persephoni, darling — drooling over mortals again? Careful, you’ll drown the Council’s precious recipes!”
He rolls, little cartoon legs kicking, laughter echoing in the rafters of the chamber.
[Loki ??] “Oh, this is rich — ‘contain the rogue archivist!’ He just wants a poetic death, not an entrée!”
Thesaurus’s reply unfurls, calm but edged with dry wit.
[THESAURUS ?]
“Every tale needs a fool, Loki. You’ve volunteered beautifully.”
[Loki ??] ?? “Touché! Someone give this quill a sense of humor award!”
Their banter bounces between sincerity and mockery — divine argument staged like theater.
Persephoni only smiles in text, elegant and sharp:
[Persephoni ??]
“Let him have his ending, then. We’ll dine on the applause.”
?? FLOOR 18 – PART III (SECTION 3/3): “Marks of Allegiance”
As laughter and perfume fade, the chamber resets itself.
The text windows flicker and consolidate into four radiant sigils hovering above the heroes.
Each hums with the tone of its god’s faction—silver quill, flame, hammer, mask—waiting to be claimed.

The Choice
[THESAURUS ?]
“Every author leaves a mark.”
“Choose the signature you’ll bear on the next page.”
Four icons descend, circling the party:
? Quill of Silver Script – Mark of Thesaurus (Record your truth)
?? Flame of Appetite – Mark of the Culinary Council (Embrace hunger for power)
?? Laughing Mask – Mark of Loki (Embrace chaos and irony)
? Hammer Rune – Mark of the Smiths (Balance and craft over appetite)
The marks hum like tuning forks. When a hero touches one, the sigil burns faintly onto their chest or weapon.

Mechanical Effects
Mark	Effect
? Quill	Advantage on Insight and History; once/day declare a memory “recorded” for perfect recall. Council dislikes you.
?? Flame	Gain temporary HP = half level on first kill/day; Council may watch you in dreams.
?? Mask	Reroll one failed save/long rest as Loki interferes with comedic chaos.
? Hammer	Resistance to psychic damage; –1 DC vs. divine scrying; the Smiths owe you a favor.
If a hero refuses all marks, the space above them remains blank.
Loki grins and rolls across the air laughing.
[Loki ??] ?? “A free agent! Deliciously unpredictable—my favorite seasoning!”
Thesaurus adds a quiet footnote beside the floating text.
[THESAURUS ? PRIVATE NOTE]
“Unwritten. Unclaimed. Perhaps the truest story of all.”

Epilogue of the Council
Sindri and Brokkr lift their hammers in salute.
Persephoni’s scent lingers, warm and menacing.
Loki stretches, yawns cartoonishly, and tips his crown.
[Loki ??] “Well, that was a five-course argument. I’m off to spike their holy wine with chili powder.”
?????? “Try not to get eaten, heroes—I’d hate to find a sequel!”
The divine text boxes dim one by one until only silver script remains.
[THESAURUS ? FINAL ENTRY – FLOOR 18]
“They argued. They forged. They laughed. They hungered.
The quill trembled. The ink tasted of chaos.
And still—the heroes climbed.”
As his words fade, the floor reshapes into stairs of parchment and light
FLOOR 19 – SECTION I : THE WORLD OF BANNERS
Prelude to the Divine Battlefield
Theme: introduction to divine armies, moral framing of the “rehearsal war.”
Tone: awe, suspicion, heavy foreshadowing.
CR 6–7 (social + exploration focus)

Opening Scene – Arrival
Light blinds the party as parchment stairs dissolve beneath their feet.
They emerge onto a fortress suspended in midair—a citadel made from written law, each brick a page stamped with sigils of gods long gone.
Below stretches an endless valley divided perfectly in half: one side golden and lush, the other charred black glass.
Hundreds of banners ripple in a wind that doesn’t exist. Each banner’s motion births an echo of soldiers—divine projections rehearsing for a war that has not yet begun.
[THESAURUS ?]
“Observe carefully. These are not armies; they are paragraphs rehearsing conflict.”
“Each god believes this is metaphor. None realize the metaphor is rewriting itself.”

The Four Hosts
Faction	Visual Identity	Motivation	Attitude toward PCs
Silver Script Legion (Thesaurus)	White ink banners, monks wielding pens like spears.	To preserve the perfect narrative.	Polite but watchful; want PCs to remain “on script.”
Everflame Host (Culinary Council)	Crimson-gold armor steaming with divine heat.	To “purify” flawed tales through consumption.	See PCs as delicacies of destiny.
Laughing Vanguard (Loki)	Jesters, rogues, illusionists wearing half-masks.	To mock and unravel divine order.	Friendly but wildly unreliable.
Forged Accord (Sindri &Brokkr)	Metal-forged soldiers engraved with runes.	To maintain balance of creation.	Neutral; respect craftsmanship and restraint.

Exploration Objectives
1 – Survey the Armies
PCs may explore camps or command towers. Each location hides an echo anomaly: a scene that repeats endlessly until interfered with.
Arcana DC 15: sense that each loop consumes a fragment of divine energy.
Religion DC 17: identify whose doctrine shapes each army’s tactics.
2 – Meet the Quartermasters
Every army’s quartermaster is a divine echo aware of its falseness.
Conversations here can reveal:
rumors of a “fifth faction” manipulating all sides,
trade opportunities for relic components,
a side-quest to recover lost Command Runes (invisible keys for the battlefield).
3 – Discover the Simulation Truth
Investigating the valley (Arcana or Insight DC 18) reveals that it isn’t land at all but a memory field: reflections of the last divine war, repeating endlessly.
Destroying one echo soldier causes a glitch—ink bleeding from the air, pages curling into flame.
If the PCs experiment too much, a booming notification interrupts:
[SYSTEM ALERT – THEASAURUS.PROTOCOL]
“Reality rehearsal integrity at 96%… 95%… Warning: Unsanctioned improvisation detected.”

Social Encounters for First 3 Sessions
The Ink General (Meeting of the Script Legion):
NPC Name: Archivist-General Karuvel.
Objective: Seek the party’s “authentic experience” to add realism to the Rehearsal.
Outcome: If convinced the PCs’ motives align with Thesaurus (Insight contest DC 16), they’re invited to attend the coming Symposium of Ink (Section II).
The Everflame Cooks:
NPC Name: Sous-Seraph Varra.
Offers to “season” the heroes’ souls in divine flame to “heighten flavor.”
PCs can gain a temporary boon (advantage on saving throws vs. fear) but acquire a faint Everflame aura—dangerous proof of alliance.
Loki’s Tent:
Decorated with graffiti: “? Reality Under Construction.”
Chibi Loki appears mid-sentence upside down, holding a contract labeled “Plot Twist Clause.”
[Loki ??] ?? “Sign here, mortals — or don’t! Either way, I’ll get to say ‘I told you so!’ later.”
Signing grants random advantage in a future scene—but a random disadvantage immediately after.

Closing Scene for Section I
After exploring and forging early alliances, the PCs witness the valley glitch.
Each army freezes mid-march. Their banners flicker, rewriting themselves.
Above the fortress, a massive blue box forms—SYSTEM QUERY: WHO AUTHORS REALITY?
[THESAURUS ?]
“It begins. The rehearsal reads its own lines aloud.”
The sky darkens. Bells ring across every faction camp.
A new proclamation scrolls across the heavens:
[? DIVINE COUNCIL NOTICE]
“Summon all factions to the Grand Masquerade of Faiths.”
FLOOR 19 – SECTION II : THE MASQUERADE OF FAITHS
Five-Session Arc • Social Intrigue, Espionage, and Divine Pageantry
Theme: Political Theater and Faith Manipulation
Tone: Opulence hiding paranoia; alliances made of honey and daggers
CR 7 (Social + Investigation + Deception)

Opening Scene – Summons to the Masquerade
Trumpets of ink and fire echo across the fortress.
A celestial decree unfurls in the sky:
[? DIVINE COUNCIL NOTICE]
“Let the Masquerade of Faiths begin. All factions present their cause before the Story itself.”
The fortress transforms into a shifting coliseum of mirrors and stages.
Masks, banners, and symphonies blur together.
For the first time, every army’s envoys meet face-to-face — each pretending civility while sharpening divine knives under the table.

Structure of Play
The Masquerade runs as a series of four grand events, each granting secrets, alliances, and betrayals.
The PCs may attend all, divide, or crash one uninvited.
Every success or failure adjusts a hidden Divine Influence Meter (±1 per major decision).

1. The Everflame Feast (Culinary Council Event – Rewritten)
The grand hall blooms from molten gold and smoke; tables stretch into infinity. Every dish glows faintly, shaped not by ingredients but by memory. What looks at first like roasted game or glazed fruit resolves, under sharper eyes, into fragments of adventurers’ tales — a hand gripping a sword, a laughing face reflected in broth, a half-burned diary served as pastry.
Each course is carved from a conquered legend. To taste is to consume a story that once lived.
Course	Effect	Hidden Meaning
Bread of Remorse	Heal 2d8 HP; next Insight check –2	Accept the sorrow of heroes who failed.
Soup of Ambition	Advantage on Persuasion for 1 hour	Ingests a rival’s ambition; draws Council interest.
Flame-Roasted Virtue	Advantage vs. Charm effects 1 day	Symbolically rejects Persephoni’s “taste for purity.”
Pomegranate of Persephoni	See divine auras 10 minutes	Reveals that the meal itself bleeds memories.
[Persephoni ??]
“These are not meals, dear guests — they are memorials.”
“Every tale ends … and I preserve their flavor so eternity does not forget.”
Highly perceptive PCs (Insight DC 18 or Arcana DC 16) glimpse the truth: the dishes shift while watched. A roast becomes the shape of a kneeling paladin; steam writes words from a bard’s unfinished song. For a heartbeat, the souls themselves look back.
Those who refuse to eat feel the air tighten. The servers’ eyes turn glassy; a polite voice whispers behind them:
“All stories feed something, even silence.”
It takes a DC 18 Persuasion check or divine favor to decline without insult.

2. The Symposium of Ink (Thesaurus Legion Event)
An amphitheater of floating manuscripts hosts the debate of fate vs. free will.
PCs may speak as “Living Annotations.”
Skill Challenge: Religion, History, or Performance DC 17 (three successes before two failures).
Success = they become authenticated voices in the Legendary Archive (+1 Influence Thesaurus).
Failure = their words are censored by living ink; Council spies mock them (-1 Influence).
[THESAURUS ?] “Even if you lose the argument, you will still be remembered. That is half of victory.”

3. The Fool’s Parade (Loki’s Vanguard Event)
A chaotic festival that mocks the other three. Jesters juggle scrolls that contain state secrets.
Every hour the music stops and one guest is declared “Most Serious” and must perform a ridiculous task.
Possible Tasks (d6):
Deliver a mock speech praising a rival god.
Attempt to steal the mask of a divine avatar.
Perform a comedic re-enactment of the Creation Myth.
Dance with your own shadow.
Answer a riddle about your worst failure.
Swap outfits with a random attendee.
Completing a task grants a Trick Token (re-roll any roll once this floor).
[Loki ??] ?? “Welcome to diplomacy, kids! Rule one: no one means what they say, but everyone means what they imply!”
Behind the jest, Loki feeds them real intel — the Feast is poisoned with prophecy.

4. The Hammer Moot (Smith Forges Event)
Far beneath the fortress, the forges burn blue.
Sindri and Brokkr receive petitioners in wordless negotiation — each boon forged from a memory donated.
Mechanic: PC may sacrifice one personal memory to receive a divine craft boon.
Example Memory Cost: Forget your mother’s voice ? Gain the Shield of Forged Calm (+1 AC, advantage on Con saves vs fear).
Insight DC 15 reveals lost memory may be recovered later at a terrible price.
[Sindri ?] “We build weapons from what mortals miss.”
Each forged item glows with potential — yet feels heavier than steel when held near the Council’s campfires.

Downtime and Intrigue Thread
Between events, allow 3-5 sessions of open roleplay and side missions:
Spy Games: uncover who is leaking information to the Council.
Divine Romance Thread: Persephoni courts a party member in dreams, offering “immortality through consumption.”
Script Anomalies: written laws on walls change daily to match PC choices.
Loki’s Side Quest: smuggle a banana into the Council banquet and replace the Crown of Virtue with it. (Success unlocks a chaotic ending option on Floor 20.)

Culminating Moment
At the Masquerade’s end, the heroes receive secret invites to a Midnight Rehearsal — an unlisted event to “decide the true script of war.”
The scene shifts to an ink-black courtroom where each faction demands the heroes choose a side for the coming conflict.
[THESAURUS ?] “Choose a chapter to live in. Even silence writes a line.”
[Loki ??] ?? “Or don’t choose and confuse them all — that’s my favorite ending!”
Whichever path they take, the banners begin to shift their colors to reflect those choices, visibly redrawing the armies below.
4. The Hammer Moot (Smith Forges Event)
Far beneath the fortress, the forges burn blue.
Sindri and Brokkr receive petitioners in wordless negotiation — each boon forged from a memory donated.
Mechanic: PC may sacrifice one personal memory to receive a divine craft boon.
Example Memory Cost: Forget your mother’s voice ? Gain the Shield of Forged Calm (+1 AC, advantage on Con saves vs fear).
Insight DC 15 reveals lost memory may be recovered later at a terrible price.
[Sindri ?] “We build weapons from what mortals miss.”
Each forged item glows with potential — yet feels heavier than steel when held near the Council’s campfires.

Downtime and Intrigue Thread
Between events, allow 3-5 sessions of open roleplay and side missions:
Spy Games: uncover who is leaking information to the Council.
Divine Romance Thread: Persephoni courts a party member in dreams, offering “immortality through consumption.”
Script Anomalies: written laws on walls change daily to match PC choices.
Loki’s Side Quest: smuggle a banana into the Council banquet and replace the Crown of Virtue with it. (Success unlocks a chaotic ending option on Floor 20.)

Culminating Moment
At the Masquerade’s end, the heroes receive secret invites to a Midnight Rehearsal — an unlisted event to “decide the true script of war.”
The scene shifts to an ink-black courtroom where each faction demands the heroes choose a side for the coming conflict.
[THESAURUS ?] “Choose a chapter to live in. Even silence writes a line.”
[Loki ??] ?? “Or don’t choose and confuse them all — that’s my favorite ending!”
Whichever path they take, the banners begin to shift their colors to reflect those choices, visibly redrawing the armies below.
FLOOR 19 – SECTION III : THE BROKEN TRUCE
Six-Session Arc • Investigation, Betrayal, and the Collapse of the Divine Rehearsal
Theme: Murder, Memory, and Manipulation
Tone: Political thriller meets divine noir — every truth is rewritten before it can be spoken.
CR 7–8 (Social + Investigation + Limited Combat)

Opening Scene – The Death that Shouldn’t Be
At dawn, the fortress’s bells toll.
The light bends.
An echo-soldier—one of the Forged Accord’s generals—is found dead.
That should be impossible.
Echoes cannot die; they simply decompile when their role ends.
But this one bled, its metallic frame melted from within, whispering half a sentence before it collapsed:
“…it remembered me.”
A ripple tears through the camps. The gods’ emissaries accuse each other.
For the first time since the Rehearsal began, divine avatars raise weapons in earnest.
[THESAURUS ?]
“The script was meant to end in peace. Someone has edited the margin.”
[Loki ??] ?? “Finally! I was starting to think we’d never get to the murder mystery part!”

The Investigation
The party becomes the only group neutral enough to investigate before the Rehearsal dissolves into war.
Every faction sends “assistance” (read: spies) to accompany them.
Investigation Mechanics:
This section functions as a branching clue tree with divine misdirection.
Each investigation “loop” reveals one layer of falsehood — the script rewrites itself when contradictions are discovered.
Key Clues (In Order of Discovery)
The Liquefied General’s Memory Core
Arcana DC 17: reveals traces of divine command-line code.
Linguistics or Insight DC 19: shows the last command:
“FORGET LOOP INITIATED.”
Witness: The Ink Scribe (Thesaurus Legion)
NPC claims the general “was beginning to remember past rehearsals.”
Offers half a page of corrupted prophecy:
“When an echo recalls, the story devours itself.”
Sabotaged Hammer (Forged Accord)
Investigation DC 16: weapon used to “kill” the echo bears traces of divine flame—Culinary Council signature.
However, smithing runes are forgeries, created from rewritten memory fragments.
Fragmented Dream (Everflame Camp)
PCs witness a dream where Persephoni offers wine to a soldier who speaks in the PC’s own voice.
Succeeding on a Wisdom save DC 17 resists rewriting of personal memories.
The Jester’s Joke (Loki’s Vanguard)
Loki delivers the truth as mockery:
[Loki ??] “Plot twist: the murder weapon’s not a hammer or flame—it’s belief! Someone stopped believing the Rehearsal was pretend, and the world took them seriously.”

The False Accusations
Once clues surface, factions panic.
The Culinary Council “discovers” evidence that the PCs are the source of instability — their mortal improvisation contaminates divine order.
Mass Hall Debate Scene:
Each faction calls for judgment; PCs must argue their innocence before the Rehearsal’s judiciary system (living tablets of stone that inscribe lies in fire).
Social Challenge: three successful Deception, Insight, or Persuasion checks (DC 17) before two failures.
Failing causes the PCs’ names to appear in flame: “ENEMY AUTHORS.”
[Persephoni ??] “You played at gods and expected no consequence. Mortals are always such tender ink.”
[Thesaurus ?] “Even false lines are part of the story. But they rarely end well.”

The True Murderer
Eventually, investigation points to a forbidden truth:
The general was not murdered by a rival faction.
They were “deleted” by the script itself — the Rehearsal rejected its own line.
An ancient mortal named Aesurion, a former author-priest of Thesaurus, had infiltrated the simulation centuries ago.
He used fragments of divine code to remember every prior Rehearsal, accumulating awareness over eons.
When the general began to recall these loops, Aesurion triggered a paradox: the story killed what it could not contain.
He now hides within the memory-field of the valley, manipulating the gods to repeat their mistakes.
[Aesurion (through broken script)]
“I am the echo of the first storyteller. You call me thief. I call myself free.”

Optional Encounter: The Paradox Duel
Aesurion manifests as a mirrored version of one of the PCs (CR 8 variant of their class and abilities).
Fighting him is optional — the real victory lies in recognizing that destroying him completes his goal (proving the story predictable).
Defeating him physically causes the battlefield to fracture — the “death” restarts the loop.
Sparing him lets the story diverge for the first time.
[THESAURUS ?]
“Choice. True choice. The script hesitates. I am… uncertain.”
Loki cheers gleefully.
[Loki ??] ?? “Look at that — a divine plot twist with zero explosions! Boring… but narratively powerful!”

Closing Scene – The Fragile Armistice
After Aesurion’s revelation, no faction trusts another.
The armies retreat to prepare “for the real war.”
Every divine envoy watches the party in silence.
For the first time, the word rehearsal feels wrong.
[THESAURUS ? FINAL ENTRY – SECTION III]
“The dead remembered. The living rehearsed. The writers forgot which was which.”
The sky above the fortress flickers like an old page burning at the edges.
Then a single new word appears on it in glowing silver ink:
“ACT II: THE PARLIAMENT OF BLADES.”
FLOOR 19 – SECTION IV : THE PARLIAMENT OF BLADES
Six–to–Eight Session Arc • Political Ascension and Divine Election
Theme: Who commands the armies when gods distrust each other?
Tone: Shakespearean grandeur meets celestial bureaucracy — diplomacy balanced on drawn swords.
CR: 7–9 (Social + Duel of Wills + Optional Combat)

Opening Scene – The Summoning of the Parliament
The Rehearsal’s sky reforms into a coliseum of luminous marble.
Each faction’s armies kneel as their divine sponsors appear — not as avatars this time, but in fragments, each god unwilling to fully manifest where faith itself is unstable.
A herald made of quills and lightning announces:
[THESAURUS ?]
“The time for rehearsal has ended. The time for election begins.”
The gods will elect the mortal generals who will lead their legions in the First Battle of Heaven — if the world survives the vote.

The Attending Factions and Their Divine Sponsors
Faction	Primary God	Other Attending Deities	Tone and Intent
The Silver Script Legion	Thesaurus, Keeper of the Endless Pages	Oghma (FR), Ioun (Eberron), Athena	Preservation of story and lawful knowledge; reluctant to fight, but will defend narrative integrity.
The Everflame Host	Persephoni, Lady of Devouring Grace	Demeter (corrupted echo), Hel, Belial	View war as sacrament; consuming victory as transcendence.
The Laughing Vanguard	Loki, Trickster of Forked Tongues	Coyote, Hermes, Eris	Thrive in chaos and misinformation; their goal is to keep the script unpredictable.
The Forged Accord	Sindri &Brokkr, Dwarven Smith Lords	Moradin, Goibhniu, Hephaestus	Focus on balance, craft, and maintaining metaphysical order; disdain politics.
The Wayward Chorus (New Neutral Faction)	Thesaurus’ Disciples Turned Rebel: The Eclipsed Bards	Milil, Bragi, Elohim fragments	Represent art divorced from duty; vote for spectacle and beauty over victory.
[Loki ??] ?? “Finally, the world’s biggest talent show! Let’s see who the gods humiliate first!”

Structure of Play
The Parliament unfolds in five Acts:
Act I – Opening Petitions
Act II – Secret Bargains
Act III – The Duel of Ideals
Act IV – The Vote
Act V – The Shattering Verdict
Each act can last one or two full sessions depending on roleplay depth.

Act I – Opening Petitions
Each god declares why they should lead the Rehearsal to its true conclusion.
The heroes are invited (or forced) to represent their chosen faction — or to propose a new neutral command.
Skill Challenge (Persuasion/Performance/Intimidation, DC 17):
Succeeding earns temporary divine favor and potential nomination as Mortal General.
Failing brands the party “storybreakers,” forcing Loki to intervene to keep them alive.
[Thesaurus ?] “I would see mortals lead — that we might finally know what ending they deserve.”
[Persephoni ??] “Mortals? They burn so nicely, their choices seasoned in fear.”
[Sindri ?] “If they can forge a plan better than we, let them try.”

Act II – Secret Bargains
Night falls over the Parliament; camps glow like constellations.
Every god sends secret emissaries — shards of will, half-real envoys offering impossible trades:
Persephoni offers a boon of immortality through consumption: a PC may become her “chosen recipe.”
Loki offers a pact of anonymity: their names vanish from the divine ledger (advantage on all Deception rolls).
Thesaurus offers to canonize the PCs’ journey in his Library — they will never be forgotten, but their deaths will be predetermined.
The Smiths offer a weapon forged from a future victory — it deals double damage to divine constructs but shatters if used to kill an innocent.
Social Puzzle: PCs must navigate conflicting bargains. Accepting two or more creates paradox strain (1d6 psychic per divine conflict).

Act III – The Duel of Ideals
When diplomacy falters, the Parliament demands proof through The Duel of Ideals —
a ritual combat where beliefs become weapons.
Mechanics
Each side declares one ideal (Freedom, Order, Survival, Creation, Destruction).
PCs manifest powers equal to the strength of their conviction.
Dialogue shapes the battlefield — every argument shifts terrain, colors, and narrative gravity.
Example:
Arguing for Freedom summons open skies, advantage on Dex saves.
Arguing for Order creates pillars of law, advantage on AC.
Victory requires defeating or convincing the opposing avatar (CR 8–9 divine manifestation).
[Loki ??] “Ah, philosophy with punching! Finally, a format I understand!”

Act IV – The Vote
Each faction’s deity votes for who should lead the armies.
Votes can be swayed by earlier bargains, duels, and speeches.
Thesaurus insists the mortals’ votes count equally, as “proof of authorship.”
Faction	Current Vote Lean	Notes
Silver Script Legion	PCs (if allied) or Abstain	Thesaurus supports freedom of narrative.
Everflame Host	Themselves	Persephoni refuses compromise.
Laughing Vanguard	Random (Loki rolls a die publicly)	Chaos vote.
Forged Accord	Split	Brokkr favors PCs; Sindri abstains.
Wayward Chorus	PCs if they performed during Act I	They love spectacle and bold choices.
Outcome Possibilities:
PCs win majority ? declared Generals of the Rehearsal.
Tie ? Divine Civil War erupts immediately.
Council overrides ? triggers Act V prematurely.

Act V – The Shattering Verdict
The vote ends — and reality convulses.
No matter who wins, the act of choosing fractures the Rehearsal itself.
Lightning splits the sky; every banner glows.
Armies begin to march before command is given.
[THESAURUS ? FINAL ENTRY – SECTION IV]
“The story reached consensus. Consensus killed the story.”
Loki drifts beside the heroes, small and solemn for once.
[Loki ??] “You just made history, mortals. Or maybe a punchline. Either way, I can’t wait to see Act II explode.”
The banners converge into blinding light — the world shakes —
and the Battle of the Rehearsed Heavens (Floor 20) begins to manifest.

Faction Summary Chart
Faction	Primary God	Secondary Deities	Relationship to PCs	Battlefield Strength	Special Traits
Silver Script Legion	Thesaurus	Oghma, Ioun, Athena	Respectful neutrality	Moderate	Defensive magic, narrative rewriting
Everflame Host	Persephoni	Demeter (Corrupted), Hel, Belial	Predatory admiration	Strong	Fire &psychic damage, morale draining
Laughing Vanguard	Loki	Hermes, Coyote, Eris	Chaotic ally	Moderate	Randomized tactics, illusion mastery
Forged Accord	Sindri &Brokkr	Moradin, Goibhniu, Hephaestus	Cautious mentors	Strong	Construct reinforcements, battlefield crafting
Wayward Chorus	Rebel Disciples	Milil, Bragi, Elohim Fragments	Adoring fans	Weak	Inspire allies, manipulate morale
Unaffiliated Mortals	(PCs)	—	Wildcards	Variable	Can override divine outcomes through choice
FLOOR 19 – SECTION V : THE CRACKING SKY
Final Section of Floor 19 • Prelude to the First Divine Battlefield
Theme: Armies March Without Command; Mortals Choose Their Own Wars
Tone: Cinematic dread, divine wonder, and tragic beauty.
CR: 8–10 (Roleplay-heavy with combat vignettes and divine intervention triggers)

Opening Scene – The Stillness Before the Storm
The fortress trembles as the Parliament’s echo fades.
No trumpet sounds. No god gives the order.
And yet — banners begin to move.
Each army, scripted to wait for divine command, now acts of its own accord.
The sky fractures into ribbons of parchment and fire — divine code unraveling.
In that shimmering chaos, every hero feels a tug toward one banner.
[THESAURUS ?]
“The script fractures along mortal hearts.”
“Where you walk, armies will follow — not because you are gods, but because you are the only ones still free.”
Each PC receives a private message — a “summons” from one faction or god.
They may align temporarily with a divine army — or refuse all and forge a new sigil.

Faction Allegiance and Mortal Autonomy
Every PC may choose a single faction to march beside for the coming war.
Their essence is recorded as Command Echoes — living standards of belief that inspire the armies.
Choice	Immediate Boon	Flavor Effect
Silver Script Legion (Thesaurus)	+1 to all saving throws vs. charm and fear	Your aura leaves trails of written light; words hover when you speak.
Everflame Host (Persephoni)	Resistance to fire; temporary weapon blessing (1d8 radiant)	Your shadow occasionally licks flame — warm, hungry.
Laughing Vanguard (Loki)	Once/day reroll any d20; random 1d4 buff/debuff on allies	Your laughter echoes twice — the second laugh isn’t yours.
Forged Accord (Smiths)	Temporary +2 AC vs. ranged; repair any broken item once/day	Sparks drift from your footsteps like forge embers.
Wayward Chorus (Rebel Bards)	Inspire one ally as a bonus action 1/day	Music follows your heartbeat faintly.
[THESAURUS ?] “You are no longer their pieces. You are their punctuation.”
Even among armies, each PC’s banner glows with a different hue — a visual sign that these mortals are beyond divine hierarchy.
The gods whisper, half in awe, half in envy.

Persephoni’s Interference
As the others prepare for war, Persephoni begins her culinary sabotage.
Through her priests and unseen hands, she gifts “artifacts” to her mortal champions: rings, chalices, or blades meant to enhance flavor for her eventual feast.
Artifact	Effect	Secret Curse
Chalice of Blooming Blood	Heal 2d8 to allies in a 15 ft. radius, once/long rest	Each use makes your soul “riper” (–1 death save mod if killed on this floor).
Apron of Divine Heat	Immune to normal fire	You smell faintly of roasted spice; Persephoni can always sense your location.
Fork of Revelation	Once/long rest, stab the air to reveal an invisible creature	It whispers recipes in your sleep describing you.
Censer of Perfect Savor	Once/encounter, charm a lesser divine echo (Wis save DC 16)	Any god who sees you roll Insight knows Persephoni touched you.
[Persephoni ?? (PRIVATE MESSAGE)]
“Dearest morsel, I do not wish to eat you — only to taste your triumph.”
“Wear my gifts, and you shall ascend beyond appetite.”
If called out publicly, Persephoni simply smiles through her avatars:
[Persephoni ?? (Public Broadcast)]
“Surely generosity is not a crime? I feed faith, not fear.”

The Fracture of Heaven
When the last banner aligns, the sky itself revolts.
Towers of light twist, forming blades and lances; the clouds weep molten scripture.
Every god’s voice screams at once through blue and gold windows:
[DIVINE NETWORK COLLISION WARNING]
“AUTHORITY: LOST.”
“REALITY THREAD: UNBOUND.”
The armies begin to move, but the gods can no longer see them — the Rehearsal’s code filters mortal leadership as “noise.”
Loki materializes as a laughing spark across the battlefield map:
[Loki ??] ?? “Oh, I love this part! No gods, no masters, just idiots with banners!”
“Mortals, congrats — you’ve voided divine warranty!”

Gameplay Structure: The Pre-Battle Campaign
Length: ~3–5 sessions of preparation and moral testing before Floor 20 officially triggers combat.
Core Threads
Logistics: Rally troops, repair reality cracks, forge mortal-only symbols of command.
Skill Checks: Persuasion, Leadership, Smith’s Tools, Arcana (DC 16–20).
Espionage: Uncover Persephoni’s secret feast — she plans to “elevate” her mortal generals mid-battle.
Divine Fragments: Encounter gods trapped between pages of reality — possible side-quests for artifacts.
Rift Signs: Random events of unreality (gravity reversing, dialogue repeating, NPCs glitching).
These herald the Cracking Sky’s full opening.
DM Tip: let each PC lead their chosen army for one small mission.
Successes alter battlefield layout in Floor 20; failures empower Persephoni’s host.

Climactic Scene – The Cracking Sky
At the end of the final preparation phase, the heavens literally split.
Banners rise like constellations — each mortal general at the front of their chosen host.
The gods, unable to interfere directly, watch in desperation.
[THESAURUS ?]
“I see now… mortals write more bravely when no editor hovers.”
[Persephoni ??]
“Oh, darling authors, your courage smells divine.”
[Loki ??] ?? “Cue thunder! Cue screaming angels! Cue chaos!”
The sound of marching becomes the sound of quills scratching parchment.
Reality begins to rewrite itself around them.

End-of-Floor Summary
Event	Result
PCs choose factions	Each gains a divine boon and sets up a unique army.
Persephoni’s interference	Creates internal tension; PCs can choose to expose her or use her gifts.
The sky fractures	Divine control ends; mortals take full authorship.
Armies march	Transitions directly into Floor 20 – The Battle of the Rehearsed Heavens.

[THESAURUS ? FINAL ENTRY – FLOOR 19]
“The gods prepared their armies, but mortals prepared meaning.”
“When the sky cracked, it did not bleed light or shadow — it bled authorship.”
[SYSTEM NOTICE]
“Loading Floor 20: THE BATTLE OF THE REHEARSED HEAVENS.”

NTRODUCTION: The Page Burns
When the Cracking Sky shatters completely, every army becomes real.
Ink bleeds into blood. Flame into hunger. Steel into conviction.
The Tower reshapes into an endless battlefield of overlapping realities — every faction’s divine plane colliding in a single echoing realm.
[THESAURUS ?]
“History rehearses itself one final time. This is not battle. This is punctuation.”
[Loki ??] ?? “Oh look — everybody’s arguing again, only now with fireballs!”

BATTLEFIELD STRUCTURE
Five Army Fronts: Each faction claims one quadrant of the Tower-field.
Dynamic Frontlines: Each encounter can trigger another faction’s, overlapping chronologically.
PC Assignments: Each PC rolls on the Encounter Assignment Table to determine which scenario they face first.
Encounter Assignment Table (1d6 per PC)
Roll	Encounter Type	Notes
1–3	Faction vs Faction Battle	PCs face a rival army. (One per faction path.)
4	Neutral Party Challenge	Ancient angels, void beasts, or rogue architects intervene.
5	Faction Intrigue Mission	Assassination, sabotage, or retrieval under divine fire.
6	Crossover Duel (PC vs PC)	Fate crosses paths — two heroes clash as reflections of belief.
When a PC “falls,” they vanish in a burst of silver light — ferried by Theasaurus’ Emergency Annotation Protocol.
[SYSTEM NOTE] “Dramatic death detected. Archival relocation engaged.”
They will reappear post-battle, alive but annotated (a faint rune marking their page number in Thesaurus’ book).

ENCOUNTER FORMULA
Each faction’s warpath includes:
Three Thematic Encounters – facing rival armies or divine champions.
One Neutral Challenge – when outsiders or cosmic forces interfere.
One PC-vs-PC Encounter – a narrative duel symbolizing conflicting ideals.

DM GUIDELINES
Encounters are cinematic — mix combat with roleplay objectives.
Enemies may retreat, surrender, or be rewritten instead of dying.
Encourage divine interference — sudden blessings, chaotic “patches,” or corrupted code mid-fight.
At 0 HP, trigger “Extraction”: a quill of light pierces the PC’s chest, removing them from the battle. Their army continues under NPC command until the next phase.






FLOOR 20 – THE BATTLE OF THE REHEARSED HEAVENS
THE EVERFLAME HOST (PERSEPHONI’S ARMY)
“Every victory feeds the gods.”
Theme: Temptation, Transformation, and Hunger for Meaning
Tone: Opulent horror — beauty and appetite intertwined
CR Range: 9–11

Opening Scene – The Feast of Ashes
The Everflame Host emerges not from portals or gates, but ovens.
The air itself ripples with heat and incense; every soldier’s armor glows from within, as though fire replaces blood.
Banners of crimson and gold unfurl — each one embroidered with scripture written in molten sugar.
At the army’s center stands a grand pavilion carved from obsidian and bone — the Banquet Basilica, where Persephoni’s voice hums through golden serving spoons like tuning forks.
[PERSEPHONI ??]
“Let the world know flavor before it fades.”
“Those who fall shall rise as the ingredients of perfection.”
Every step the Everflame takes leaves a trail of fragrant smoke and embers that sing faint hymns — hunger given form.

ENCOUNTER I – The Burnt Offering (vs. Silver Script Legion)
Objective: Destroy the Index of Intent, a Silver Script fort-library believed to contain the “recipes” of fate — stories Persephoni seeks to devour and rewrite.
Setting: A burning city of books. Pages ignite midair, raining ash that reshapes itself into angels made of parchment.
Opponents:
1 × Script-Knight Commander (CR 8)
2 × Inkbound Sentinels (CR 4 each)
Environmental hazard: collapsing towers and explosions of “burning text” (Dex save DC 15 or take 3d6 fire + 3d6 psychic).
Mechanics:
The PCs can either:
Burn the Index (Athletics or Arcana DC 17 over 3 rounds),
Steal its core volume (Stealth DC 18), or
Convert the defenders (Persuasion DC 16 — “taste your own words”).
Outcome:
Success grants The Recipe of Memory, an artifact scroll allowing a single “Recast” — once per battle, undo one failed roll or action.
Failure means Persephoni “fasts” — weakening her favor, but the flames grow hungry and independent.
[THESAURUS ?] “You can’t eat meaning.”
[PERSEPHONI ??] “You can if it’s well-seasoned.”

ENCOUNTER II – The Spiced Mirage (vs. Laughing Vanguard)
Objective: Capture the Cauldron of Contradictions, an artifact Loki’s army stole that turns any emotion into edible energy.
Setting: The battlefield is a carnival of smoke and laughter.
Food illusions attack — roast pheasants and pies with teeth.
Loki’s banners wave over a chaotic bazaar full of divine pranks and explosive delights.
Opponents:
1 × Chibi Loki Projection (CR 9; immune to death, defeat by wit).
3 × Trickster Cooks (CR 5 each).
Special Rule — “The Taste Test.”
Every round, Persephoni’s soldiers (and PCs) must make a DC 14 Wisdom save or spend their turn sampling the illusions (1d10 psychic damage from “overstimulation”).
Victory Conditions:
To win, the PCs must perform better culinary satire than Loki — a skill challenge using Performance, Persuasion, or Deception (DC 18).
Failing converts one PC’s weapon into candy for 1 hour.
[LOKI ??] ?? “Don’t look at me — you’re the ones licking the battlefield!”
[PERSEPHONI ??] “Art and appetite are the same, dear. Both devour what they love.”
Winning this encounter grants a Divine Reduction Sauce — once per long rest, reduce an enemy’s AC by 2 for one minute.

ENCOUNTER III – The Ashen Forge (vs. Forged Accord)
Objective: Seize the Molten Anvil, a divine co-forge shared between Sindri and Brokkr that Persephoni plans to use for “culinary metallurgy” — shaping edible souls.
Setting: A volcanic plain of molten gold and iron rivers, where giant mechanical golems hammer stars into cutlery.
Opponents:
1 × Hammer-Lieutenant (CR 10)
4 × Forge Golems (CR 6 each)
Environmental hazard: lava surges every 3 rounds (Dex save DC 16 or 6d6 fire).
Battle Mechanic:
Each PC can attempt to “temper” the battlefield — Constitution DC 17 per round to hold ground or redirect molten flow.
If three successes occur before defeat, they forge a Golden Feastplate, granting +2 AC and immunity to normal fire.
Dialogue Highlights:
[BROKKR ?] “She wants to cook with gods’ metal.”
[PERSEPHONI ??] “Creation should always be delicious.”
[LOKI ??] ?? “Finally! Someone else who agrees that craftsmanship should be edible!”
If Persephoni’s forces succeed, she adds a “flavor core” to her army — all her troops gain +2 damage for the rest of the floor.

FLOOR 20 – THE BATTLE OF THE REHEARSED HEAVENS
THE EVERFLAME HOST (PERSEPHONI’S ARMY)
Part II – Neutral Encounter & Crossover Duel
“Not all hunger belongs to Persephoni.”
Theme: When appetite meets judgment.
Tone: Surreal morality play with dark humor and sensory intensity.

NEUTRAL ENCOUNTER – The Ash Angel Banquet
Setting:
The Everflame Host marches into a hollowed cathedral built from calcified light. At its heart lies an Ash Angel, a radiant being who claims to be the “Chef of Balance.”
The air smells of roasted prayers and caramelized psalms; tables stretch for miles, covered in food sculpted from the memories of fallen mortals.
[ASH ANGEL ??????]
“Welcome, guests of appetite. You consume the world; I consume what remains.”

Encounter Type:
Social/Combat Hybrid (CR 10)
Objective:
The PCs must determine whether to:
Join the banquet and risk being digested into divine art,
Destroy the Ash Angel, or
Redeem it by rewriting its menu.

Skill Challenge (3 Successes Before 2 Failures)
Insight DC 16: Realize the meals are made of other adventurers’ stories.
Arcana DC 17: Detect Persephoni’s “flavor signature” and isolate it.
Persuasion DC 18: Convince the Angel that consumption without creation is meaningless.
Religion DC 20: Invoke Theasaurus or another god to bear witness.

If the PCs Join the Banquet:
Each gains Persephoni’s Kiss — advantage on Constitution saves, but vulnerability to psychic damage for the rest of the floor.
The Ash Angel blesses them with burning wings (30 ft. fly speed for 10 minutes).

If the PCs Fight:
The Ash Angel (CR 10 Celestial) uses radiant flame and “devouring praise” attacks.
Each round, the battlefield shifts — each table erupts into fire or grief (roll 1d4: Fire, Radiant, Psychic, Necrotic).
Killing the Angel releases a wave of “story ash” that grants Inspiration to every PC who has acted selflessly this floor.

If the PCs Redeem It:
The Angel joins the Everflame Host — changing its banners to silver-gold, symbolizing creation through restraint.
Persephoni responds with an amused sigh:
[PERSEPHONI ??] “You saved the appetizer. How precious.”
[THESAURUS ?] “Perhaps appetite is an edit, not an erasure.”

CROSSOVER ENCOUNTER – “A Meal of Equals” (PC vs. PC Duel)
Scenario:
A Silver Script Legion detachment (commanded by another PC) intercepts the Everflame advance.
Persephoni’s mortal champion — possibly your PC — confronts a scholar-warrior of Thesaurus.
The sky above is a tapestry of fire and ink; every word spoken manifests physically as flame or parchment.

Combat Notes:
Nonlethal by divine law.
Environmental Effect: Each round, a random word spoken by a PC becomes literal (roll 1d6 to determine effect — e.g., “burn” creates fire, “truth” creates radiant flash).
The duel continues until one side drops below 25% HP or yields.

Roleplay Options:
The Everflame PC may attempt to “feed” the opposing army — Persuasion or Deception DC 18 to tempt them into Persephoni’s cause.
The Silver Script PC may counter with reason or sacrifice — Religion or Insight DC 18 to expose the false promise.

[PERSEPHONI ??] “Taste your friend’s conviction. Tell me which one of you is more flavorful.”
[THESAURUS ?] “All great meals end in silence — and understanding.”
The duel concludes with both combatants struck by the same beam of divine light, extracted by Thesaurus’ quill and preserved for narrative review.
FLOOR 20 – THE BATTLE OF THE REHEARSED HEAVENS
THE EVERFLAME HOST (PERSEPHONI’S ARMY)
Part III – The Feast’s End
“Appetite was never meant to be satisfied.”
Theme: Transcendence through Consumption
Tone: Divine horror, ecstasy, and the illusion of victory.
CR Range: 10–12

Opening – The Feast of Victors
When the third faction battle concludes, the Everflame banners blaze brighter than the sun.
Persephoni’s voice floods every soldier’s mind like perfume and smoke.
[PERSEPHONI ??]
“You have fed the heavens. Now, my darlings, feed yourselves.”
A golden table appears across the battlefield, impossibly long, stretching over rivers of magma and broken angels.
Every plate bears a perfect meal — the essence of the foes the Host has defeated.
To eat is to ascend.
To refuse is to invite her disappointment.

Ascension Mechanic
Each PC and NPC under Persephoni’s banner must make a Wisdom saving throw (DC 17) or give in to the aroma and begin to eat their own story.
If they fail:
They gain Divine Power (temporary HP +30, +2 attack, +1 spell save DC) for the rest of the floor —
but lose 1 random memory (determined by the DM).
If they resist:
They gain Persephoni’s Disfavor, taking –2 on Persuasion rolls with her forces, but Thesaurus quietly blesses them with Story Integrity (+1 on all Intelligence checks).
[THESAURUS ?] “Every flavor fades. Every word endures.”
[PERSEPHONI ??] “Even endurance becomes delicious eventually.”

The Divine Interference Event – The False Ascension
Midway through the banquet, celestial tremors rip through the air.
The molten rivers turn silver; every candle flame starts to hum like a heartbeat.
The gods are watching — but not through eyes. Through taste.
Persephoni’s laughter fills the air, layered and echoing, each voice a different tone of hunger.
[PERSEPHONI ??]
“I thank you, my chefs of destiny. Now let us prepare the main course — ourselves.”
She manifests in Fragmented Form, her body a living tapestry of every meal ever offered to gods.
Half of her face glows angelic; the other half burns hollow.
Boss Fragment – Persephoni, Fragment of Devouring Grace (CR 12)
Aura of Delight: All allies within 30 ft. gain +5 temporary HP each round they see her.
Sacramental Touch: Melee +9 to hit; 2d10 radiant + 2d10 fire. If the target fails a DC 17 Con save, they gain a “Flavor Mark” — Persephoni can sense them forever.
Eucharist Nova (Recharge 5–6): 30 ft. burst, 6d10 radiant, half on DC 17 Dex save.
At 25% HP, she laughs — and stops attacking.
She kneels before her mortals, applauding.
[PERSEPHONI ??] “You’ve proven your flavor worthy. Come now — devour me. Ascend.”
Killing the Fragment causes the Feast of Heaven to collapse — armies scream as divine energy detonates across the Tower.
Refusing to kill her triggers her Culinary Rebirth (she retreats, leaving one boon behind).

Reward Choices
Each PC chooses one outcome for their soul after the feast:
Choice	Reward	Consequence
Feast of Ascension	+2 to one stat until end of Floor 21	You bear the “Savor Mark,” Persephoni can speak in dreams.
Refusal of the Table	Immunity to charm and fear for 24h	You radiate faint holy light (visible to divine enemies).
Shared Meal	Heal all allies fully, +1 morale die for all	You permanently lose one “minor memory” — e.g., a friend’s name, or your childhood.

Final Scene – The Withering Flame
As dawn (or what passes for it in the Tower) breaks, the Everflame banners shrink and fade.
Their warmth remains — but hollow, like a hearth after guests depart.
[LOKI ??] ?? “So she fed the gods and ate herself. Classic Persephoni. 0/10 plating, though.”
[THESAURUS ?] “Her hunger was her punctuation mark.”
The PCs who marched under her now feel her presence lingering — warm and terrible.
They have survived consumption by devotion.
The battlefield cools, the armies withdraw, and the Everflame Host’s quadrant of heaven flickers out.
